Guardian Relinquishing Minor's Shuf'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guardian's authority over minor's shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on a guardian relinquishing a minor's shuf'ah, state the proofs of each side, and identify the mufta bihi position with its conditions.

Core Idea
Guardians can relinquish a minor's shuf'ah when it resembles trade, not fixed rights like blood money.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classical intra-Hanafi dispute: may a father or executor (wali) give up the minor's right of preemption (shuf'ah) in a neighboring property sold to a third party? The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permit it; Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar prohibit it. The disagreement hinges on whether shuf'ah is analogous to trade (where guardians have discretion) or to fixed rights like blood money (where they do not). The author, al-Marghinani, weighs in, and the discussion also addresses sales at excessive prices.

Guided Path
1
State the Scenario and Core Disagreement
Identify the situation: a minor has a right of shuf'ah in a neighboring house sold to a buyer. The guardian (father or wasi) relinquishes that right. Does the relinquishment take effect? The Shaykhayn say yes; Muhammad and Zufar say no.
2
Examine the Proofs of the Opposing Side (Muhammad & Zufar)
They analogize shuf'ah to blood money (diyah) and retaliation (qisas) – fixed rights that guardians cannot waive. Moreover, shuf'ah is legislated to repel harm; nullifying it causes harm instead.
Qiyas with shabahah (resemblance) based on fixed right and harm-repelling purpose.
3
Examine the Proofs of the Shaykhayn
They argue shuf'ah is 'in the meaning of trade' – a transaction involving assessment of benefit and harm. Guardians can cancel a sale for a minor, so they can also leave shuf'ah. Silence (not demanding) is equivalent to relinquishment. This applies at market value.
Key concept: shuf'ah oscillates between benefit and harm; guardianship is based on consideration (nazar).
4
Identify the Author's Tarjih and Mufta Bihi Position
Al-Marghinani states 'wa huwa al-sahih' (and it is the correct position) in favour of the Shaykhayn. The operative ruling is that the guardian's relinquishment is valid when the property is sold at market value.
This overrides a narration that groups the Shaykhayn together inconsistently.
5
Analyse Qualifications for Over/Under Market Sales
If sold at an excessive overprice (ghabn fahish), two opinions: consensus allows relinquishment (pure benefit) or disallows it (no right to take). If sold at an excessive discount, Abu Hanifa says relinquishment invalid. The reasoning: relinquishment is a branch of taking; if guardian cannot take (like a stranger), he cannot relinquish.
These edge cases refine the main rule.

كتاب الشفعة
تشریح صغیر کی ماں کا انتقال ہو گیا تھا جس سے اس کو ایک مکان میراث میں مل تھا اب اس کے پڑوس میں ایک مکان فروخت ہوا جس میں بچہ کو شفعہ پہنچتا ہے مگر باپ نے یا باپ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں وصی نے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی تو یہ صحیح ہے یا نہیں۔ تو حضرات شیخین نے اس کو جائز کہا اور امام محمد و زفر نے اس کو جائز نہیں کہا بلکہ اس ک معتبر نہیں مانا۔ اور بچہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد اپنے شفعہ پر برقرار رہے گا۔ ان دونوں نے صراحت دست برداری دے دی ہو یا شفعہ کی طلب نہ کی ہو دونوں صورتوں میں یہی اختلاف ہے۔ اور اگر کسی نے کسی کو اپنے لئے طلب شفعہ کا وکیل بنایا ہو اس گھر کے اندر جو اس کے پڑوس میں فروخت ہوا اور اس وکیل نے شف۔ طلب کے بجائے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی ہو تو اس میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے۔
اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا: وهو الصحیح، یہ اسلئے فرمایا تا کہ اس روایت کی تردید ہو جائے جس میں حضرات طرفین کو ایک ساتھہ کہا گیا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول کو ان دونوں کے خلاف کہا گیا ہے۔
امام محمد و امام زفر کی دلیل .
لمحمد وزفرانه حق ثابت للصغير فلا يملكان ابطاله كدينه وقوده ولانه شرع لدفع الضرر فكان ابطاله إضرارا به
ترجمہ اما محمد اد از فرکی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حق شفعہ ایسا حق ہے جو بچہ کیلئے ثابت ہے تو یہ دونوں اس کے ابطال کے مالک نہ ہوں گے جیسا کہ اس کی دیت اور اس کا قصاص اور اس لئے کہ یہ حق مشروع ہوا ہے ضرر کو دور کرنے کیلئے تو اس کا ابطال بچہ کو نقصان پہنچانا ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح یہ اما محمد اور امام زفرتی دلیل ہے کہ جیسے باپ اور وصی بچہ کی دیت اور اس کے قصاص کو معاف نہیں کر سکتے کیونکہ وہ منجانب شرع حق ثابت ہے اسی طرح حق شفعہ کو بھی باطل نہیں کر سکتے اور مشروعیت شفعہ کا مقصد دفع ضرر ہے تو اگر اس کا حق باطل کر دیا گیا تو بجائے دفع شر کے بچہ کیلئے اضرار اور نقصان دینا ہے لہذا یہ دونوں ابطال کے مالک نہ ہوں گے۔
شیخین کی دلیل
ولهما انه في معنى التجارة فيملكان تركه الاترى ان من اوجب بيعا للصبي صح رده من الأب والوصى ولانه دائر بين النفع والضرر وقد يكون النظر فى تركه ليبقى الثمن على ملكه والولاية نظرية فيملكانه وسكوتهـما كـابـطـالهـمـا لكونه دليل ألاعراض هذا اذا بيعت بمثل قيمتها
ترجمہ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ( شفعہ میں لینا) تجارت کے درجہ میں ہے تو وہ دونوں اس لئے ترک کے مالک ہوں گے کیا آپ دیکھتے نہیں کہ جس نے بچہ کیلئے بیج کا ایجاب کیا تو باپ اور وصی کی طرف سے اس ایجاب کو رد کرنا صحیح ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ نفع اور نقصان کے درمیان دائر ہے اور کبھی شفقت اس کے چھوڑ دینے میں ہوتی ہے تا کہ ثمن بچہ کی ملکیت پر باقی رہے اور ولایت نظری ہے تو وہ دونوں اس کے مالک ہوں گے اور ان دونوں کا سکوت ان کے ابطال کے مثل ہے اس کی دلیل اعراض ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ گھر کو اس کی قیمت کے مثل کے بدلہ فروخت کیا جائے۔

كتاب الشفعة
تشریح پی شیخین کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شفعہ میں ایک قسم کی تجارت ہے جس میں نفع اور نقصان دونوں کا احتمال ہے اور بچہ پر ولایت اسلئے ملتی ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ شفقت کا برتاؤ کیا جائے۔
اور کبھی ترک شفعہ ہی میں شفقت ہوگی کیونکہ مصلحت کا یہاں یہی تقاضہ ہے اسلئے باپ اور وصی کو یہ بق حاصل ہوا کہ وہ شفعہ لینا چھوڑ دیں اور جس طرح صراحۃ ابطال کا حکم ہے سکوت کا بھی یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ سکوت اعراض کی دلیل ہے تو گو یا دونوں صورتوں میں اعراض پایا گیا۔ اول میں صراحت اور ثانی میں دلالتہ ۔ مگر ان حضرات کا یہ اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ مکان اتنی قیمت میں فروخت ہو جتنی اس کی مالیت ہے اور اگر کمی بیشی کے ساتھ فروخت ہوگا تو اس کا حکم آگے آرہا ہے۔ غبن فاحش کے ساتھ مکان بیچا گیا پھر وصی نے شفعہ سے دست برداری کی تو یہ دست برداری درست ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
فان بیعت باكثر من قيمتها بما لا يتغابن الناس فيه قيل جاز التسليم بالاجماع لانه تمحض نظرا وقيل لا يصح بالاتفاق لانه لا يملك الاخذ فلا يملك التسليم كالا جنبى وإن بیعت باقل من قيمتها محاباة كثيرة فعن ابي حنيفة انه لا يصح التسليم منهما ولا رواية عن ابى يوسف و الله اعلم
ترجمہ پس اگر گھر اپنی قیمت سے زیادہ کے ساتھ بیچا جائے اتنی زیادتی کے ساتھ کہ لوگ اس مقدار میں خسارہ برداشت نہ کرتے ہوں تو کہا گیا ہے کہ بالا جماع دست برداری جائز ہے اسلئے کہ یہ خالی شفقت ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ بالا تفاق دست برداری صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے کوئی ایک شفعہ میں لینے کا مالک نہیں ہے تو تسلیم کا بھی مالک نہ ہو گا۔ اجنبی کے مثل اور اگر بہت زیادہ فرو گذاشت کے ساتھ اپنی کم قیمت میں فروخت ہوا ہوںام ابو حنیفہ سے منقول ہے کہ ان دونوں کی تعلیم میچ نہیں ہے اورام ابو یوسف سے کوئی روایت نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم ۔
تشریح اگر مکان کی مالیت مثلا تین ہزار ہے اور فروخت ہوا ہے ہیں ہزار میں تو اتنا خسارہ لوگوں میں برداشت کرنے کی عادت نہیں ہے اور ان دونوں میں سے کسی نے دست برداری دے دی تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟
تو مصنف فرماتے ہیں اس میں دو قول ہیں:
پہلا قول تو یہ ہے کہ بالاجماع تسلیم درست ہے کیونکہ یہ سراسر شفقت ہے۔
اور دوسرا قول جس کو اصبح قرار دیا گیا ہے یہ ہے کہ تسلیم می نہیں بلکہ بچہ کا حق بدستور باقی رہے گا۔ واہ حضور یہ عجیب منطق ہے؟ جواب غور کیجئے کہ تسلیم شفعہ میں لینے کی فرع ہے یعنی جو شخص جہاں شفعہ میں لینے کا حق رکھتا ہو وہی دست برداری دے سکتا ہے اور یہاں غبن فاحش کی وجہ سے جب باپ اور وصی کو شفعہ میں لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔
تو اب یہ دونوں اجنبی کے مثل ہو گئے تو جس طرح اجنبی کی تسلیم میچ نہیں ہوگی ایسے ہی ان دونوں کی تعلیم میچ نہیں ہوگی۔
For the minor whose mother passed away, he inherited a house. Then a neighboring house was sold, giving the child a right of preemption (shuf'ah). But the father, or if no father, the guardian, relinquished the shuf'ah. Is this valid or not? The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) deemed it permissible, while Imam Muhammad and Zufar deemed it impermissible and not valid. The child, upon reaching maturity, retains his right of preemption. The same disagreement applies whether they explicitly relinquished or simply did not demand shuf'ah. And if someone appointed an agent to demand shuf'ah for him in a neighboring sold house, and the agent relinquished instead of demanding, the same disagreement applies. The author (al-Marghinani) said: 'And it is the correct position.' He said this to refute a narration that aligns both parties together and attributes a statement of Abu Yusuf against them. The proof of Imam Muhammad and Zufar: 'For Muhammad and Zufar, it is a right established for the minor, so they do not have the authority to nullify it, like his blood money (diyah) and his retaliation (qisas). And because it was legislated to repel harm, so nullifying it is causing harm to him.' Translation: The proof of Imam Muhammad and Zufar is that the right of shuf'ah is a right established for the child, so these two (father and guardian) do not have authority to nullify it, just as they cannot waive the child's blood money or retaliation. And because this right was legislated to repel harm, nullifying it would cause harm to the child. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Muhammad and Zufar: just as a father and guardian cannot waive the child's blood money and retaliation because it is a right established by Sharia, similarly they cannot nullify the right of shuf'ah. And the purpose of legislation of shuf'ah is to repel harm, so if his right is nullified, it brings harm and loss to the child instead of repelling evil. Therefore, these two are not owners of nullification. The proof of the two Shaykhs: 'And for them (the two Shaykhs), it is in the meaning of trade, so they have authority to leave it. Do you not see that whoever makes a sale contract for a minor, its cancellation by the father or guardian is valid? And because it (shuf'ah) oscillates between benefit and harm, and sometimes the best interest lies in leaving it so that the price remains in his ownership, and guardianship is based on consideration, so they have authority over it. And their silence is like their nullification because it is evidence of turning away. This is when the house is sold at its value.' Translation: The proof of the two Shaykhs is that taking shuf'ah is in the category of trade, so they have authority to leave it. Do you not see that when someone makes a sale for a minor, its cancellation by the father or guardian is valid? And because shuf'ah oscillates between benefit and harm, and sometimes the consideration (shafaqah) is in leaving it so that the price remains in the child's ownership, and guardianship is based on consideration, so they have authority over it. And their silence is like their nullification because it is evidence of turning away. This disagreement applies when the house is sold at its value. Then if it is sold with an excessive gain (more than market value with a difference that people do not overlook), it was said that relinquishment is permissible by consensus because it is pure consideration; and it was said that it is not valid by agreement because they do not have the right to take, so they do not have the right to relinquish, like a stranger. And if it is sold for less than its value with a large favor, from Abu Hanifa it is reported that relinquishment is not valid from them, and there is no report from Abu Yusuf. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a father or guardian can relinquish the right of preemption (shuf'ah) on behalf of a minor. The text first presents the scenario: a minor inherits a house, and a neighboring house is sold. The minor has a right of shuf'ah, but the father or guardian relinquishes that right. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) consider this permissible, while Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar consider it impermissible. The passage then provides the proofs for each side. Imam Muhammad and Zufar argue that the right of shuf'ah is a fixed right for the minor, analogous to blood money (diyah) and retaliation (qisas), which guardians cannot waive. Additionally, since shuf'ah was legislated to repel harm, nullifying it would itself cause harm. The two Shaykhs counter that shuf'ah is like trade; guardians can cancel a sale for a minor, so they can also leave shuf'ah. It oscillates between benefit and harm, and sometimes it is in the minor's best interest to leave it to preserve the price. The author then notes that the corrected position is that of the Shaykhayn. The text also discusses divergent cases: if the property is sold at a very high price (ghabn fahish), two opinions exist—one allowing relinquishment by consensus as pure benefit, another disallowing it because the guardian lacks the right to take (and thus to relinquish). If sold at a very low price, Abu Hanifa reportedly disallows relinquishment. The commentary explains the reasoning: relinquishment is a branch of taking; if the guardian cannot take due to excessive loss, he becomes like a stranger and cannot validly relinquish.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of preemption: a neighbor or partner's right to buy a sold property by paying its price to the buyer.
ولي (wali): Guardian, specifically father or executor (wasi) for a minor.
دست برداري (dast-bardari): Relinquishment or withdrawal from the right of shuf'ah.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Excessive loss or overpayment that people do not normally tolerate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (al-Marghinani), whose position is 'the correct one' regarding the guardian's relinquishment of a minor's shuf'ah at market value?
A) The position of Imam Muhammad and Zufar
B) The position of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
C) A compromise between the two
D) None; the author leaves it unresolved

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi position is that a guardian can validly relinquish a minor's shuf'ah when the property is sold at market value, based on the trade analogy.

Father's Waiver of Minor's Pre-emption at a Low Price
Intra-Hanafi dispute on father's waiver of minor's shuf'a at low price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on a father's waiver of minor's shuf'a at a low price, state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and explain the legal reasoning (imtina' vs tabarru').

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: waiver of minor's shuf'a is abstention, not donation; Muhammad: it is a donation of minor's property.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether a father can waive his minor child's right of pre-emption when the property is sold significantly below market value. The dispute turns on whether the waiver is deemed a mere abstention from acquiring a new right (imtina') or an active donation (tabarru') of the minor's property. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi juristic approach to guardianship and the protection of minors' interests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The property is worth 10,000 but sold for 3,000. The father waives the minor's right of pre-emption (shuf'a).
The disparity in price is critical; if the price were fair, the waiver might be uncontested.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds the waiver is valid because it is abstention (imtina') from entering the property into the minor's ownership, not removal (izalah) of an already owned right.
He categorizes this as a non-donative act, thus within the father's authority as guardian.
3
State Muhammad's Position
Muhammad holds the waiver is invalid because it is akin to donating the minor's property (tabarru'), which requires capacity the minor lacks.
He sees the waiver as actively giving up a valuable right, equivalent to a gift.
4
Recognize the Missing Narration from Abu Yusuf
No narration from Abu Yusuf on this specific issue; the passage refers to al-Tabyin for further discussion.
The absence of a third opinion leaves the dispute binary.
5
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the waiver is valid and the sale proceeds; under Muhammad, the minor retains shuf'a and may invalidate the sale after reaching majority.
This practical consequence affects the finality of the transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر مکان کی مالیت مثلاً دس ہزار ہے اور رعایت اور فروگذاشت کی وجہ سے بائع نے اس کو تین ہزار میں فروخت کر دیا ہوتو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اب باپ [اور وحی کی تعلیم؟] درست نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ اس میں بچہ کا کھلا ہوا نقصان ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کیا فرماتے ہیں؟ جواب ان سے اس بارے میں کوئی روایت نہیں ہے واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ تنبیہ: مجمع الانہر ج ۲ ص ۴۶۹ پر ہے و في الكافى اذا سلم الاب شفعة الصغير والشراء باقل من قيمته بكثير فعن الامام ان التسليم يجوز لانه امتناع عن ادخاله في ملكه لا ازالة عن ملكه ولم يكن تبرعاً و عن محمد انه لا يجوز لانه بمنزلة التبرع بماله ولا رواية عن ابى يوسف و فى التبيين كلام فيطالع
And if the price of the house is, for example, ten thousand, and due to concession and negligence the seller sold it for three thousand, then what is the ruling? So Imam Abu Hanifa says that the father's [waiver?] is not valid because there is clear loss to the child. Imam Abu Yusuf: what does he say? Answer: There is no narration from him regarding this. And Allah knows best what is correct. Note: In Majma' al-Anhur, vol. 2, p. 469: And in al-Kafi: If the father waives the pre-emption of a minor and the purchase is for far less than its value, then from Imam (Abu Hanifa): the waiver is permissible because it is abstaining from entering it into his ownership, not removing from his ownership, and it is not a donation. And from Muhammad: it is not permissible because it is akin to donating his property. And there is no narration from Abu Yusuf. And in al-Tabyin there is discussion, so refer.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of a father's waiver of his minor child's right of pre-emption (shuf'a) when the property is purchased at a price far below its market value. The Urdu portion first poses a scenario where the seller sells a house worth ten thousand for three thousand, and Abu Hanifa holds that the father's waiver is invalid due to clear loss to the child. However, the tanbih (note) from al-Kafi clarifies that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the waiver is permissible because it is considered an abstention (imtina') from acquiring the property for the child, not a removal (izalah) of an already owned right, and therefore not a donation (tabarru'). Imam Muhammad, on the other hand, considers it akin to a donation of the child's property and thus invalid. No narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is recorded. The passage directs the reader to al-Tabyin for further discussion. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Abu Hanifa's view, the father can validly waive the minor's shuf'a even at a low price, preserving the sale, whereas under Muhammad's view, the minor retains the right of pre-emption, potentially nullifying the sale.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf‘ah): The right of pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property at the sale price before it is transferred to a third party.
تسليم (taslīm): Waiver or relinquishment of the right of pre-emption, i.e., the father's act of not claiming shuf‘a on behalf of the minor.
تبرع (tabarru‘): A gratuitous act or donation; in this context, donating the minor's property without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the father's waiver of the minor's shuf‘a valid even when the purchase price is far below the property's value?
A) Because the father has authority to donate the minor's property.
B) Because it is considered abstention from acquisition, not a donation.
C) Because the minor will benefit from the low price.
D) Because the sale was with the minor's consent.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa validates the father's waiver of minor's shuf'a because it is abstention from acquisition, not a donation; Muhammad invalidates it as a donation of the minor's property.

Division of Joint Properties: Afraz and Mubadala
Ruling with proof and expansion on dual nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division of joint property, explain its dual nature (afraz and mubadala), and apply the distinction between mithli and non-mithli goods to determine legal consequences.

Core Idea
Division of joint property combines separation and exchange; the ruling varies by property type.

Division of joint property (qismah) is a legislated practice in Islam, rooted in the Prophet's actions in spoils and inheritances. This passage from al-Hidayah unpacks the unique dual nature of division: it is both a separation (afraz) of shares and an implicit exchange (mubadala) of rights between partners. Understanding which aspect predominates based on the type of property is crucial for determining when a partner may act unilaterally and how subsequent sales are treated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
Locate the ruling that division is legislated (mashru') and the dalil naqli: the Prophet's practice (fi'l) in spoils and inheritances, and the continuous consensus (sukut al-ankara).
The proof is based on prophetic action and tacit approval.
2
Understand the dual nature: afraz and mubadala
Analyze why division necessarily involves exchange: each partner receives a portion that partly belonged to the other, so there is an implicit swap of residual shares.
The example of Zayd and Bakr buying a house illustrates this.
3
Distinguish mithli from non-mithli goods
Determine which aspect predominates based on the property's characteristics. Mithli (fungible) goods like measured/weighed items lack disparity, so afraz predominates. Non-mithli goods (animals, goods) have disparity, so mubadala predominates.
This classification is key for subsequent rules.
4
Apply the distinction to practical scenarios
Using the predominance rule, derive the two practical consequences: (1) taking a share in the partner's absence and (2) selling the share by murabahah after division.
The text explicitly links afraz predominance to permissibility of both actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال القسمة في الاعيان المشتركة مشروعة لان النبي عليه السلام باشرها في المغانم والمواريث وجرى التوارث بها من غير نكير ثم هي لا تعرى عن معنى المبادلة لان ما يجتمع لأحدهما بعضه كان له وبعضه كان لصاحبه فهو ياخذه عوضا عما بقى من حقه فى نصيب صاحبه فكان مبادلة وافرازا والا فراز هو الظاهر فى المكيلات والموزونات لعدم التفاوت
ترجمہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا مشترک چیزوں میں بٹوارہ مشروع ہے اسلئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے مغانم اور مواریث میں بنوارہ فرمایا اور بغیر نکیر کے اس کے ساتھ تو ارث جاری ہے پھر بنوارہ مبادلہ کے معنی سے خالی نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ دوشریکوں میں سے ایک کیلئے جو حصہ جمع ہوا ہے اس میں سے بعض تو اسی کا تھا اور بعض اس کے ساتھی کا تھا تو وہ اس کو لے لیتا ہے اس حصہ کے عوض میں جو اس کے ساتھی کے حصہ میں اس کا حق باقی رہتا ہے تو یہ مبادلہ اور افراز ہوا اور مکیلات و موزونات کے اندر تفاوت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے افراز ہی ظاہر ہے۔ تشریح افراز کہتے ہیں اپنے عین حق کو لینا اور مبادلہ کہتے ہیں اپنے حق کے ساتھ دوسرے کے حق کو ملانا۔ تو قسمت میں جہاں افراز ہے وہاں مبادلہ بھی ہے مثلاً زید اور بکر دونوں نے ایک گھر خریدا تو دونوں کی ملکیت میں شیوع ہے۔ پھر جب بٹوارہ ہوا تو ایک جانب زید کو ملی اور دوسری جانب بکر کو ۔ حالانکہ دونوں کی ملکیت میں شیوع تھا تو جو حصہ زید کو ملا ہے اس میں بکر کا حصہ تھا اور بکر والے حصہ میں زید کا حصہ تھا اب گویا زید نے اپنے حصہ کے ساتھ بکر کا حصہ ملالیا اور اس کے حصہ کے بدلہ اس کو وہ حصہ دیا جو زید کا اس جانب میں ہے جو بکر کے حصہ میں ہے۔ لہذا یہ اس میں مبادلہ کا پہلو ہے۔
تو قسمت میں افراز و مبادلہ دونوں کا پہلو ہے مگر مکیلات و موزونات میں افراز غالب ہے اور غیر مثلی کے اندر مبادلہ کے معنی غالب ہیں ۔
افراز کی صورت میں اپنے شریک کی عدم موجودگی میں بھی حصہ لے سکتا ہے
حتى كان لاحدهما ان ياخذ نصيبه حال غيبة صاحبه ولو اشترياه فاقتسماه يبيع احدهما نصيبه مرابحة بنصف الثمن ومعنى المبادلة هو الظاهر فى الحيوانات والعروض للتفاوت حتى لا يكون لاحدهما اخذ نصيبه عند غيبة الآخر ولو اشترياه فاقتسما لا يبيع احدهما نصيبه مرابحة بعد القسمة ترجمہ یہاں تک کہ حق ہو گا ان میں سے ایک کیلئے کہ اپنے ساتھی کی غیبت کے وقت اپنا حصہ لے لے اور اگر دونوں نے اس کو خریدا
He said: Division in joint properties is legislated because the Prophet (peace be upon him) practiced it in spoils and inheritances, and inheritance has been transmitted by it without disapproval. Then it is not free from the meaning of exchange, because what is collected for one of them — part of it was his and part was his companion's. So he takes it in exchange for what remains of his right in his companion's portion. Thus it is exchange and separation. And separation is apparent in measured and weighed items due to the lack of disparity. Translation: The author of al-Hidayah said: Division in joint properties is legislated because the Prophet (peace be upon him) practiced division in spoils and inheritances, and inheritance has continued by it without disapproval. Then division is not free from the meaning of exchange. Because for one of the two partners, the share that is collected — part of it was his and part was his companion's. So he takes it in exchange for the part of his right that remains in his companion's share. So it is exchange and separation. And in measured and weighed items, due to the absence of disparity, separation is apparent. Explanation: Afraz means taking one's exact right, and mubadala means mixing one's right with another's right. So in division, wherever there is afraz, there is also mubadala. For example, Zayd and Bakr bought a house, so both have ownership in common. Then when division occurred, one side went to Zayd and the other to Bakr. Even though both had common ownership, the portion that Zayd received contained Bakr's share, and the portion of Bakr contained Zayd's share. Now Zayd has taken Bakr's share along with his own, and in exchange for that share, he gave the share that Zayd had in that side which is in Bakr's portion. Therefore, there is an aspect of exchange in this. So in division, there are both aspects of afraz and mubadala, but in measured and weighed items, afraz is predominant, and in non-mithli items, the meaning of exchange is predominant. In the case of afraz, one can take his share even in the absence of his partner. Until it is permissible for one of them to take his share in the absence of his companion, and if they both bought it and divided it, one of them may sell his share by murabahah at half the price. And the meaning of exchange is apparent in animals and goods due to disparity, so that it is not permissible for one of them to take his share in the absence of the other, and if they both bought it and divided it, one of them may not sell his share by murabahah after division. Translation: Until one of them has the right to take his share during the absence of his companion, and if they both bought it...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents the opening ruling of the Hidayah for Kitab al-Qismah: division of joint properties is legislated (mashru'). The proof is the prophetic practice (fi'l) in spoils and inheritances, and the continuous transmission (tawatur) without disapproval. The commentary then explains the dual nature of division: it involves both afraz (separation) and mubadala (exchange). Afraz is taking one's exact physical share; mubadala is the implicit exchange of rights because each partner's allotted portion contains elements of the other's original share. The text illustrates this with the example of two partners (Zayd and Bakr) buying a house jointly: after division, each receives a portion that originally contained the other's share, so there is an implicit exchange. The predominance of afraz or mubadala depends on the type of property. For mithli (fungible) goods like measured and weighed items, afraz is predominant because there is no significant disparity between units; thus one partner may take his share even in the absence of the other. For non-mithli items like animals and goods (where disparity exists), mubadala is predominant, and a partner cannot unilaterally take his share in the other's absence. The ruling also affects subsequent sales: for mithli goods, after division, one may sell his share by murabahah based on half the purchase price (since afraz predominates), while for non-mithli goods, such a sale is not valid because the division involved exchange, not mere separation.

Key Terms
افراز (afraz): Taking one's exact right or share from the jointly owned property without any exchange.
مبادلة (mubadala): Exchange of shares between partners, occurring implicitly in division when each partner receives a portion that contains part of the other's original share.
مثلی (mithli): Goods that are fungible and have no significant disparity between units, such as measured or weighed items.
قسمة (qismah): Division of joint property, encompassing both separation (afraz) and exchange (mubadala).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of property can a partner take his share even in the absence of the other partner?
A) Animals and goods
B) Measured and weighed (mithli) items
C) Real estate with unique features
D) All joint properties

Key Takeaway
Division of joint property is a unique contract with dual aspects; the predominant aspect—afraz or mubadala—depends on the property's fungibility, affecting legal consequences.

The Legitimacy and Dual Nature of Division of Common Property (Qismah)
Establishes the ruling on division and its dual nature as separation and exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proofs for the legitimacy of qismah and distinguish between ifraz and mubadala to determine when a partner may take his share alone or sell by muarabaha.

Core Idea
Division of common property combines separation of exact shares and exchange; this duality dictates the legal consequences for absence and sale.

This lesson unpacks the foundational ruling on dividing common property (qismah) in Hanafi fiqh. We begin with the textual proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, then explore the school's unique analysis of division's dual nature: the separation of exact shares (ifraz) and the exchange of interdependent rights (mubadala). Mastering this distinction is essential for applying the correct rules when a co-owner is absent or wishes to sell his portion.

Guided Path
1
List the proofs for legitimacy
Identify the Quranic verse (water division), Prophetic practice (dividing spoils and inheritances), hadith ('give each rightful one his right'), and consensus cited in the passage.
These proofs establish that qismah is mashru' (legislated).
2
Understand the dual nature of division
Recognize that every division necessarily involves both ifraz (taking one's exact share) and mubadala (exchange of shares), as exemplified by dividing a house where each partner receives a part that originally belonged to both.
The passage states: 'it is not free from the meaning of exchange.'
3
Distinguish fungibles from non-fungibles
In fungible goods (mukeelat/mawzunat like grain, metals), ifraz is dominant because units are identical. In non-fungibles (animals, merchandise), mubadala dominates due to inherent disparity.
This dominance determines the applicable rules.
4
Apply the distinction to practical rules
For fungibles, a partner may take his share in the other's absence and may sell his share by muarabaha for half the total price. For non-fungibles, neither is allowed without the partner's presence or consent.
The ruling hinges on whether division is primarily ifraz or mubadala.
5
Consider judicial compulsion
When animals are of one species, a judge can compel division upon a partner's request, akin to compelling debt payment. For different species, no compulsion because balancing is impossible.
Consent is still required for heterogeneous property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
جواب جی ہاں ! ارشاد باری تعالی و نبتهم ان الماء قسمة بينهم، لكل شرب محتضر، لها شرب و لكم شرب يوم معلوم واذا حضر القسمة اولو القربی ۔ نیز حدیث سے اس کی مشروعیت ہے کیونکہ سرکار دو عالم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مواریث وغنائم کو تقسیم فرمایا ہے اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنی ازواج مطہرات کے درمیان باری مقر فر مارکھی تھی۔ نیز آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے. وأعط كل ذي حق حقہ۔ نیز اس کی مشروعیت پر اجماع امت ہے۔ آگے حضرت مصنف فرماتے ہیں۔
اعیان مشترکہ میں تقسیم مشروع ہے
قال القسمة في الاعيان المشتركة مشروعة لان النبي عليه السلام باشرها في المغانم والمواريث وجرى التوارث بها من غير نكير ثم هى لا تعرى عن معنى المبادلة لان ما يجتمع لاحدهما بعضه كان له وبعضه كان لصاحبه فهو ياخذه عوضا عما بقى من حقه فى نصيب صاحبه فكان مبادلة وافرازا والا فراز هو الظاهر فى المكيلات والموزونات لعدم التفاوت
ترجمہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا مشترک چیزوں میں بٹوارہ مشروع ہے اسلئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے مغانم اور مواریث میں بنوارہ فرمایا اور بغیر نکیر کے اس کے ساتھ تو ارث جاری ہے پھر بنوارہ مبادلہ کے معنی سے خالی نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ دوشریکوں میں سے ایک کیلئے جو حصہ جمع ہوا ہے اس میں سے بعض تو اسی کا تھا اور بعض اس کے ساتھی کا تھا تو وہ اس کو لے لیتا ہے اس حصہ کے عوض میں جو اس کے ساتھی کے حصہ میں اس کا حق باقی رہتا ہے تو یہ مبادلہ اور افراز ہوا اور مکیلات و موزونات کے اندر تفاوت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے افراز ہی ظاہر ہے۔ تشریح افراز کہتے ہیں اپنے عین حق کو لینا اور مبادلہ کہتے ہیں اپنے حق کے ساتھ دوسرے کے حق کو ملانا۔ تو قسمت میں جہاں افراز ہے وہاں مبادلہ بھی ہے مثلاً زید اور بکر دونوں نے ایک گھر خریدا تو دونوں کی ملکیت میں شیوع ہے۔ پھر جب بٹوارہ ہوا تو ایک جانب زید کو ملی اور دوسری جانب بکر کو ۔ حالانکہ دونوں کی ملکیت میں شیوع تھا تو جو حصہ زید کو ملا ہے اس میں بکر کا حصہ تھا اور بکر والے حصہ میں زید کا حصہ تھا اب گویا زید نے اپنے حصہ کے ساتھ بکر کا حصہ ملالیا اور اس کے حصہ کے بدلہ اس کو وہ حصہ دیا جو زید کا اس جانب میں ہے جو بکر کے حصہ میں ہے۔ لہذا یہ اس میں مبادلہ کا پہلو ہے۔
تو قسمت میں افراز و مبادلہ دونوں کا پہلو ہے مگر مکیلات و موزونات میں افراز غالب ہے اور غیر مثلی کے اندر مبادلہ کے معنی غالب ہیں ۔
افراز کی صورت میں اپنے شریک کی عدم موجودگی میں بھی حصہ لے سکتا ہے
حتى كان لاحدهما ان ياخذ نصيبه حال غيبة صاحبه ولو اشترياه فاقتسماه يبيع احدهما نصيبه مرابحة بنصف الثمن ومعنى المبادلة هو الظاهر فى الحيوانات والعروض للتفاوت حتى لا يكون لاحدهما اخذ نصيبه عند غيبة الآخر ولو اشترياه فاقتسما لا يبيع احدهما نصيبه مرابحة بعد القسمة ترجمہ یہاں تک کہ حق ہو گا ان میں سے ایک کیلئے کہ اپنے ساتھی کی غیبت کے وقت اپنا حصہ لے لے اور اگر دونوں نے اس کو خریدا ہو پھر بنوارہ کیا ہو تو ان میں سے ایک اپنے حصہ کو بیع مرابحہ کے ساتھ فروخت کر سکتا ہے نصف ثمن کے بدلہ اور مبادلہ کے معنی غالب ہیں حیوانات اور عروض میں تفاوت کی وجہ سے یہاں تک کہ ان میں سے کسی ایک کو حق نہ ہوگا کہ دوسرے کی غیبت میں اپنا حصہ لے اور اگر دونوں نے اس کو خریدا ہو پھر بنوارہ کیا تو ان میں سے کوئی ایک اپنے حصہ کو بٹوارہ کے بعد بیع مرابحہ کے طریقہ پر نہیں بچ سکتا۔ تشریح چونکہ افراز میں اپنا عین حق لیا جاتا ہے اور مبادلہ میں اپنے حق کا عوض لیا جاتا ہے تو افراز کی صورت میں شریک کی عدم موجودگی میں بھی اپنا حصہ لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ اپنا حصہ لینا ہے۔ اور اگر افراز والی صورت میں جو کہ مثلیات میں ہوتی ہے دو آدمیوں نے مل کر ایک مثلی چیز خریدی پھر آپس میں بٹوارہ کر لیا۔ اب ایک شریک اپنے حصہ کو مرابحہ یا تولیہ کے طریقہ پر فروخت کرنا چاہتا ہے تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی نصف شمن کے بدلہ، کیونکہ ہر ایک نے اپنا عین حق لیا ہے جو انہوں نے خریدا تھا تو بیع مذکور جائز ہوگی۔ اور اگر مبادلہ کی صورت ہو تو چونکہ وہاں ہر ایک کا حصہ بدل گیا ہے تو جوخریدا تھاوہ فروخت نہیں کیا گیا اسلئے وہاں بیج مرابحہ اور تولیہ کے طریقہ پر نصف شمن کے بدلہ بھی جائز نہ ہوگی اور اسی طرح اپنے شریک کی عدم موجودگی میں اپنا حصہ نہیں لے سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ مبادلہ ہے اور مبادلہ کیلئے دوسرے شریک کا ہونا ضروی ہے۔
تنبیہ ولو اشتریان کا مرجع اول میں مثلی ہے اور ثانی میں غیر مشکلی۔ کما ہو ظاہر
حیوانات میں قسمت افراز کے معنی میں ہیں بلکہ مبادلہ کے معنیٰ ہے
الا انها اذا كانت من جنس واحد جبر القاضى على القسمة عند طلب احد الشركاء لان فيه معنى الافراز لتقارب المقاصد والمبادلة مما يجرى فيه الجبر كما في قضاء الدين وهذا لان احدهم يطلب القسمة يسأل القاضى ان يخصه بالانتفاع بنصيبه ويمنع الغير عن الانتفاع بملكه فيجب على القاضي اجابته وان كانت اجناسا مختلفة لايجبر القاضي على قسمتها لتعذر المعادلة باعتبار فحش التفاوت فى المقاصد ولو تراضوا عليها جاز الحق لهم.
لان
ترجمہ مگر تحقیق جبکہ وہ حیوانات ایک جنس کے ہوں تو قاضی بنوارہ پر مجبور کرے گاشر کا میں سے کسی ایک کی طلب کے وقت اسلئے کہ اس میں افراز کے معنی ہیں مقاصد کے قریب قریب ہونے کی وجہ سے اور مبادلہ ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جس میں جبر جاری ہوتا ہے جیسے قرض کو ادا کرنے میں اور یہ اسلئے کہ ان میں سے کوئی بٹوارہ کو طلب کر کے قاضی سے یہ درخواست کرتا ہے کہ اس کے حصہ سے استفارع کے ساتھ اس کو خاص کر دیا جائے اور غیر کو اس کی ملکیت سے متنفع ہونے سے روک دے تو قاضی پر اس کی درخواست قبول کرنا ضروری ہے اور اگر حیوانات اجناس مختلفہ ہوں تو قاضی اس کے بٹوارہ پر جبر نہیں کرے گا مقاصد کے اندر خش تفاوت کی وجہ سے برابری کے مستعد رہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر وہ سب بنوارہ پر راضی ہو جائیں تو جائز ہے اسلئے کہ حق انہیں کا ہے۔
تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ حیوانات کی صورت میں قسمت افراز کے معنی میں نہیں بلکہ مبادلہ کے معنی میں ہے۔
Book of Partition. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 13. Answer: Yes! The command of Allah the Exalted: 'And inform them that the water is divided between them, each drinking share attended.' [al-Qamar:28] And 'When the division is attended by relatives...' [al-Nisa:8]. Also from Hadith its legitimacy is established because the Prophet ﷺ divided inheritances and spoils, and he ﷺ set turns among his pure wives. And his ﷺ saying: 'And give each rightful one his right.' Also there is consensus of the Ummah on its legitimacy. Next the author says: Division of common property is legislated. He said: Division in common properties is legislated because the Prophet ﷺ practiced it in spoils and inheritances, and inheritance has continued with it without disapproval. Then it is not free from the meaning of exchange, because what is gathered for one of them—part of it was his and part was his partner's—so he takes it in exchange for what remains of his right in his partner's share. So it is exchange and separation. Separation is apparent in measured and weighed goods due to lack of disparity. Translation: The author of Hidayah said: Division of common things is legislated because the Prophet ﷺ performed division in spoils and inheritances, and inheritance continues with it without disapproval. Then division is not free from the meaning of exchange because for one of the two partners, the share that is collected—some of it was his and some was his partner's—so he takes it in exchange for the portion of his right that remains in his partner's share. So this is exchange and separation. And in measured and weighed goods, due to no disparity, separation is apparent. Elaboration: Separation (ifraz) means to take one's exact right, and exchange (mubadala) means to mix one's right with another's right. So in division, where there is separation, there is also exchange. For example, Zayd and Bakr bought a house, so both have ownership with shuyu' (common ownership). Then when division occurred, one side went to Zayd and the other to Bakr. Even though both had common ownership, the share that Zayd received contained Bakr's share, and in Bakr's share there was Zayd's share. Now it is as if Zayd mixed Bakr's share with his share and in exchange for his share gave him that share which Zayd had in that side which is in Bakr's share. Hence there is an aspect of exchange in this. So in division, both aspects of separation and exchange exist, but in measured and weighed goods, separation is dominant, and in non-fungible goods, the meaning of exchange is dominant. In the case of separation, he can take his share even in the absence of his partner. So that one of them may take his share during the absence of his partner. And if they both bought it and then divided it, one of them may sell his share as muarabaha for half the price. And the meaning of exchange is apparent in animals and goods due to disparity, so that one of them does not have the right to take his share during the absence of the other. And if they both bought it and then divided it, one of them cannot sell his share as muarabaha after the division. Translation: So much so that one of them has the right to take his share during the absence of his partner. And if they both bought it and then divided it, one of them can sell his share as muarabaha for half the price. And the meaning of exchange is dominant in animals and goods due to disparity, so that none of them has the right to take his share during the other's absence. And if they both bought it and then divided it, none of them can sell his share as muarabaha after the division. Elaboration: Since in separation one takes his exact right, and in exchange he takes a substitute for his right, so in the case of separation, he can take his share even in the absence of the partner because it is taking his own share. And if in the case of separation, which occurs among fungibles, two people together bought a fungible item and then divided it among themselves, now one partner wants to sell his share by muarabaha or tawliyah, then it is permissible—that is, for half the price—because each took his exact right which they had purchased, so the mentioned sale is valid. And if it is a case of exchange, since each person's share has changed, what was purchased is not sold, therefore the sale by muarabaha or tawliyah for half the price is not valid. Similarly, he cannot take his share during the absence of his partner because this is exchange, and exchange requires the presence of the other partner. Note: The reference of 'and if they both bought' in the first case is to fungibles, and in the second to non-fungibles, as is apparent. Division in animals is not in the sense of separation but rather in the sense of exchange. Except that if they are of one species, the judge compels division upon the request of one of the partners because there is the meaning of separation due to similarity of purposes. And exchange is among things in which compulsion is applied, as in the payment of debt. This is because one of them requests division, asking the judge to allocate him the benefit of his share and prevent others from benefiting from his property, so it is obligatory upon the judge to grant it. And if they are of different species, the judge does not compel division because balancing is impossible due to gross disparity in purposes. But if they all agree upon it, it is permissible because the right is theirs. Translation: But indeed, when the animals are of one species, the judge will compel division at the request of one of the partners, because there is the meaning of separation due to similarity of purposes. And exchange is among those things in which compulsion is applied, as in payment of debt. This is because one of them requests division, asking the judge to allocate him the benefit of his share and prevent others from benefiting from his property, so it is obligatory upon the judge to grant his request. And if the animals are of different species, the judge does not compel division due to the difficulty of achieving equality because of gross disparity in purposes, and if they all agree upon division, it is permissible because the right is theirs. Elaboration: The author says that in the case of animals, division is not in the sense of separation but rather in the sense of exchange.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, opening the Book of Partition (Kitab al-Qisma). The author first establishes the legitimacy of dividing common property (a'yan mushtaraka) by citing the Quranic verse about the division of water between Thamud, the Prophet's practice of dividing inheritances and spoils, his hadith 'give each rightful one his right', and the consensus of the Ummah. This is a ruling with proof from multiple sources. The author then explains the dual nature of division: it combines separation (ifraz)—taking one's exact share—and exchange (mubadala)—the mutual transfer of rights. For fungible goods (mukeelat and mawzunat) where units are identical, ifraz is dominant; for non-fungibles like animals and goods (urud), mubadala dominates due to inherent disparity. The practical implications are detailed: in ifraz-based division, a partner may take his share in the other's absence and may sell his share via muarabaha (profit-sharing sale) for half the total price, because he is selling his exact original share. In mubadala-based division, the partner cannot take his share without the other's consent (since it's an exchange) and cannot sell by muarabaha because the share received is not the same as the one originally purchased. A note clarifies that the first scenario applies to fungibles, the second to non-fungibles. Finally, the commentary addresses the judge's power of compulsion: for animals of one species, where purposes are similar, the judge can compel division upon a partner's request, analogous to compelling debt payment. For animals of different species, where purposes vary widely, the judge cannot compel division, but voluntary division is allowed. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that division is a form of exchange subject to mutual consent except when the property is homogeneous and separation is possible.

Key Terms
قسمت (qismah): Division of property among co-owners to separate shares and eliminate common ownership (shuyu').
شیوع (shuyu'): Common ownership where each partner owns a share in every part of the property.
افراز (ifraz): Taking one's exact, specific share from the common property without replacement; dominant in fungibles.
مبادلہ (mubadala): Exchange where each partner gives up his share in part of the property and receives a substitute share from another part; dominant in non-fungibles.
مکیلات و موزونات (mukeelat wa mawzunat): Fungible goods sold by measure (e.g., grain) or weight (e.g., metals), where units are identical.
حیوانات و عروض (hayawanat wa urud): Non-fungible goods like animals and merchandise, where individual units differ in value and purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can a co-owner of fungible goods (mukeelat/mawzunat) take his share in the absence of his partner?
A) Always, as long as the property is common.
B) Only if the judge orders the division.
C) Only if the division is by ifraz (separation).
D) Never, because division must be by both partners.

Key Takeaway
Division of common property is legislated by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma; its dual nature (ifraz/mubadala) determines when a partner may act alone or sell by muarabaha.

Dividing the Qasim's Fee: Headcount vs. Shares (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fee apportionment in qismah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of the qasim's fee and apply the rulings of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The qasim's fee: Abu Hanifa divides by headcount; Sahibayn by share proportion. Both are valid Hanafi views.

When co-owners with unequal shares hire a divider (qasim), how should his fee be split? This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds the fee is divided equally by headcount, while the two disciples (Sahibayn) argue it should be proportional to each owner's share. The disagreement hinges on whether the fee is compensation for the indivisible act of distinguishing shares or a burden of ownership. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi principles of apportionment.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa (by headcount) and the Sahibayn (by share proportion). Note that both are within the Hanafi school.
The matn states Abu Hanifa's view first, indicating it is the primary narration.
2
Identify the core disagreement and reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues the fee is for the act of distinguishing (tamyiz), which is equal for all co-owners. The Sahibayn argue it is a burden of ownership (mu'nat al-milk), which should be apportioned according to shares.
The nature of the qasim's service is the key point of contention.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's analogies (qiyas)
The Sahibayn analogize the qasim's fee to the fee of a weigher, cost of digging a shared well, and maintenance of a jointly owned slave. In each case, the expense is divided by ownership proportion.
These analogies are based on the principle that expenses of joint property follow ownership.
4
Evaluate Abu Hanifa's counterargument and the mufta bihi
Abu Hanifa distinguishes tamyiz from these analogies because the act of distinguishing is a single, indivisible service that does not vary with share size. The later relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, due to general principles of apportionment.
Although the text cuts off Abu Hanifa's proof, later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidayah, Fath al-Qadir) discuss the tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واجرة القسمة على عدد الرؤس عند ابي حنيفة قال ابو يوسف ومحمد على قدر الانصباء لانه مؤنة الملك فيتقدر بقدره كاجرة الكيال والوزان وحضر البير المشتركة ونفقة المملوك المشترك ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور بٹوارہ کی اجرت عدد روس کے مطابق ہوگی ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور فرمایا ابو یوسف اور محمد نے حصوں کی مقدار کے مطابق ہوگی اسلئے کہ اجرت ملکیت کی مشقت ہے تو اجرت بقدر ملک مقدر ہوگی جیسے کتیال اور وزن کی اجرت اور مشترک کنواں کھودنے کی اجرت اور مشترک مملوک کا نفقہ۔ تشریح قاسم کو اجرت کس حساب سے دی جائے گی جبکہ ایک کا حصہ کم ہے اور دوسرے کا زیادہ تو فرمایا امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جتنے آدمی ہیں ان پر برابر برابر اجرت ہوگی حصوں کی کمی بیشی ملحوظ نہ ہوگی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ جتنا حصہ ہوگا اس کے مطابق اجرت ہوگی کیونکہ اجرت یہاں ملکیت کا بارخرچہ ہے تو جتنی جس کی ملکیت ہو گی اتنی ہی اس پر اجرت ہوگی ۔ مثلاً ایک گھر میں زید کا حصہ آدھا ہے اور بکر کا تہائی ہے اور خالد کا چھٹا ہے۔ انہوں نے اس کو تقسیم کرایا جس کی اجرت بارہ روپے مقرر ہوئی ۔ تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہر ایک پر تین تین روپے ہوئے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک زید پر چھ روپے اور بکر پر چار اور خالد پر دو ہوئے کیونکہ ملکیت اس تناسب سے ہے۔ پھر صاحبین نے چندا مثلہ پیش فرمائیں جن میں اجرت بقدر ملک ہے۔ ا۔ جب شرکا ء نے کسی کو اجیر بنایا تاکہ ان کے سامان کو کیل کر دے یا تول دے تو بالا تفاق اجرت بقدر ملک ہو گی۔ - مشترک کنواں اجرت پر کھدوایا تو بقدر ملک کھودنے والے کی اجرت واجب ہوگی۔ ۳۔ دو آدمیوں کے درمیان کوئی مملوک مشترک ہے جس کو نفقہ کی ضرورت ہے تو نفقہ بقدر ملک واجب ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ولابى حنيفة ان الاجر مقابل بالتمييز وانه لا يتفاوت وربما يصعب الحساب بالنظر الى القليل وقد ينعكس الامر فتعذر اعتباره فيتعلق الحكم باصل التمييز بخلاف حفر البير لان الاجر مقابل ينقل التراب وهو يتفاوت
He said: And the fee of division is according to the number of heads according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: according to the amount of shares, because it is a burden of ownership, so it is measured by its measure, like the fee of the weigher and the weigher, and the digging of a shared well, and the maintenance of a jointly owned slave. Translation: Quduri said: The fee of division will be according to the number of heads according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it will be according to the amount of shares, because the fee is the expense of ownership, so it is measured by the amount of ownership, like the fee of the weigher and the weigh-man, and the digging of a shared well, and the maintenance of a jointly owned slave. Commentary: On what basis will the qasim's fee be given? When one's share is less and another's more, Imam Abu Hanifa said: as many men as there are, the fee will be equally divided among them, regardless of the difference in shares. The Sahibayn said: the fee will be according to the share, because here the fee is the burden of ownership, so the fee will be in proportion to ownership. For example, in a house, Zayd has half, Bakr has a third, Khalid has a sixth. They had it divided, and the fee was fixed at twelve rupees. According to Imam (Abu Hanifa), each pays three rupees. According to Sahibayn, Zayd pays six, Bakr four, and Khalid two, because ownership is in that proportion. Then Sahibayn presented examples where the fee is according to ownership: (1) When partners hire someone to measure or weigh their goods, the fee is unanimously according to ownership. (2) A shared well dug on hire, the fee for digging is due according to ownership. (3) A jointly owned slave who needs maintenance, the maintenance is due according to ownership. The proof of Abu Hanifa: According to Abu Hanifa, the fee is in exchange for distinguishing (the shares), and that does not vary. Sometimes calculation becomes difficult considering a small share, and the matter may invert, so considering it becomes impossible, so the ruling attaches to the origin of distinguishing. Unlike digging a well, because the fee is in exchange for moving earth, and that varies.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding how the fee of the qasim (divider) should be allocated among co-owners when their shares are unequal. The issue arises after the division is completed and the qasim's fee is due: should each co-owner pay an equal share (by headcount) or a share proportional to their ownership stake? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the fee is divided equally among all co-owners, regardless of the size of their share. His reasoning, partially given at the end, is that the fee is compensation for the act of distinguishing (tamyiz) the shares themselves, which is a single service that does not vary in effort based on the size of each share. Moreover, calculating fee by share could be complicated when some shares are very small, and the benefit of division is common to all. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that the fee should be divided in proportion to each co-owner's share because the fee is a burden (mu'nah) of ownership — like other expenses associated with jointly owned property, such as the fee for weighing, digging a well, or maintaining a slave — which are apportioned according to ownership. They provide analogies: if partners hire someone to weigh or measure goods, the fee is split by ownership; if they hire someone to dig a shared well, the cost is by ownership; and for maintenance of a jointly owned slave, each pays according to ownership. The text then begins to present Abu Hanifa's counter-argument but is cut off. The practical difference is illustrated with an example: three partners owning a house in halves, thirds, and sixths, with a fee of 12 rupees. Abu Hanifa says each pays 4 rupees; Sahibayn say Zayd pays 6, Bakr 4, Khalid 2. The dispute is significant in practice and is resolved by the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, which is often the view of the Sahibayn due to its consistency with general principles of apportionment, though the text does not explicitly state tarjih here.

Key Terms
عدد الرؤس (adad al-ru'us): Number of individuals (headcount); each co-owner counted as one regardless of share.
قدر الانصباء (qadr al-ansiba'): Proportion of shares; the fee is divided according to the value or fraction of each co-owner's property.
تمييز (tamyiz): The act of distinguishing or separating shares from the joint property; the service performed by the qasim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, how should the qasim's fee be divided among co-owners?
A) Proportionally to their shares
B) Equally by headcount
C) According to the qasim's discretion
D) Only the largest shareholder pays

Key Takeaway
The qasim's fee is divided according to shares (Sahibayn's view) in the operative Hanafi position, not equally by headcount.

Second Narration: Division Fee on the Demander Only
Second transmission from Abu Hanifa on division fee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the second narration regarding the division fee and identify the condition under which it applies.

Core Idea
The division fee falls only on the demander when some partners refuse, not when all demand.

This lesson examines a second transmission (riwayah) from Imam Abu Hanifa on who bears the fee for dividing jointly owned property. While the stronger position is that the fee is shared equally or proportionally, this narration places the entire cost on the partner who demands division, provided others refuse. Understanding the conditionality of this ruling clarifies when it may be applied in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the second narration
The text states that the fee (ujrah) is incumbent only on the demander (talib), not on the refuser (mumtani'). Recognise this as a second transmission from Abu Hanifa that diverges from the standard position.
The term 'talib' refers to the partner who actively requests division; 'mumtani'' refers to the one who declines.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
The fee is on the demander because he benefits from the division, while the refuser is harmed. In Hanafi usul, benefit (naf') can be a basis for liability.
This is a ta'lil argument: the ruling is tied to the presence of benefit and harm.
3
Recognise the condition (shart)
The commentator explicitly states that this ruling applies only when some partners demand and others refuse. If all demand, the fee is shared equally (per Imam Abu Hanifa's first narration) or proportionally (per Sahibayn).
The condition is critical: the second narration is not generalised; it applies specifically to cases of partial demand.
4
Compare with other positions
Contrast this second narration with the first narration (equal fee) and with Sahibayn (proportional fee in real estate). Note the authoritative weight: the first narration is mufta bihi, the second is a conditional option.
This step reinforces the hierarchy of riwayat within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ اجرت طالب پر ہے نہ کہ انکار کرنے والے پر طالب کے نفع کی وجہ سے اور ممتنع کے نقصان کی وجہ سے۔

Second narration from Imam Sahib: His narration: the fee is on the demander, not on the refuser, due to his benefit and the refuser's harm. Translation: And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that the fee is on the demander, not on the one who refuses, because of the benefit to the demander and the harm to the refuser. Commentary: This is a second narration from Imam Sahib: that the fee is wajib only on the one who demanded, and not on the one who refused division, because the demander's wish is fulfilled so he receives benefit, and the refuser suffers harm, so according to benefit, the demander should bear the compensation. But this is only when some demand and some refuse; otherwise if all demand, the fee is equal among all or proportional to share. The conclusion: in the case of measuring/weighing, according to the majority, fee is by share; in the case of real estate, according to Imam Sahib it is equal, and according to Sahibayn by share.

Commentary
This passage presents a second transmission (riwayah) from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the division fee. In this narration, the fee is placed solely on the partner who demands division (talib), not on those who refuse (mumtani'). The reasoning is that the demander benefits from the division, while the refuser suffers harm (being forced to split). The commentary clarifies that this ruling applies only when some demand and some refuse; if all partners demand division, then the fee is either equal (according to Imam Abu Hanifa's first narration) or proportional (according to Sahibayn). The passage concludes by summarizing the rules: for measuring and weighing, the fee is proportional by share (according to the majority); for real estate, it is equal per Abu Hanifa's first view, and proportional per Sahibayn.

Key Terms
طالب (talib): The partner who demands division of the jointly owned property.
ممتنع (mumtani'): The partner who refuses to participate in the division.

Key Takeaway
The second narration only applies when some partners demand and others refuse; otherwise, the fee is shared.

Division Without Proof of Ownership Transfer
Ruling that judge divides without proof of ownership transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division when claimants do not specify ownership transfer and explain why qada' 'ala al-ghayr does not apply.

Core Idea
Division is allowed without proof of ownership transfer when no third party's rights are at stake.

When co-owners ask a judge to divide property without explaining how they acquired it, the Hanafi school permits division—provided they do not acknowledge ownership for anyone else. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that ruling and highlights an internal difference within the school.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the legal question
The passage asks: if partners come to the judge requesting division of joint property but do not state the means of ownership transfer, what should the judge do?
The focus is on the absence of proof (bayyinah) regarding the source of ownership.
2
2. Extract the ruling from the matn
Al-Quduri's matn states: 'If they claim ownership without stating how it transferred to them, he (the judge) divides it between them.'
This is the base ruling.
3
3. Understand the rationale (dalil)
The proof is that such a division does not involve qada' 'ala al-ghayr (judgment against a non-litigant) because the claimants did not acknowledge any prior ownership for another person.
Thus no third-party rights are harmed.
4
4. Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Hidayah commentary reports that this ruling is from the riwayah of Kitab al-Qismah in al-Mabsut. However, al-Jami' al-Saghir has a contrary narration requiring proof (iqamat al-bayyinah) for division.
Both narrations are from Imam Muhammad's Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
5. Apply the principle to analogous cases
The passage earlier distinguished cases of movable vs. immovable property and purchase to avoid qada' 'ala al-mayyit. Here, since no third party is mentioned, qada' 'ala al-ghayr is absent.
Qiyas with other scenarios is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Because movable property needs protection, unlike land which is inherently preserved. Another reason: the person who takes possession of a movable item becomes a guarantor for it, so there is compassion for the deceased; but the person in possession of land is not a guarantor. Therefore Abu Hanifa said that land cannot be usurped. Anyway, from this discussion it is known that it is not correct to analogize the case of land to movable property. As for the case of purchase, when the seller sold the item, he is no longer its owner, even if the buyers have not yet divided it among themselves; here qada' 'ala al-ghayr does not apply, while in the first case qada' 'ala al-mayyit applies, so analogizing the latter two cases to the first is a qiyas ma'a al-fariq. If partners come to the judge asking for division without stating how they acquired ownership, what is the ruling? He (al-Quduri) said: If they claim ownership without stating how it transferred to them, he divides it between them because in this division there is no judgment against a non-litigant, as they did not acknowledge ownership for anyone else. He said: This is the narration of Kitab al-Qismah. Translation: Al-Quduri said: If they claim ownership without stating how it transferred to them, the judge divides it between them because in this division there is no qada' 'ala al-ghayr, as they did not acknowledge ownership for anyone else. Sahib al-Hidayah said: This is the narration of Kitab al-Qismah from al-Mabsut. Explanation: If partners come to the judge claiming division without stating how they got the land, since they did not acknowledge any prior ownership for anyone else that would necessitate qada' 'ala al-ghayr, the judge divides the land between them. Now Sahib al-Hidayah said: This is the narration of Kitab al-Qismah from al-Mabsut. And the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir is contrary to it, which prohibits division without establishing proof.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding division (qismah) when claimants do not specify how they acquired ownership. The commentary begins by distinguishing between movable property (manqul) and land ('aqar) in the context of guarantee and qada' 'ala al-ghayr. The author establishes that qiyas between land and movable property is not valid here. The core ruling from Quduri's matn states: if people claim ownership of a property and request division without explaining how they came to own it, the judge should divide it between them. The proof is that such a division does not involve judgment against a non-litigant (qada' 'ala al-ghayr) because the claimants have not acknowledged ownership for anyone else. The commentary then notes that this ruling is from the riwayah of Kitab al-Qismah in al-Mabsut (a Zahir al-Riwayah text), while the riwayah of al-Jami' al-Saghir prohibits division without establishing proof (iqamat al-bayyinah). This shows a difference in transmission within Imam Muhammad's works. The translator emphasizes that since the claimants made no acknowledgment of a third party's ownership, there is no risk of harming an absent party.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division or partition of joint property among co-owners, dividing either ownership or physical possession.
قضاء على الغير (qada' 'ala al-ghayr): A judicial judgment that affects a third party who is not present in the litigation, which is prohibited in Hanafi law.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal proof or evidence, typically testimony of witnesses, required to establish ownership in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because land does not require protection like movable property.
B) Because the claimants did not acknowledge ownership for anyone else, so there is no qada' 'ala al-ghayr.
C) Because the judge presumes they are truthful.
D) Because the Quran permits it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, division of joint property without proof of ownership transfer is permitted only when no third-party rights are acknowledged, to avoid qada' 'ala al-ghayr.

8 min
Division of Land Requires Proof of Ownership
Intra-Hanafi dispute over a ruling on land partition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires proof of ownership (milk) rather than mere possession (yad) for judicial partition of land, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute about the source of this ruling.

Core Idea
Possession alone does not justify partition; ownership must be proven because land needs no preservative division.

Two men claim the same land and each proves they are holding it. Should the judge split it between them? The Hanafi tradition says no—not until they prove it actually belongs to them. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that rule, the two types of division in Hanafi law, and an early disagreement within the school about whose view it represents.

Guided Path
1
Recognise the scenario and initial ruling
Identify the facts: two claimants, each proves possession (yad) of the same land. The judge is asked to partition. The ruling from al-Jami‘ al-Saghir says he must not divide until ownership (milk) is proven.
The ruling is based on the possibility that the land belongs to someone else.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Two opinions are reported: (1) this ruling is only the view of Abu Hanifa; (2) it is the view of all three founders (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani). Al-Hidayah declares the second as more correct (asahh).
The dispute is about attribution, not about the ruling itself.
3
Understand the two types of division
Division (qismah) is of two kinds: qismat al-hifz (preservative division, needed for movable property) and qismat al-milk (ownership division, needed for any property when ownership is established). Land does not require preservative division because it is inherently preserved.
This distinction is the key legal reasoning.
4
Apply the distinction to the case
Since land does not need preservative division, any division must be qismat al-milk. That type requires proof of ownership. Because the claimants have only proven possession, not ownership, the division is prevented.
Hence the judge cannot order partition until ownership is established.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
If the ruling were only Abu Hanifa’s, the other two imams might have allowed division without proof. But the asahh view (all three require proof) is the operative rule (mufta bihi) because it is based on sound reasoning and avoids potential injustice to unknown third parties.
Practical consequence: the judge must insist on proof of ownership in all cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو آدمیوں نے قاضی کے پاس آکر زمین کا دعویٰ کیا اور بینہ قائم کر دیئے کہ وہ زمین ہمارے قبضہ میں ہے قاضی تقسیم کرے یا نہ کرے وفى الجامع الصغير ارض دعاها رجلان واقاما البينة انها فى ايديهما وارادا القسمة لم يقسمها يقيما البينة انها لهما لاحتمال ان تكون لغيرهما ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ ایک زمین ہے جس کے بارے میں دو شخصوں نے دعوی کیا اور دونوں نے بینہ قائم کیا اور یہ ان کے قبضہ میں ہے اور دونوں نے قسمت کا ارادہ کیا تو قاضی اس کو تقسیم نہیں کرے گا یہاں تک کہ دونوں بینہ قائم کریں۔ اس بات پر کہ یہ زمین ان دونو سات سے اس بات کے استمال کی وجہ سے کہ وہ ان کے غیر کی ہو۔ تشریح جامع صغیر کی روایت سے معلوم ہوا کہ اقامت بینہ ضروری ہے۔ اب آگے مصنف فرمائیں گے کہ یہ کس کا قول فرماتے ہیں۔ اقوال فقہاء ثم قيل هو قول أبي حنيفة خاصة وقيل هو قول الكل وهو الاصح لان قسمة الحفظ في العقار غير محتاج اليه وقسمة الملك تفتقر الى قيامه ولا ملک فامتنع الجواز ترجمہ پھر کہا گیا کہ یہ مخصوص ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ سب کا قول ہے اور یہی اصح ہے اسلئے کہ حفاظتی بنوارہ زمین میں اس کی جانب احتیاج نہیں ہے اور ملک کا بٹوارہ قیام ملک کا محتاج ہے اور ملک ہے نہیں تو جواز ممتنع ہو گیا۔ تشریح یعنی جامع صغیر میں جو قول ہے ایک قول کے مطابق تو یہ صرف امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے اور دوسرے قول کے مطابق یہ علماء ثلاثہ کا قول ہے۔ اسی کو صاحب ہدایہ نے اصبح قرار دیا ہے۔ اب اس کی دلیل بیان کریں گے کہ اقامت بینہ یہاں کیوں ضروری ہے۔ اولاً سمجھتے کہ قسمت کی دو قسمیں ہیں: ا بٹوار و اسلئے ہوتا ہے کہ اس شی کی حفاظت ہو اس کو قسمة الحفظ کہتے ہیں۔ - اسلئے بنوارہ ہو کہ ہر ایک کو اس کی ملکیت ممتاز ہو کر مل جائے ۔ اب دیکھئے کہتے ہیں کہ اگر زمین کی اس قسمت مذکورہ اس کو قسمت الحفظ قرار دیں وہ بھی غلط ہے کیونکہ زمین تو خود بخود محفوظ ہے تو اس میں حفاظتی قسمت کا کیا مطلب، اور اگر اس کو قسمۃ الملک قرار دیا جائے تو اس کیلئے ثبوت ملک کی ضرورت ہے اور ملکیت کا ثبوت ہے نہیں تو پھر جو از قسمت ہی ممتنع ہو گیا۔
Two men came to the judge and claimed land, and they established proof that the land was in their possession. Should the judge divide it or not? In al-Jami' al-Saghir: Land claimed by two men who establish proof that it is in their hands and they desire division, the judge does not divide it until they establish proof that it belongs to them, because it might belong to someone else. Translation: In al-Jami' al-Saghir, regarding land claimed by two men who establish proof that it is in their possession and want division, the judge does not divide until they establish proof that it is theirs due to the possibility that it belongs to someone else. Explanation: From the narration of Jami' al-Saghir, it is understood that establishing proof is necessary. Now the author will say whose opinion this is. Statements of the Jurists: Then it was said that this is the opinion of Abu Hanifa alone, and it was said that it is the opinion of all (three imams), and this (latter) is more correct. Because qismat al-hifz (division for preservation) in land is not needed, and qismat al-milk (division of ownership) requires proof of ownership, and there is no (proven) ownership, so permissibility is prevented. Translation: Then it was said that this is specifically the opinion of Abu Hanifa, and it was said that it is the opinion of all, and this is more correct. Because division for preservation is not needed for land, and division of ownership depends on proof of ownership, and there is no ownership, so permissibility is prevented. Explanation: The opinion in Jami' al-Saghir, according to one view, is only that of Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to another view, it is the opinion of the three imams. Sahib al-Hidayah considered the latter as more correct. Now he will give the reason why establishing proof is necessary here. First understand that division is of two types: (1) division for the purpose of preserving the property, called qismat al-hifz; (2) division so that each gets his ownership distinct, called qismat al-milk. Now note: if this division of land is considered qismat al-hifz, that is wrong because land is inherently preserved, so what need is there for preservative division? And if it is considered qismat al-milk, then proof of ownership is required, and ownership is not proven, so permissibility of division is prevented.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an earlier ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir. The scenario: two claimants each prove that the land is in their possession (yad), but they do not prove ownership (milk). The ruling from Jami' al-Saghir is that the judge does not divide the land between them until they prove it belongs to them, because it might belong to someone else. The commentary then discusses whose view this represents. Two opinions are reported: (1) it is the view of Abu Hanifa alone, and (2) it is the view of all three founders (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani). Al-Hidayah declares the latter as the more correct (asahh) position. The reasoning is based on the distinction between two types of division: qismat al-hifz (division for preservation) and qismat al-milk (division of ownership). Since land is inherently preserved, qismat al-hifz is unnecessary. Therefore, the division must be qismat al-milk, which requires proof of ownership. Since ownership is not established, division is not permitted. This ruling guards against the misunderstanding that possession alone suffices for partition.

Key Terms
قسمة الحفظ (qismat al-hifz): Division aimed at preserving the property by giving each co-owner a distinct portion, typically for movable items that need protection.
قسمة الملك (qismat al-milk): Division based on ownership, where each co-owner receives their exact share, requiring proof of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the asahh view in Al-Hidayah, why is proof of ownership required for division of land when claimants only prove possession?
A) Because land needs preservative division.
B) Because division of ownership requires proof of ownership, and land does not need preservative division.
C) Because Abu Hanifa alone requires it.
D) Because the Quran commands it.

Key Takeaway
Division of land requires proof of ownership, not just possession, because land does not need preservative division and only ownership-based division is valid.
