Compulsory Division of Same-Genus Property
Introduces the ruling on compulsory division for same-genus property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a judge can compel partition of jointly owned property and distinguish it from exchange requiring mutual consent.

Core Idea
Judge can compel division only for same-genus property; different genera require mutual consent.

In the Hanafi school, not every joint property can be forcibly divided by a judge. The key factor is the genus (jins) of the property. This lesson unpacks the rule from Kitab al-Qismah, explaining when compulsion is allowed and when it is not, based on the nature of the property and the purpose of division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is the judge's compulsory division. The condition is that the property must be of a single genus (jins wahid).
2
Understand the rationale
When genus is united, the co-owners' purposes are identical; division achieves equality and complete benefit (tamthil wa takmil).
3
Contrast with two genera
If property is of different genera (e.g., camels and horses), there is no genuine mixture. Division becomes an exchange (mu'awadah), which requires mutual consent, not compulsion.
4
Apply to examples
Same genus: cloth, sheep, money of same currency. Mixed genera: camels and horses, rice and wheat, gold and silver.
The judge can compel only for same-genus cases.
5
Determine the ruling for a mixed scenario
If property includes two genera, the judge cannot force division. The parties must agree on a value or exchange; only then can division proceed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور سامانوں کو قاضی تقسیم کرے گا (جبراً) جبکہ ایک جنس سے ہوں اسلئے کہ اتحاد جنس کے وقت مقصود متحد ہے تو قسمت میں تعدیل اور منفعت میں تکمیل حاصل ہو جائے گی۔
تشریح شی منقول میں شرکاء نے قسمت کا مطالبہ کیا اور وہ جنس واحد ہے مثلاً کپڑے ہیں تو جنس کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے یہاں برابری حاصل ہو سکے گی اور منفعت میں تکمیل حاصل ہوگی جو قسمت کا مقصد و موضوع ہے لہذا قاضی تقسیم کر دے گا اور اس میں قاضی کیلئے منکر پر جبر جائز ہوگا۔
قاضی دو جنسوں تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا
ولا يقسم الجنسين بعضها في بعض لانه لا اختلاط بين الجنسين فلا تقع القسمة تمييز ابل تقع معاوضة وسبيلها التراضي دون جبر القاضي
ترجمہ اور قاضی دو جنسوں کو تقسیم نہیں کرے گا ان میں سے بعض کو بعض کے اندر اسلئے کہ دوجنسوں کے درمیان اختلاط نہیں ہوتا تو قسمت تمیز واقع نہیں ہوگی بلکہ وہ معاوضہ واقع ہوگا اور معاوضہ کی سبیل تراضی ہے نہ کہ جبر قاضی ۔
تشریح پہلی صورت میں تو قاضی کو جبر کی ولایت حاصل ہے لیکن اگر دو جنسیں ہوں تو پھر قاضی کو ولایت جبر نہیں ہے مثلا اونٹ اور گھوڑے ہیں تو ان میں اختلاط تو ہو گا نہیں کہ قسمت کو یہاں امتیاز کیلئے قرار دیا جائے بلکہ یہ تو معاوضہ کی صورت ہوگی اور معاوضہ میں جبر نہیں ہو سکتا بلکہ اس کی آسمان راہ یہی ہے کہ شر کا ء راضی ہو جائیں پھر ایسی تقسیم جائز ہے۔
Book of Partition. Translation: Quduri said: The judge will divide (compulsorily) the properties when they are of one genus, because when the genus is united, the purpose is united, so in division equality and in benefit completion will be achieved. Commentary: If the partners demand division and the property is of one genus, e.g., cloth, then due to unity of genus, equality can be achieved and completion of benefit will be achieved, which is the purpose of division; therefore the judge will divide, and for the judge compulsion over the denier is permissible. The judge cannot divide two genera: And he does not divide two genera into each other because there is no mixture between two genera, so division does not occur as separation; rather it occurs as exchange, and its way is mutual consent, not compulsion of the judge. Commentary: In the first case, the judge has authority of compulsion, but if there are two genera, then the judge has no authority of compulsion; e.g., camels and horses: there is no mixture, so division here is not for separation; rather it is a form of exchange, and in exchange there cannot be compulsion; rather its way is that the partners agree, then such division is permissible.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Qismah (Book of Partition) establishes the fundamental principle: a judge may compel a division of jointly owned property only when it is of a single genus (jins wahid). The reasoning is that with a single genus, the parties' purposes are identical, so compulsory division achieves the goals of equality and complete benefit. When the property comprises two different genera (like camels and horses), there is no genuine mixture; dividing them would be an exchange (mu'awadah), not a partition. Exchange requires mutual consent, so the judge cannot compel it. This is a clear ruling from the Hanafi school, based on rational analysis of the nature of property and division.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Partition or division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
جنس (jins): Genus or type of property (e.g., cloth, camels). Unity of genus is key for compulsory division.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion by the judge to enforce division despite a co-owner's refusal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a judge compel division of jointly owned property?
A) When the property is of different genera
B) When the property is of the same genus
C) When the co-owners are all heirs
D) When the property is large in quantity

Key Takeaway
A judge may compel division only for same-genus property; for mixed genera, mutual consent is required as the division is an exchange.

Items Divisible by Compulsion: Weighed, Measured, and More
Enumeration of property types for compulsory division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which categories of property a Hanafi judge can compel to be divided and explain the underlying principle of equality.

Core Idea
Compulsory division requires the possibility of equal shares without gross disparity in value or type.

This passage from al-Hidayah enumerates specific types of property where a judge may compel division between co-owners, and those where he may not. The key is whether the items can be divided into equal portions without creating a gross disparity (tafawut fahish) in value or kind. This is a practical application of the principle of justice in partition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories where division is compulsory
List the categories from the text: (1) weighed items (mawzun), (2) measured items (makil), (3) countable similar items (ma'dud mutaqarib), (4) ingots of gold, silver, iron, copper (tibr), (5) individual herds of camels, cows, sheep.
All these share the property that equal division is feasible without significant disparity.
2
Identify the categories where division is NOT compulsory
List items from the text: (1) mixing different animals (e.g., a sheep and a camel, a horse and a donkey), (2) vessels even if made of the same material due to craftsmanship differences.
In these cases, gross disparity (tafawut fahish) exists, making compulsory division unjust.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The common thread is the possibility of equal division. For weighed/measured/countable items and ingots, equality can be achieved. For different species or crafted items, the value or utility differs too much.
This principle is based on qiyas: the inability to divide fairly without damage or inequity precludes compulsion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقسم كل موزون ومكيل كثيرا اوقليل والمعدود المتقارب وتبر الذهب والفضة وتبر الحديد والنحاس والابل بانفرادها او البقر او الغنم ولا يقسم شاة وبعيرا وبرذونا وحمارا ولا يقسم الاواني لانها باختلاف الصنعة التحقت بالاجناس المختلفة
تشریح پہلی صاحب ہدایہ کچھ تفریعات بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ کن چیزوں کے اندر قاضی جبر اتقسیم کر سکتا ہے اور کہاں نہیں کر سکتا۔ تو بتایا کہ
ا۔ ہر وزنی اور کیلی چیز قلیل ہو یا کثیر ان میں قاضی کو قسمت کا جبر احق ہے۔
۔ یہی حال معدود متقارب کا ہے۔
۔ اور سونے اور چاندی نیز لو ہا اور تانبے کا بھی یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ مساوات و برابری کی جاسکتی ہے۔ تبو ٹکڑا۔
۴۔ تنہا اونٹوں میں اور گائے اور بکری میں قاضی تقسیم کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ ان کے درمیان اتحاد جنس کی وجہ سے تفاوت کم ہے۔ - بکری اور اونٹ گھوڑا اور گدھا ان کے درمیان تفاوت فاحش ہے۔ لہذا یہاں قاضی جبراً تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ جب ایک طرف گھوڑا اور دوسری طرف گدھا جائے گا تو اس میں تفاوت فاحش کا ہونا ظاہر ہے تو اس کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ پہلے گھوڑوں کو تقسیم کر دے
پھر گدھوں کو ۔ - برتنوں کے اندر بھی تفاوت فاحش ہے تو اگر چہ برتن ایک ہی چیز کے ہوں مگر چونکہ ان میں صنعت مختلف ہیں اور اختلاف صنعت اختلاف جنس کے درجہ میں ہے اور مختلف الجنس میں قاضی کو جبرا تقسیم کا حق نہیں ہے۔
And he divides every weighed and measured thing, much or little, and countable similar items, and ingots of gold and silver, and ingots of iron and copper, and camels individually or cows or sheep, and he does not divide a sheep and a camel, and a mule and a donkey, and he does not divide vessels because they, due to difference in craftsmanship, are joined to different genera. Commentary: First, the author of Hidayah states some details: what things the judge can divide by compulsion and where he cannot. So he said: 1. Every weighed and measured thing, little or much – the judge has right of compulsion in division. 2. The same applies to countable similar items. 3. And gold and silver, also iron and copper: the same ruling, because equality can be achieved. [Tabu tukra?]. 4. In camels alone and cows and sheep, the judge can divide because due to unity of genus, the disparity is small. Sheep and camel, horse and donkey: the disparity between them is gross. Therefore, the judge cannot divide by compulsion here. Because when one side gets a horse and the other a donkey, the gross disparity is obvious. The method is to first divide the horses, then the donkeys. In vessels also there is gross disparity, even if the vessels are of the same material, but because the craftsmanship differs, and difference in craftsmanship is on the level of difference in genus, and in different genera the judge has no right to compel division.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed list of items where the judge may or may not compel division. The underlying principle is that compulsory division requires the possibility of equal distribution without significant disparity. Weighed (موزون) and measured (مکيل) items are divisible by nature. Countable similar items (معدود متقارب) also qualify. Precious metal ingots (تبر) are treated similarly because they can be equalized. Individual species of livestock (camels, cows, sheep) are divisible within their own kind due to minor differences. However, mixing different species (sheep with camel) or different animals (horse with donkey) creates gross disparity (تفاوت فاحش), so compulsion is not allowed. Similarly, vessels, even if made of the same material, differ in craftsmanship, which is considered equivalent to difference in genus, hence no compulsory division. Note: the phrase 'tabu tukra' is unclear, but likely refers to breaking or cutting of ingots.

Key Terms
موزون (mawzun): Item sold by weight, such as grains, metals.
مكيل (makil): Item sold by measure (volume), like liquids.
معدود متقارب (ma'dud mutaqarib): Countable items that are similar in value and type, e.g., eggs, nuts.
تبر (tibr): Ingot or lump of metal, especially gold, silver, iron, copper.
تفاوت فاحش (tafawut fahish): Gross disparity in value or type that prevents compulsory division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a judge not compel division of vessels according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because vessels are too many
B) Because vessels differ in craftsmanship, which is treated as a difference in genus
C) Because vessels are not sold by weight
D) Because vessels are always expensive

Key Takeaway
A judge may compel division only where the property can be divided into equal shares without gross disparity; otherwise, co-owners must agree voluntarily.

Division of Cloth and Garments: Conditions for Compulsory Partition
Rulings on compulsory division of cloth and garments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge can compel division of cloth or garments and apply the ruling to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A single garment cannot be divided because cutting destroys its utility; value disparity also prevents compulsory division.

In this passage, al-Marghinani outlines the specific rules for dividing cloth and garments among co-owners. The guiding principle is whether division can be accomplished without causing harm (darar) or gross inequality. We will examine four cases: Marwi cloth of a single type, a single garment, two garments of different value, and three garments, learning the rationale behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of items
List the four distinct items discussed: Marwi cloth (same type), a single garment, two garments of different value, and three garments.
2
Determine the ruling for each category
State whether compulsory division is permissible or not according to the text.
Marwi cloth: permissible; single garment: not permissible; two garments differing in value: not permissible; three garments: permissible with adjustment.
3
Analyze the underlying rationale
For each ruling, explain the legal cause (sabab): unity of type, harm from cutting (darar), value disparity, and possibility of partial division.
Focus on the concept of darar – cutting a single garment renders it useless.
4
Understand the exception for three garments
Three garments can be divided by adjusting shares (e.g., one garment for two garments) because it is a partial division (qismat ba'd) that does not require cutting all items.
Partial division is allowed as it avoids the darar of cutting each garment.
5
Apply the rules to new scenarios
Using the principles, evaluate hypothetical cases such as a bed sheet, a roll of fabric, or a set of different garments.
Test each condition: unity of type, darar, value parity, adjustability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقسم الثوب الهروي لاتحاد الجنس
ترجمہ اور قاضی تقسیم کر دے ہر وی کپڑوں کو جنس کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح خراسان میں ایک شہر ہے جس کا نام ہرات ہے اس کی جانب نسبت کرتے ہوئے ہر وی بولتے ہیں الشباب الهرويه یعنی ہر دی کپڑے۔ جیسے ہمارے یہاں بولتے ہیں بنارسی ساڑھی وغیرہ۔ تو چونکہ یہاں صنف میں اتحاد ہے اسلئے یہاں قاضی جبراً تقسیم کر سکتا ہے۔
ولا يقسم ثوبا واحداً لاشتمال القسمة على الضرر إذ هي لا تتحقق إلا بالقطع
ترجمہ اور قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا ایک کپڑے کو قسمت کے شامل ہونے کی وجہ سے ضرر پر اسلئے کہ قسمت متحقق نہیں ہو گی مگر کاٹنے کے ساتھ ۔
تشریح اگر ایک کپڑا ہے مثلا کر تہ ہے یاشیروانی یا پائجامہ تو اگر اس کو تقسیم کیا جائے گا تو ضرر ہوگا کیونکہ تقسیم کیلئے اس کو کاٹنا پڑے گا پھر وہ کسی کیلئے بھی انتفاع کے قابل نہ رہے گا۔
ولا ثوبين اذا اختلفت قيمتهما لما بينا بخلاف ثلثة اثواب اذا جعل ثوب بثوبين او ثوب وربع ثوب بثوب وثلثة ارباع ثوب لانه قسمة البعض دون البعض وذالك جان
ترجمہ اور تقسیم نہیں کرے گا دو کپڑوں کو جبکہ ان دونوں کی قیمت مختلف ہو اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ بخلاف تین کپڑوں کے جبکہ ایک کپڑے کو دو کپڑوں کے بدلہ میں کر دیا جائے یا ایک کپڑے اور ایک کپڑے کے ۴/ اکو دوسرے کپڑے اور دوسرے کے ۳/۴ کے بدلہ کر دیا جائے اس لئے کہ یہ بعض کی قسمت ہے۔ نہ کہ بعض کی اور یہ جائز ہے۔
And he divides the Marwi cloth due to unity of genus. Commentary: There is a city in Khorasan called Herat; relating to it, they say Marwi cloth. Like we say Banarasi sari etc. Since there is unity of type, the judge can divide by compulsion. And he does not divide a single garment because division includes harm, as it is not realized except by cutting. Commentary: If there is one garment, e.g., a shirt or sherwani or pajama, if it is divided, there will be harm because it must be cut, then it will not remain beneficial for anyone. And he does not divide two garments when their values differ, due to what we have explained. Exception: three garments, when one garment is made equal to two garments, or one garment and a quarter garment to a garment and three-quarters garment, because it is a division of part without the other, and that is permissible.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage concludes the chapter with specific rulings on cloth and garments. First, Marwi cloth (from Herat) of the same genus can be divided by compulsion, similar to any single-genus property. Second, a single garment (e.g., a shirt, sherwani, or pajama) cannot be compulsorily divided because cutting it would destroy its usefulness, causing loss to both parties. This is a deterrent consideration (darar). Third, two garments of different values cannot be divided by compulsion, as value disparity makes equal division impossible. However, three garments can be divided by adjusting shares, e.g., one garment in exchange for two, or one and a quarter in exchange for one and three-quarters. This is permissible because it is a division of some garments only, not all, which is allowed. Note: In the second matn, the Arabic text is corrupted; the correct matn is 'ويقسم الثوب الهروي لاتحاد الجنس' as given in the commentary.

Key Terms
ثوب ہروی (thawb harawi): Cloth from Herat (in Khorasan), of a single type and quality, allowing compulsory division.
ضرر (darar): Harm or loss; here, cutting a single garment renders it useless, preventing compulsory division.
قسمة بعض (qismat ba'd): Division of some items among the partners while leaving others undivided; permissible when shares are adjusted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a judge not compel division of a single garment according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is too small
B) Because it is not of a single genus
C) Because division requires cutting, which would make it useless (harm)
D) Because the judge has no authority over garments

Key Takeaway
Compulsory division of property is only allowed when it can be done without destroying the item's utility or creating gross inequality.

Division of Clothes with Different Values
Ruling on forced division of garments by the qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on forced division (qismah jabr) to scenarios involving garments of differing values, distinguishing when cutting is required and when partial division is permissible.

Core Idea
The qadi can force division only when no cutting is needed – harm prevents compulsion.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the limits of the qadi's power to force division of jointly owned clothes. The general principle is that forced division is only allowed when it does not cause harm, such as cutting the cloth. Through concrete examples, the text illustrates how the number and value of garments determine whether forced division is possible, and it also validates partial division where some items are fully divided and others remain shared.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Rule
State the principle: forced division (jabr) by the qadi is not permissible if it requires cutting the cloth, because cutting causes harm.
The harm (darar) is the key preventing factor.
2
Apply to Two Garments of Different Values
When there are only two garments and they are of unequal value, dividing them equally would require cutting one garment. Therefore, the qadi cannot force division.
Example: one kurta and one sherwani.
3
Apply to Three Garments
With three garments, it may be possible to assign whole garments to each co-owner without cutting. The qadi can then force such a division.
Example: two kurtas and one sherwani – one gets sherwani, other gets both kurtas.
4
Understand Partial Division
Another permissible scenario is partial division: some garments are divided while others remain jointly owned. This does not require cutting and is allowed.
Example: one gets kurta and 3/4 sherwani, other gets pajama and 1/4 sherwani.
5
Confirm the Basis
The underlying justification is that cutting causes harm, so it is avoided. The author quotes the Hidayah: 'it is a division of some parts without others, and that is permissible.'
This illustrates the Hanafi commitment to preventing harm in property division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح اگر دو کپڑے ہیں اور دونوں کی قیمت مختلف ہے وہاں بھی قاضی قسمت پر جبر نہیں کر سکتا۔ مثلاً ایک کرتہ ہے اور ایک شیروانی ہے تو یہاں بھی قسمت کیلئے قطع کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی اور اس کا مضمر ہونا ظاہر ہے۔ اور اگر کپڑے تین ہیں تو وہاں جبر ا تقسیم کی جاسکتی ہے مثلاً دو کرتے ہیں جو قیمتی ہیں اور ایک شیروانی ہے تو شیروانی ایک کو اور دو کرتے ایک کومل جائیں گے تو بالکل قطع کی نوبت نہ آئے گی۔ یا ایک کر تہ اور ایک پائجامہ ہے اور ایک شیروانی ہے تو پائجامہ اور شیروانی کا چوتھائی ایک کو دے دیا اور کرتہ اور شیروانی کے تین چوتھائی دوسرے کو تو کرتے اور پائجامے میں تقسیم ہوگئی شیروانی مشترک رہی تو یہ صورت جائز ہے۔ اس کو مصنف نے کہا ہے ولانه قسمة البعض دون البعض وذالك جائز.
Explanation: If there are two garments and their value is different, the qadi cannot force division. For example, one kurta and one sherwani, then for division cutting would be needed, and its harm is obvious. And if there are three garments, then forced division can be done: for example, two kurtas of value and one sherwani - one gets the sherwani and the other gets two kurtas, so no cutting occurs. Or one kurta, one pajama, and one sherwani: one gets the pajama and a quarter of the sherwani, and the other gets the kurta and three-quarters of the sherwani; so the kurta and pajama are divided, the sherwani remains shared. This is permissible. The author said: 'because it is a division of some parts without others, and that is permissible.'
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the forced division of garments by the qadi. The key principle is that the qadi can compel division only when it does not require cutting the cloth, which would cause harm. With two garments of different values, equal division would require cutting, so the qadi cannot force it. With three garments, it may be possible to assign whole garments to each party without cutting, as in the examples given. Moreover, partial division—where some property is fully divided and some remains shared—is also permissible, as the author states quoting the original text of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division or partition of jointly owned property.
قطع (qat'): Cutting of cloth, which is harmful and thus prevents forced division.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion by the qadi to force division among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only when all garments are of equal value.
B) When there are two garments of different values.
C) When there are three or more garments and whole pieces can be assigned without cutting.
D) Only when the co-owners request it in writing.

Key Takeaway
The qadi's power to force division of garments is limited to cases where no cutting is required; otherwise, partial division or mutual agreement must be used.

Forced Division of Slaves: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forced division of slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state both positions in the intra-Hanafi dispute on forced division of slaves, explain the proofs, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa forbids forced division of slaves because human disparity mirrors different genera.

This passage presents a vital intra-Hanafi debate on whether a qadi can compel co-owners to divide a slave. Abu Hanifa holds that the inherent disparity among humans prevents forced division, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that slaves, as one genus, can be divided like livestock. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates how qiyas (analogy) is constrained when the underlying illa (effective cause) fails due to human uniqueness.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the Core Dispute
Determine the legal issue: does the qadi have authority to force division (qismah jabr) of slaves among co-owners?
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school, not between madhhabs.
2
2. State Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Know that Abu Hanifa prohibits forced division due to tafawut fahish (great disparity) in humans. His proof: humans differ in inner qualities, making them like different genera (jins mukhtalif).
He further argues that male and female humans are treated as separate genera in law, while in animals they are the same.
3
3. State the Sahibayn's Position and Proof
The Sahibayn allow forced division because slaves are of one genus (jins wahid). They analogize to camels and goats (despite internal disparity) and to slaves from war booty.
Their qiyas is based on unity of genus and the permissibility of division in similar cases.
4
4. Examine Abu Hanifa's Rebuttal of the Sahibayn's Qiyas
Abu Hanifa refutes each analogy: (a) animals differ slightly, humans greatly; (b) booty slaves are divided by monetary value only, not by the specific item.
Thus, the two analogies (qiyas al-ibil wa al-ghanam and qiyas al-maghanim) fail due to disparity in the illa.
5
5. Determine the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, co-owners must voluntarily agree; under the Sahibayn, a qadi can force division. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's view.
This affects real estate and partnership disputes involving slaves or people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام اور جواہر کو قاضی تقسیم کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
و قال ابو حنيفة لا يقسم الرقيق والجواهر لتفاوتهما وقالا يقسم الرقيق لاتحاد الجنس كما في الابل والغنم
ورقيق المغنم
ترجمہ اور فرمایا ابو حنیفہ نے قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا غلام کی اور جواہر کی ان دونوں کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا
غلاموں کی تقسیم کر دے گا جنس کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ اونٹ بکری اور غنیمت کے غلاموں کے اندر۔
تشریح غلاموں کے اندر آپس میں تفاوت فاحش ہے اور ایسے ہی ہیروں میں تو قاضی ان میں جبر ا تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا۔ مگر صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ چونکہ غلاموں کی جنس متحد ہے اور اس وجہ سے تقسیم کر دی جائے گی ۔ استدلال میں صاحبین نے فرمایا ۔ جیسے اونٹ اور بکری میں تفاوت کے باوجود قسمت جائز ہے۔ ایسے ہی غنیمت میں جو غلام ملے ان کی قسمت جائز ہے تو یہاں بھی غلاموں کے اندر قسمت جائز ہوگی۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل
وله ان التفاوت في الآدمى فاحش لتفاوت المعانى الباطنة فصار كالجنس المختلف بخلاف الحيوانات لان التفاوت فيها يقل عندا تحاد الجنس الاترى ان الذكور والانثى من بنى آدم جنسان ومن الحيوانات جنس واحد
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آدمی کے اندر معانی باطنہ کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے تفاوت فاحش ہے تو یہ جنس مختلف کے مثل ہو گیا بخلاف حیوانات کے اسلئے کہ تفاوت حیوانات میں قلیل ہے اتحاد الجنس کے وقت کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ مذکر و مونث بنی آدم میں سے دو جنسیں ہیں اور حیوانات میں سے جنس واحد ہے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کا غلام کو حیوانات پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں کیونکہ حیوانات میں اتحاد جنس کی صورت میں تفاوت قلیل ہے۔
اور انسانوں کے اندر معانی باطنہ اور کمالات باطنہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے تفاوت فاحش ہے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ فقہا ، مرد و عورت کو مختلف الجنس شمار کرتے ہیں اور حیوانات کے اندر مذکر و مونث کو متحد الجنس شمار کرتے ہیں ۔
صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب
بخلاف المغانم لان حق الغانمين فى المالية حتى كان للامام بيعها وقسمة ثمنها وههنا يتعلق بالعين والمالية جميعا فافترقا
Can the qadi force division of slaves and jewels? Statements of jurists: Abu Hanifa said: He will not divide slaves and jewels due to their disparity. The two (Sahibayn) said: He will divide slaves due to unity of genus, as in camels and goats, and slaves of war booty. Translation: And Abu Hanifa said: The qadi will not divide slaves and jewels due to their disparity. And the Sahibayn said: He will divide slaves due to unity of genus, like camels, goats, and slaves of war booty. Explanation: Among slaves, the disparity is great, and similarly among jewels, so the qadi cannot force division. But the Sahibayn said: Since the genus of slaves is unified, division will be made. Their evidence: Just as division is permissible among camels and goats despite disparity, similarly division of slaves of booty is permissible, so here too. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: He said: Disparity in humans is severe due to differences in inner qualities, so it is like different genera, unlike animals because disparity in animals is slight when the genus is united. Do you not see that male and female among humans are two genera, while among animals they are one genus? Explanation: This is Abu Hanifa's proof: The Sahibayn's analogy of slaves to animals is incorrect because disparity among animals of the same genus is slight, but among humans it is severe. Response to the Sahibayn's analogy: Unlike booty (ghanim), because the right of the warriors is only in monetary value, to the extent that the Imam may sell them and divide their price; while here the right is attached to both the specific item and the monetary value, so they differ.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the qadi can force the division of slaves (and jewels) among co-owners. Abu Hanifa holds that forced division is not permissible due to the great disparity among human beings in internal qualities, which makes them akin to different species. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that since slaves are of one genus, forced division is allowed, analogizing to camels and goats, and to slaves from war booty. The text then gives Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the disparity in humans is far greater than in animals, even to the point that in Islamic law, male and female humans are considered different genera for some purposes, while in animals they are the same. Finally, a response to the Sahibayn's qiyas on booty: the right of warriors in booty is only in monetary value, not in the specific slave, whereas here co-owners have rights in both the specific item and its value. Therefore, the analogy fails. The implication is that Abu Hanifa's view is stronger.

Key Terms
رقيق (raqiq): Slaves; in this context, male slaves owned as property.
تفاوت فاحش (tafawut fahish): Great or extreme disparity, which prevents forced division.
جنس (jins): Genus or kind; legal category determining homogeneity for division.
مغنم (maghnam): War booty; specifically the slaves taken as booty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Abu Hanifa gives for prohibiting forced division of slaves?
A) Slaves are not valuable enough for division
B) Humans have great internal disparity (tafawut fahish) making forced division inequitable
C) The qadi lacks jurisdiction over slaves
D) Division is only allowed if all parties agree

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that a qadi cannot force division of slaves due to the great disparity among humans, making forced division inequitable.

Why the Judge Cannot Force Division of Inherited Slaves: Refuting Sahibayn's Qiyas
Refuting Sahibayn's analogy of inherited slaves to war booty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa rejects Sahibayn's qiyas on forced division of inherited slaves and distinguish the nature of rights in war booty versus inheritance.

Core Idea
The judge cannot force division of inherited slaves because partners' right attaches to both the property and its value, unlike war booty.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the forced division of jointly inherited slaves. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) had analogized inherited slaves to war booty, where the imam can sell and distribute without the warriors' consent. The author refutes this by identifying a critical distinction: the nature of the partners' right. This lesson unpacks the qiyas and its rebuttal, sharpening your ability to evaluate analogical reasoning in property law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the two conflicting positions: Sahibayn's view that the judge can force division, and Abu Hanifa's view that he cannot.
2
Examine Sahibayn's qiyas
Identify the asl (war booty), the far' (inherited slave), and the claimed illa (shared ownership).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the distinction: in booty, right is only in value; in inheritance, right is in both property and value.
This distinction breaks the qiyas.
4
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: under Sahibayn, judge can force sale; under Abu Hanifa, judge cannot.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The text sides with Abu Hanifa; this is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
اور انسانوں کے اندر معانی باطنہ اور کمالات باطنہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے تفاوت فاحش ہے یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ فقہا ، مرد و عورت کو مختلف الجنس شمار کرتے ہیں اور حیوانات کے اندر مذکر و مونث کو متحد الجنس شمار کرتے ہیں ۔
صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب
بخلاف المغانم لان حق الغانمين فى المالية حتى كان للامام بيعها وقسمة ثمنها وههنا يتعلق بالعين والمالية جميعا فافترقا
ترجمہ بخلاف غلیموں کے اسلئے کہ نامین کا حق مالیت میں ہے یہاں تک کہ امام کو حق ہے غنیمت کو بیچنے اور اس کی شمن کو تقسیم کرنے کا اور یہاں حق عین اور مالیت دونوں کے ساتھ متعلق ہے تو یہ دونوں جدا جدا ہو گئے۔
تشریح صاحبین نے رقیق کو رقیق غنیمت پر قیاس کیا تھا۔ اس کا جواب دیا گیا کہ یہ قیاس بھی صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ غنیمت میں مجاہدین کا حق فقط مالیت کا ہے اور رقیق مذکور میں شرکاء کا حق مین و مالیت دونوں میں ہے۔ یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ امام کو حق ہے غنیمت کے غلاموں کو فروخت کر کے ان کی قیمت غانمین کے درمیان تقسیم کر دے اور یہاں قاضی کو اس کا حق نہیں ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ قیاس مذکور درست نہیں۔
Book of Division. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume 13. And among humans, due to the difference in inner meanings and inner perfections, there is a huge disparity. This is the reason why jurists consider male and female as different species, and among animals they consider male and female as the same species. Response to the qiyas of Sahibayn: Contrary to war booty, because the right of those who obtain spoils is in the monetary value, to the extent that the imam has the right to sell it and divide its price. And here (in the case of inherited slaves) the right is attached to both the physical property and the monetary value, so they are distinct. Translation: Contrary to war booty, because the right of the ghanimin is in the monetary value, to the extent that the imam has the right to sell the spoils and divide their price. And here the right is related to both the physical property and the monetary value, so these two are separate. Explanation: Sahibayn had analogized the slave to the slave of war booty. This was answered that this analogy is also not correct, because in war booty the right of the mujahideen is only in the monetary value, and in the mentioned slave the right of the partners is in both the physical property and the monetary value. This is the reason why the imam has the right to sell the slaves of war booty and divide their price among the ghanimin, while here the judge does not have that right. It is understood that the mentioned analogy is not correct.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the forced division of inherited slaves. The matn likely states that the judge cannot force division of inherited slaves. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) raised a qiyas: if war booty slaves can be sold and divided by the imam without the warriors' consent, then inherited slaves should also be divisible by the judge. The author refutes this by pointing out a fundamental difference in the nature of the right. In war booty, the warriors' right is solely in the monetary value (al-maliyyah), so the imam can sell the actual slaves and distribute the price. However, in inherited slaves, the partners' right is attached to both the physical property (al-ayn) and the monetary value. Therefore, selling the actual object would violate that right. Hence, the judge cannot force division without consent. This distinction is key to understanding why the analogy fails.

Key Terms
رقیق (raqiq): A male slave, specifically the one inherited by partners in this context.
غنیمت (ghanimat): War booty taken from the enemy, which becomes state property before distribution to warriors.
غانمین (ghanimin): The warriors who participated in the battle and are entitled to a share of the spoils.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared illa.
ضرر (darar): Harm or detriment that would result from forced division, used as a reason to prohibit it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does the judge not have the right to force division of inherited slaves?
A) Because the imam has exclusive authority over war booty.
B) Because the partners' right is only in the monetary value.
C) Because the partners' right is in both the physical property and monetary value.
D) Because slaves are not considered property in inheritance.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a qiyas depends on identifying the correct illa; here, the distinction between monetary-only rights and dual rights invalidates the analogy.

Three Opinions on Forced Division of Jewels
Presenting three views on forced division of shared jewels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on forced division of jewels, explain the reasoning behind each, and apply the strongest opinion (mufta bihi) using the evidence from marriage mahr.

Core Idea
Jewels cannot be forced to divide because their value uncertainty is greater than that of slaves.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical problem in partnership law: when two people own a jewel jointly and one wants to force division, can the judge compel it? The text presents three views within the Hanafi school, culminating in an absolute prohibition based on a powerful analogy from marriage mahr. Understanding these opinions reveals the school's careful handling of uncertain property (jahalah) in financial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
List the three views: (1) division prohibited if species differ (pearls vs. rubies), (2) large jewels not divided, small divided due to disparity level, (3) absolute prohibition for all jewels.
2
Understand the rationale for each
Opinion 1: species difference causes extreme uncertainty. Opinion 2: size affects degree of uncertainty – large jewels have greater variation. Opinion 3: all jewels have extreme uncertainty regardless of size or species.
3
Recognize the dalil
The proof for the third opinion is a qiyas awla (a fortiori analogy) from marriage mahr: specifying a jewel as mahr invalidates the contract due to jahalah, whereas specifying a slave is valid. Since slaves cannot be forced to divide, jewels are even more deserving of that prohibition.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the absolute prohibition (third opinion), as it is the most consistent with the principle of avoiding jahalah and is supported by the author's preference (awla).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاما الجواهر فقد قيل اذا اختلف الجنس لا يقسم كاللآلي واليواقيت وقيل لا يقسم الكبار منها لكثرة التفاوت ويقسم الصغار لقلة التفاوت وقيل يجرى الجواب على اطلاقه لان جهالة الجواهر افحش من جهالة الرقيق الأترى انه لوتزوج على لؤلؤة او ياقوتة او خالع عليها لاتصح التسمية ويصح ذالك على عبد فالاولى ان لا يجبر على القسمة
ترجمہ پس بہر حال جواہر پس کہا گیا ہے کہ جب جنس مختلف ہو تو قاضی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا جیسے موتی اور یا قوت اور کہا گیا ہے کہ ان میں سے بڑوں کی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا تفاوت کی کثرت کی وجہ سے اور چھوٹوں کو تقسیم کر دے گا تفاوت کی قلت کی وجہ سے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ جواب اپنے اطلاق پر جاری ہے۔ اسلئے کہ جواہر کی جہالت رقیق کی جہالت سے زیادہ بخش ہے۔ کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر نکاح کیا موتی اور یا قوت پر یا ان پر ضلع کیا تو تسمیہ صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس بدرجہ اولی یہ بات ہوگی کہ قسمت پر جبر نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہیروں کے اندر عدم قسمت کا بیان فرمایا ہے۔ اب یہاں تین قول بیان کرتے ہیں :- - اگر ان کی جنس مختلف ہو تو پھر قاضی جبر ا تقسیم نہیں کر سکتا جسے موتی اور یا قوت کی جنس مختلف ہے۔ ۲۔ بڑے ہیروں میں تفاوت زیادہ ہے اور چھوٹوں میں کم ہے لہذا اول میں تقسیم صحیح نہیں اور ثانی میں جائز ہے۔ ۳- مطلقاً جائز نہیں کیونکہ ہیروں کے اندر مطلق غلاموں سے زیادہ جہالت ہے اور جب غلاموں کے اندر جبر ا تقسیم نہ ہوگی تو ہیروں کے اندر بدرجہ اولی نہ ہوگی۔
سوال ہیروں میں تفاوت رقیق کے تفاوت سے زیادہ ہے اس کی دلیل کیا ہے؟ جواب اگر کسی نے کسی عورت سے نکاح کیا اور مہر میں یا قوت یا موتی کا نام لیا تو چونکہ اس میں تفاوت فاحش ہے اسلئے یہ تسمیہ معتبر نہ ہوگا اور اگر غلام پر نکاح کرتا تو یہاں تسمیہ درست ہے ہدایہ جلد ثانی باب المبر میں جس کی تفصیلات موجود ہیں۔
As for jewels, it is said: if the species differ, they are not divided, like pearls and rubies. And it is said: the large ones among them are not divided due to great disparity, and the small ones are divided due to little disparity. And it is said: the answer runs on its absolute (generality), because the unknown (jahalah) of jewels is more egregious than the unknown of slaves. Do you not see that if one marries on a pearl or a ruby, or divorces by khul' for them, the specification (tasmiyah) is not valid, whereas it is valid for a slave? So a fortiori, one should not be compelled to division. Translation: So in any case, regarding jewels, it is said: when the species differ, the judge will not divide, like pearls and rubies. And it is said: among them, the large ones will not be divided due to the abundance of disparity, and the small ones will be divided due to the scarcity of disparity. And it is said: the answer runs on its absolute (generality), because the ignorance (jahalah) of jewels is more repugnant than the ignorance of slaves. Do you not see that if one marries on a pearl or a ruby, or divorces by khul' on them, the specification is not valid? So a fortiori, it will be that one should not be compelled to division. Explanation: The author of Hidayah stated the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding non-division of diamonds. Now here three sayings are mentioned: 1. If their species differ, then the judge cannot compel division, such as the different species of pearls and rubies. 2. In large diamonds, disparity is great, in small ones it is little; hence in the first, division is not valid, in the second it is permissible. 3. Absolutely not permissible, because in diamonds, the ignorance is greater than in slaves, and when in slaves there is no forced division, then a fortiori in diamonds there will not be. Question: What is the proof that disparity in diamonds is greater than disparity in slaves? Answer: If someone marries a woman and mentions in the dower a ruby or a pearl, because of the egregious disparity, this specification is not valid. But if he marries on a slave, the specification is valid. Details are in Hidayah, volume 2, chapter on al-mabr.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage presents three opinions regarding the forced division of jointly owned jewels (jawahir). The first opinion distinguishes based on species: if the jewels are of different types (e.g., pearls vs. rubies), the judge cannot force division because mixing different species would introduce excessive uncertainty. The second opinion distinguishes by size: large jewels have significant quality variation, so forced division is not allowed, while small jewels have minimal variation, so it may be allowed. The third opinion (and the strongest, as the commentary suggests) is that forced division is absolutely prohibited for all jewels, because the unknown (jahalah) regarding jewels is even greater than that regarding slaves. The proof is taken from nikah: if a pearl or ruby is specified as mahr, the marriage contract is invalid due to the extreme unknown (since such jewels vary vastly in value). In contrast, specifying a slave as mahr is valid. Since slaves cannot be forced to divide (as established earlier), jewels should be treated the same way a fortiori (bi al-awla). This shows the Hanafi school's caution in forcing division of items with high value variation.

Key Terms
جواہر (jawahir): Precious stones, jewels, including pearls and rubies.
جہالت (jahalah): Legal uncertainty about the value or quality of an object, which can invalidate contracts or prevent forced division.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The specification of mahr (dower) in a marriage contract or the specified property in khul' divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third and most authoritative opinion, why can a judge not force division of jewels?
A) Because jewels are too small to divide.
B) Because the jahalah in jewels is greater than in slaves, and slaves themselves cannot be forced to divide.
C) Because the partners never agree on the division of jewels.
D) Because jewels are not considered property in Hanafi law.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that forced division of jewels is absolutely prohibited because their value uncertainty exceeds even that of slaves.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Combining Houses in Division
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing multiple houses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding combining multiple houses in division, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) in a judge's decision.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa requires separate division of houses; Sahibayn leave it to the judge — equity demands individual assessment.

This passage presents an important intra-Hanafi disagreement on property division (qismah). When multiple houses are jointly owned, can the judge combine them in a single division, or must each be divided separately? Imam Abu Hanifa takes a strict view emphasizing the practical impossibility of equating properties with vastly different values, while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) grant the judge discretion based on the degree of similarity. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the Hanafi method of weighing textual and rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the legal question being debated? Is it permissible to combine multiple houses into a single division (qismah jami'ah) or must each be divided separately (qismah fardah)?
This is the core ikhtilaf.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa requires separate division. His evidence: the objective (maqsud) varies extremely with location, neighbors, etc., making equitable adjustment impossible. He analogizes with agency to buy a house and specifying a house as dower, both invalid due to extreme disparity.
He cites the principle that meaning (ma'na) is the basis, and it differs fundamentally.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and dalil
The Sahibayn argue that houses have two aspects: unity of genus (residence, name) and difference of genus (meaning, amenities). Because both exist, the judge may choose either combined or individual division based on his assessment of which aspect prevails.
They leave the choice to the judge's ijtihad.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a case of multiple shared houses, the judge following Imam Abu Hanifa would divide each separately, while following the Sahibayn he may combine them if he deems them similar enough. This affects the division's fairness and feasibility.
The difference is in the judge's discretion vs. a strict rule.
5
Note the tarjih (preferred view)
The passage does not explicitly state a preferred view. However, later Hanafi fatwa practice often relies on Imam Abu Hanifa's view for precision, though the Sahibayn's view is also applied when equality can be achieved.
The mufta bihi may vary by context.

ترجمہ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ (ادوار ) سکنی کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے نام اور صورت کے اعتبار سے جنس واحد سے مختلف جنسیں میں معنی کے اعتبار سے مقاصد کے اختلاف اور وجوہ سکنی کے اختلاف کی جانب نظر کرتے ہوئے تو ترجیح قاضی کی رائے کی جانب مفوض ہوگی ۔ تشریح سکنی تو ہر گھر میں حاصل ہو سکتا ہے مگر بعض گھروں میں جو راحت و آرام ملتا ہے وہ دوسرے میں نہ ملے یہ ہوتا رہتا ہے اور یہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ متحد الجنس چیزیں ایک ساتھ تقسیم ہوں گی اور مختلف الاجناس الگ الگ۔
تو حضرات صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ دار میں دو پہلو میں اتحاد جنس کا بھی اور اختلاف جنس کا بھی ، تو ہم نے دونوں کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اس معاملہ کو قاضی کی رائے پر چھوڑ دیا وہ اتحاد جنس کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے قسمت جمع کو اختیار کرے تو کر سکتا ہے اور ختلاف جنس کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے قسمت فرد کو اختیار کرے تو کر سکتا ہے۔
اگر ہم یہ دیکھیں کہ دار نفس سکنی میں سب برابر ہیں اور نام اور صورت میں اتحاد ہے تو اس سے اتحاد جنس کا پتہ چلتا ہے اور اگر دوسرے عوارض کو دیکھا جائے تو چونکہ معنی میں تفاوت ہے تو اس سے اختلاف جنس کا پتہ چلتا ہے۔ بہر حال ہم نے دونوں کی رعایت کی ہے۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل
وله ان الاعتبار للمعنى وهو المقصود ويختلف ذالك باختلاف البلدان والمحال والجيران والقرب الى المسجد والماء اختلافاً فاحشا فلا يمكن التعديل فى القسمة ولهذا لا يجوز التوكيل بشراء دار وكذا لوتزوج على دار لا تصح التسمية كما هو الحكم فيهما فى الثوب بخلاف الدار الواحدة اذا اختلفت بيوتها لان في قسمة كل بيت على حدة ضررا فقسمت الدار قسمة واحدة
ترجمہ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معنی کا عتبار ہے اور معنی ہی مقصود ہے اور مقصود بدل جاتا ہے شہروں اور محلوں اور پڑوسیوں کے اختلافات سے اور مسجد اور پانی کے قرب سے اختلاف فاحش کے ساتھ تو قسمت میں برابری ممکن نہ ہو گی ۔ اور اسی وجہ سے گھر کے خریدنے میں تو کیل جائز نہ ہوگی اور ایسے ہی اگر دار پر نکاح کیا تو تسمیہ صحیح نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ یہی حکم ہے ان دونوں ( توکیل و تزوج میں ) میں کپڑے کے اندر بخلاف ایک گھر کے جبکہ اس کے بیوت مختلف ہوں۔ اسلئے کہ ہر گھر کو الگ الگ بانٹنے میں ضرر ہے تو دار کو قسمت واحدہ کے ساتھ تقسیم کر دیا جائیگا۔ تشریح امام ابوحنیفہ نے دلیل دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ پیڑ گئے ہیں یا آم کھانے ہیں یعنی فقط معنی اور مقصود کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور بظا ہر ہے کہ مقصود کے اندر شہروں کے اور محلوں کے بدل جانے سے اختلاف فاحشن پیدا ہوتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی پڑوسیوں کی وجہ سے اور مسجد سے قرب و بعد کی وجہ سے اختلاف فاحش ہوا کرتا ہے۔ جب بات یوں ہے تو پھر ایک ساتھ ملا کر قسمت میں برابری نہ ہو سکے گی جو قسمت کا اصلی مقصد ہے۔ چونکہ گھروں میں اختلاف فاحش ہے تو اگر کسی نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا کہ میرے لئے ایک گھر خرید دو تو یہ تو کیل صحیح نہ ہوگی۔
اسی طرح اگر مرد نے نکاح کرتے وقت مہر کے بارے میں کہا کہ ایک گھر دوں گا تو یہ تسمیہ صحیح نہ ہوگا اور بجائے گھر کے یہ تو کیل و تزوج کا مسئلہ کپڑے کے اندر ہو تو وہاں بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ توکیل صحیح نہیں اور تزوج میں تسمیہ صحیح نہیں۔ اسلئے کہ کپڑوں کے اندر بھی اختلاف فاحش ہے۔ ہاں اگر ایک دار دو شریکوں میں مشترک ہے جس میں چند بیوت ہیں تو یہاں اگر ہر کمرہ کی تقسیم الگ ہو تو نقصان کا ہونا ظاہر ہے۔ اسلئے یہاں قسمت جمع کو اختیار کیا جائے گا۔ اور ایک کو کچھ بیوت اور دوسرے کو کچھ بیوت دے دیئے جائیں گے۔
Book of Division. 10. Translation: The evidence of the Sahibayn is that this (periods?) consideration of residence in terms of name and form, from the aspect of a single genus, to different species in terms of meaning, the difference of objectives and the difference of reasons of residence, then the preference is entrusted to the opinion of the judge. Explanation: Residence can be obtained in every house, but the comfort and ease found in some houses is not found in others; this continues. And it has passed earlier that things of the same type are divided together, and different types separately. So the Sahibayn say: In a house there are two aspects, unity of type and difference of type. So we, observing both, left this matter to the opinion of the judge. If he chooses combined division based on unity of type, he may; and if he chooses individual division based on difference of type, he may. If we look that houses are equal in the essence of residence and have unity in name and form, then this indicates unity of type. And if other attributes are considered, since there is difference in meaning, this indicates difference of type. In any case, we have observed both. The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa: 'And for him: Verily consideration is for meaning, and it is the objective, and that differs with differences of cities, localities, neighbors, proximity to mosque and water, with extreme difference, so equitable division is not possible. For this, appointment of an agent to purchase a house is not valid, and likewise if one marries on (the consideration of) a house, the specification (of dower) is not valid, just as is the ruling in both these (agency and marriage) in the case of cloth. Unlike a single house when its rooms differ, because dividing each room separately causes harm, so the house is divided in a single division.' Translation: And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that meaning is considered, and meaning is the objective, and the objective changes with differences of cities, localities, neighbors, and proximity to mosque and water with extreme difference, so equitable division is not possible. And for this reason, appointment of an agent to purchase a house is not permissible, and similarly if marriage is upon a house, the specification (of dower) is not valid, just as this is the ruling in both (agency and marriage) in the case of cloth. Unlike a single house when its rooms differ, because dividing each room separately causes harm, so the house is divided with a single division. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa, presenting evidence, said that fruits are eaten, meaning only meaning and objective are considered, and apparently, the objective changes due to change of cities and localities, causing extreme difference. Similarly, due to neighbors and proximity to mosque, extreme difference occurs. When this is the case, then combining together equitable division cannot be achieved, which is the main objective of division. Since there is extreme difference in houses, if someone appointed an agent that 'buy a house for me', then this agency is not valid. Similarly, if a man at the time of marriage said about the dower, 'I will give a house,' then this specification is not valid. And instead of a house, if this issue of agency and marriage occurs in cloth, then also the same ruling applies: agency is not valid and specification in marriage is not valid, because there is extreme difference in cloth. Yes, if there is one house shared by two partners, which contains several rooms, then if each room is divided separately, harm is apparent. Therefore, here combined division will be adopted, and some rooms will be given to one and some to the other.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the division of multiple houses owned jointly. The Sahibayn hold that houses have two aspects: unity of genus (jins) in terms of the essence of residence and name, and difference of genus in terms of meaning, location, and amenities. Since both aspects exist, they leave the choice to the judge: he may combine all houses in a single division (qismah jami'ah) or divide each separately (qismah fardah), based on his assessment of equality. Imam Abu Hanifa, on the other hand, argues that the true consideration is the meaning (ma'na) and purpose (maqsud), which vary greatly based on city, neighborhood, neighbors, proximity to mosque and water. Such extreme disparity (tafawut fahish) makes equitable adjustment impossible. Therefore, he requires that multiple houses be divided individually. To support his position, he draws an analogy with the permissibility of agency (tawkil) and marriage (tazwij): just as one cannot validly appoint an agent to buy an unspecified house (due to great variation among houses), and just as specifying a house as dower is invalid (because the house is not adequately known), similarly multiple houses cannot be equitably combined. This is analogous to cloth, which also varies greatly. However, Imam Abu Hanifa makes an exception: if a single house has multiple rooms (buyut), they must be divided together in one division because separating them would cause harm (darar). The commentary explains that the Sahibayn's view grants flexibility, considering both aspects, while Imam's view emphasizes the practical impossibility of equalizing significantly different properties. The discussion also clarifies that the ruling on cloth follows the same principle. This lesson establishes that the default in the Hanafi school for dividing multiple houses is individual division, except when the owner(s) or judge decide otherwise based on the Sahibayn's concession.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners. In this context, the method of dividing houses.
اتحاد جنس (ittihad jins): Unity of genus: similarity in essence, name, and form. Here, houses are of the same genus regarding the essence of residence.
اختلاف جنس (ikhtilaf jins): Difference of genus: dissimilarity in meaning, utility, or value. Here, houses differ in location, amenities, etc.
سكنى (sukna): Residence; the primary function of a house, which is common to all houses.
ضرر (darar): Harm or loss. In division, harm occurs if dividing a single house's rooms separately would cause loss of value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is it not permissible to combine multiple houses in a single division?
A) Because houses are of different genera by essence.
B) Because the extreme difference in meaning and value makes equitable division impossible.
C) Because the Sahibayn ruled against combining.
D) Because it is a form of gambling.

Key Takeaway
The division of multiple houses is subject to intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the judge must assess if the houses are so different that only separate division yields equity.

Division of Two Houses in Two Different Cities
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining houses in two cities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining houses in two cities for compulsory division and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Two houses in two cities are not combined in compulsory division according to the Sahibayn.

When co-owners own houses in different cities, can they request a single court division combining both properties? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point. This lesson unpacks the dispute between the Sahibayn and a narration of Imam Muhammad, and establishes the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Start with the text of Quduri: division is discussed for houses in 'one city'. Note that this restriction is deliberate.
2
State the Sahibayn position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), houses in different cities are not combined; each must be divided separately.
This is also reported by Hilal from them.
3
State the conflicting narration
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani also has another narration that allows combining the houses into one division.
This shows intra-madhhab ikhtilaf even from the same imam.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator and later authorities (Durr al-Mukhtar, Shami) side with the Sahibayn, making their view the operative position for fatwa.
Thus separate division is required.

دو شہروں میں مشترکہ گھر ہوں تو کیسے تقسیم کیا جائے گا
قال تقييد الوضع في الكتاب اشارة الى ان الدارين اذا كانتا في مصرين لا تجمعان في القسمة عندهما وهو رواية هلال عنهما وعن محمد انه يقس مدانه يقسم إحدهما في الأخرى ترجمہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا وضع مسئلہ کو مقید کر دینا کتاب میں اس بات کی جانب اشارہ ہے کہ وہ گھر جبکہ دو شہروں میں ہو تو قسمت میں جمع نہیں کئے جائیں گے صاحبین کے نزدیک اور یہی صاحبین سے ہلال کی روایت ہے اور محمدؐ سے مروی ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک کو دوسرے کے ساتھ مل کر تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسئلہ کی وضع میں امام قدوری نے فی مصر واحد کی قید لگا رکھی ہے جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر دو شہروں میں گھر ہوں تو صاحبین کے نزدیک بھی اب قسمت فرد اختیار کی جائے گی ۔ ہلال نے صاحبین سے یہی روایت کیا ہے۔ اور امام محمد کی دوسری روایت اس کے برعکس ہے یعنی قسمت جمع کے ساتھ تقسیم درست ہے۔ صاحب در مختار کہتے ہیں وفی مصرین فقولهما كقوله - ملاحظہ ہو شامی ص ۱۶۶ ج ۵
Question: How are jointly owned houses in two cities divided? He said: Restricting the case in the book indicates that when two houses are in two cities, they are not combined in division according to them (Sahibayn), and this is Hilal's narration from them. And from Muhammad, he divides [؟] such that one is divided within the other. Translation: The author of Hidayah said: Restricting the case indicates that when there are two houses in two cities, they are not combined in division according to Sahibayn, and this is narrated by Hilal from them. And from Muhammad, it is narrated that one of them is combined with the other for division. Commentary: The author of Hidayah says that Imam Quduri has imposed the restriction of 'in one city' in the case, indicating that if there are houses in two cities, according to Sahibayn as well, individual division will be adopted. Hilal narrated this from Sahibayn. And there is another narration from Imam Muhammad contrary to this, i.e., collective division is valid. The author of Durr al-Mukhtar says: 'In two cities, their view is like his view' – see Shami vol. 5 p. 166.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of two jointly owned houses located in two different cities. The base text of Quduri restricts the case to a single city. The commentary explains that this restriction implies that if the houses are in two cities, they are not combined for division according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani). Hilal reported this from them. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani has another narration that allows combining them for division. The commentator notes that the author of Durr al-Mukhtar agrees with the Sahibayn. The practical consequence is that a judge must decide based on the dominant narration.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division or partition of jointly owned property among co-owners.
صاحبین (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main students of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this passage, how are two jointly owned houses in different cities divided?
A) They are combined into one division.
B) Each is divided separately.
C) The owners choose the method.
D) They are sold and proceeds divided.

Key Takeaway
Two houses in different cities cannot be combined in compulsory division per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Division of Houses and Buildings in Hanafi Partition Law
Ruling on dividing houses and intermediate buildings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify properties as bayt, dar, or manzil and state the correct Hanafi method for dividing co-owned properties based on similarity and contiguity.

Core Idea
Houses in the same alley are divided collectively; buildings (manazil) follow the ruling of houses if attached, or of large houses (dar) if separated.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical issue in property partition: how to divide co-owned properties that are not identical. The Hanafi jurists classify dwellings into small houses (buyut), large estates (dur), and an intermediate category, manazil. Understanding this classification is essential for applying the correct division method, which varies based on similarity of value and physical contiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type
Look at the description of the property: is it a small house (bayt), a large mansion (dar), or something in between (manzil)? The passage defines manzil as intermediate in size.
The classification affects the division method.
2
Determine similarity and contiguity
For bayt properties, assume they are similar enough to allow collective division. For manazil, check whether they are physically attached (muttasil) or separated (mutabayin).
Attachment is the key factor for manazil, not for bayt.
3
Apply the division rule
If the properties are bayt or attached manazil, they are divided collectively (qismah wahidah). If they are separated manazil, each is divided individually like a dar.
Collective division means pooling all similar units and dividing shares proportionally; individual division means each unit is assigned to a co-owner.
4
Consider time and custom
Allamah Shami notes that in his era, even bayt properties could vary greatly, so the classical rule may require adjustment based on actual value differences.
This is a caution: the mufti should assess whether the properties are truly similar before applying collective division.
5
State the practical outcome
The chosen method determines each co-owner's share. Collective division simplifies distribution; individual division requires valuation and possible compensation.
The goal is a fair and practical partition consistent with Hanafi principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک محلہ یا چند محلوں میں تقسیم کا طریقہ
والبيوت فى محلة او محال تقسم قسمة واحدة لان التفاوت فيما بينها يسير والمنازل المتلازقة كالبيوت والمتباينة كالدور لانه بين الدار والبيت على ما مر من قبل فاخذ شبها من كل واحد
ترجمہ اور ایک محلہ یا چند محلوں میں بہوت کو قسمت واحدہ کے ساتھ تقسیم کیا جائے گا اسلئے کہ ان کے درمیان تفاوت کم ہے اور منازل متلاصقہ ( متصلہ ) بیوت کے مثل ہیں اور متباینہ گھروں کے مثل ہیں اسلئے کہ منزل دار اور بیت کے درمیان ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے تو منزل لے لے گی مشابہت کو ہر ایک سے۔ تشریح دارکا تفصیلی حکم بیان کرنے کے بعد فرماتے ہیں کہ بیوت کا حکم اور ہے کہ ان میں زیادہ تفاوت نہیں ہوتا لہذا اگر ایک ہی یا چند محلوں میں مختلف بیوت ہیں تو سب کو ایک ساتھ ملا کر تقسیم کی جاسکتی ہے۔
اب رہا مسئلہ منازل کا جو کہ دار سے چھوٹی اور بہیت سے بڑی ہوتی ہے یعنی اس کا درجہ دار اور بیت کے درمیان ہے تو ہم نے کہا کہ
جب اس کی دونوں سے مشابہت ہے تو حکم کے اندر بھی دونوں سے مشابہت ہونی چاہئے۔
لہذا ہم نے کہا کہ منزلیں اگر متصل ہیں تو ان کا حکم بیوت کا ہے یعنی قسمت جمع درست ہے، اور اگر الگ الگ ہیں تو پھر اس کا حکم دار کا ہے اور قسمت فرد کو اختیار کرنا ضروی ہے اور دار و منزل وبیت کی تفصیل مصنف نے باب الحقوق ہدایہ ص ۷۰ ج ۳ پر کی ہے۔ علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں : اقول و لعل هذا في زمانهم والا فالمنازل والبيوت ولو من دار واحدة تتفاوت تتفاوتا فاحشانی زماننا.... الخ شامی ص ۱۶۶ ج ۵
The method of division in one alley or multiple alleys. And the houses in one alley or alleys are divided as one division because the difference between them is slight. And attached buildings are like houses, and separated ones are like (larger) houses because it is between a dar and a bayt as previously mentioned, so it takes resemblance from each. Translation: And in one alley or multiple alleys, houses will be divided as a single division because the difference between them is small. And attached buildings are like houses, and separated ones are like larger houses because a building is between a dar and a bayt according to the detail that has passed, so a building takes resemblance from each. Commentary: After explaining the detailed ruling of dar, he says that the ruling of houses is different: there is not much difference among them, so if there are various houses in one or several alleys, they can be combined and divided together. Now the issue of buildings which are smaller than a dar and larger than a bayt, i.e., their status is between dar and bayt. So we said: since it has resemblance to both, its ruling should also resemble both. Thus we said: if buildings are attached, their ruling is that of houses, i.e., collective division is valid; and if they are separated, then their ruling is that of a dar, and individual division is necessary. The author has given the detail of dar, building, and house in the chapter of rights in Hidayah vol. 3 p. 70. Allamah Shami says: I say perhaps this was in their time, otherwise buildings and houses, even from one dar, differ greatly in our time... etc. (Shami vol. 5 p. 166).
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for dividing houses (buyut) located in one or several neighborhoods. Since houses are typically similar in value, they can be divided collectively as one unit. The passage then defines 'manazil' (buildings) as structures between a dar (large house) and a bayt (small house). The ruling for manazil depends on whether they are physically attached: if attached, they follow the ruling of houses (collective division); if separated, they follow the ruling of dar (individual division). The commentator adds a note from Shami that this classification may be outdated, as in contemporary times even buildings within one dar can differ greatly, implying the need for case-by-case assessment.

Key Terms
بیت (bayt): A small house or room; in this context, a modest dwelling.
دار (dar): A large house or estate, typically with multiple rooms or courtyards.
منزل (manzil): A building intermediate in size between dar and bayt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for dividing buildings (manazil) that are physically separated?
A) They are divided collectively like houses.
B) They are divided individually like larger houses (dar).
C) They cannot be divided at all.
D) The owners may choose.

Key Takeaway
Houses (buyut) are divided collectively; buildings (manazil) are divided like houses if attached, like large houses (dar) if separated.

Partition with Right of Way and Irrigation: Preference vs Obligation
Ruling on partition with ancillary rights and drawing lots

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating ancillary rights in property partition and explain the legal status of drawing lots.

Core Idea
In Hanafi partition, separating a share with its path and water rights is preferred, not obligatory, and drawing lots is recommended, not required.

This lesson expands on a ruling from Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, as explained in the Hidayah commentary. It clarifies two common points of confusion: whether a share must always be separated with its rights intact, and whether drawing lots is mandatory. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi law in property divisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the separation of a share that includes a right of way and water right. According to the text, it is preferred (afdaliyyah) to do so, but not obligatory.
The ruling is one of preference, not obligation.
2
Distinguish preferred from permissible
The text explicitly states that if the judge does not separate the share with rights, or if it is not possible, the partition is still permissible (ja'iz).
The default permissibility remains even when the preferred action is omitted.
3
Understand the judge's authority
The judge has binding authority (wilayat al-ilzam) and can assign shares without drawing lots. Drawing lots is only a means to reassure parties and avoid bias.
The qasim (divider) acts as the judge's deputy and shares this authority.
4
Recognize the non-obligatory nature of lots
The text says 'drawing lots is not necessary' (قرعہ ڈالنا کچھ ضروری نہیں). It is recommended but not fard or wajib.
Lots are a procedural tool, not a legal requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القسمة تشریح یعنی امام قدوری نے جو فرمایا ہے کہ یہ ایک حصہ مع راستہ اور شرب کے الگ کر دے۔ یہ افضلیت کا بیان ہے ورنہ اگر قاضی ایسا نہ کرے یا یہ ممکن نہ ہو تو جب بھی جائز ہے۔ اور قرعہ ڈالنا کچھ ضروری نہیں بلکہ صرف دلوں کو مطمئن کرنے اور یہ تہمت دور کرنے کیلئے ہے کہ قاضی نے فلاں کی رخ داری کی ہے۔ ورنہ اگر قاضی بغیر قرعہ کے خود حصے مقرر کر دے تو کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ قاضی کو ولایت الزام حاصل ہے اور یہ بھنی کا ر قضاء ہے۔ اور اگر قاسم ہو تو وہ بھی قاضی کا نمائندہ ہے وہ بھی حصے مقرر کر سکتا ہے۔
Book of Partition. Elucidation: Imam Quduri said: He should separate this one share along with the road and water right. This is a statement of preference. Otherwise, if the judge does not do so, or if it is not possible, it is still permissible. And drawing lots is not necessary; rather, it is only to satisfy hearts and to remove suspicion that the judge favored someone. Otherwise, if the judge assigns shares on his own without lots, he may do so, because the judge has the authority of compulsion and this is an act of judgment. And if there is a divider (qasim), he too is the judge's representative and may assign shares.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the Hidayah expands on a ruling from Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It states that when partitioning an estate that includes a right of way (tareeq) and irrigation (shurb), it is preferred (afdaliyyah) to separate that share with those rights intact. However, if the judge does not do so, or if it is practically impossible, the partition is still valid. The text also clarifies that drawing lots (qur'ah) is not an obligation; it is merely a procedural tool to reassure the parties and remove any suspicion of bias. The judge has binding authority (wilayat al-ilzam) and can assign shares without lots. Similarly, an appointed divider (qasim) acts as the judge's deputy and may also assign shares. The ruling is straightforward: the separation of ancillary rights and the use of lots are praiseworthy but not mandatory.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division or partition of jointly owned property among co-owners.
قرعہ (qur'ah): Casting lots to assign shares of property in a partition.
شرب (shurb): Right to water, typically for irrigation of land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Obligatory
B) Recommended but not required
C) Forbidden
D) Required only if the judge is biased

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partition, separating a share with its ancillary rights is preferable, not obligatory, and drawing lots is a discretionary tool, not a legal requirement.

Rights of Way in Division (Qasmah): When Missing Easements Invalidate the Partition
Ruling on easement rights in division when not mentioned, compared to sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a division (qasmah) is invalid if a necessary easement cannot be provided, and distinguish between cases where redirection is possible versus impossible.

Core Idea
Division requires complete independence; a missing easement either forces redirection or undoes the partition.

Imagine you and your sibling inherit a house with a shared courtyard. After division, one of you needs to cross the other's part to reach the street. The Hanafi school has a clear rule: if the path can be rerouted within your own share, you must do so. If not, the division itself is invalid and must be redone. This lesson unpacks that rule from Al-Hidayah, explaining the conditions and remedies for missing easements in property division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Property Division Scenario
Recognize that the parties have divided joint property and one party has an easement (path or water channel) that passes through another party's share without being stipulated in the division agreement.
The division is assumed to have been performed by a judge (qadi) or mutual agreement.
2
Assess Whether the Easement Can Be Redirected
Determine if the party who needs the easement can relocate it within their own share without causing harm to themselves or others. This is a factual inquiry: is there space, feasibility, or alternative access?
If redirection is possible, the party must do so.
3
Apply the Ruling Based on Redirection Possibility
If redirection is possible: it is obligatory (wajib) to redirect the easement to the owner's own share, and the division remains valid (sahih). If redirection is not possible: the division is invalid (fasid) because the purpose of division (complete separation of shares) is not achieved.
Invalid division means it must be annulled and a new division performed.
4
Consider the Effect of Explicitly Mentioning Rights
If the division agreement explicitly mentions that the easement rights are transferred with the share, the rule remains the same: redirection is still required if possible. Only if the parties explicitly condition that the easement will remain as before the division does it stay. This is because the purpose of division overrides a general mention of rights.
The explicit condition to keep the easement is valid and preserves the division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

منفعت کی تکمیل کے لئے ہے اور یہ منفعت تام نہیں ہوگی مگر راستہ کے ساتھ۔ تشریح: قاضی نے شرکاء کے درمیان بٹوارہ کر دیا اور راستہ اور مسیل کا کوئی تذکرہ بوقت قسمت نہیں ہوا اور حال یہ ہے کہ ایک دوسرے کے حصہ میں کو گذرتا ہے اور اس کے حصہ میں اپنی نالی بہاتا تو اب کیا ہوگا؟ تو فرمایا کہ اب دو صورتیں ہیں: ا۔ اگر وہ اپنا راستہ اور نالی اپنے حصہ میں کر سکتا ہے تو پھر کرنا ضروری ہے۔ ۲۔ اور اگر نہیں کر سکتا
