ہے اور قسمت کا اور ہے۔ اس صورت میں قسمت کو فسخ کیا گیا ہے، قسمت کی منفعت کے مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور بیع کو برقرار رکھا جائے گا اس کے مقصود کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے، اس لئے کہ بیع کا مقصود مبیع کا مالک ہونا ہے اور یہاں تو انتفاع مختل ہی ہے۔ اگر انتفاع فی الحال محذوف بھی ہو جائے تب بھی تملیک عین حاصل ہے اس وجہ سے بیع فسخ نہ ہوگی۔ ولو ذكر الحقوق فى الوجه الأول فكذلك الجواب لان معنى القسمة الافراز والتمييز وتمام ذلك بان لا يبقى لكل واحد تعلق بنصيب الآخر وقد امكن تحقيقه بصرف الطريق والمسيل الى غيره من غير ضرر فيصار اليه بخلاف البيع اذا ذكر فيه الحقوق حيث يدخل فيه ما كان له من الطريق والمسيل لانه امكن تحقيق معنى البيع وهو التمليك مع بقاء هذا التعلق بملك غيره. ترجمہ: اور اگر پہلی صورت میں حقوق کا ذکر کیا گیا ہو تو ایسے ہی جواب ہے اس لئے کہ قسمت کے معنی افراز اور تمیز ہے اور افراز کی تمامیت یہ ہے کہ کسی دوسرے کے حصہ کے ساتھ کچھ تعلق باقی نہ رہے اور اس کا اثبات ممکن ہے راستہ اور مسیل کو پھیرنے کے ساتھ اس کے غیر کی جانب بغیر ضرر کے تو پھیر دیا جائے گا اس کی جانب بخلاف بیع کے جبکہ حقوق ذکر کئے گئے ہوں اس حیثیت سے کہ تقسیم میں وہ راستہ اور مسیل داخل ہوں گے جو اس کے لئے ہیں کہ بیع کے معنی کا اثبات اور وہ تملیک ہے ممکن ہے اس تعلق کے باقی رہنے کے ساتھ ساتھ اس کے غیر کی ملک کے ساتھ۔ تشریح: اور اگر راستہ اور مسیل کو پھیرنا ممکن نہ ہو اور قسمت میں حقوق کا ذکر آیا ہو کہ یہ حصہ تمہارے لئے ہے مع اس کے حقوق کے تو اب بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ راستہ اور مسیل کو پھیرنا ضروری ہوگا کیونکہ اس کے بغیر قسمت کا مقصود متحقق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر بعینہ یہی صورت بیع میں ہوئی ہو تو راستہ اور مسیل کے پھیرنے کی ضرورت نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ بیع کے معنی اب بھی متحقق ہیں۔ یہ تفصیل ذکر حقوق میں ہے اور اگر بہ قاعدہ یہ شرط ہوگئی کہ اس کا راستہ اور مسیل دوسرے کے حصہ میں رہے گی تو اس کو بدستور رکھا جائے گا۔ قال الشامی: اما لو اشترط تركهما على حالها فلا تفسخ ويكون له ذالك على ما كان قبل القسمة (رد المختار ص 167 ج 5) وفى الوجه الثانى يدخل فيها لان القسمة لتكميل المنفعة وذالك بالطريق والمسيل فيدخل عند التنصيص باعتبار وفيها معنى الافراز وذالك بانقطاع التعلق على ما ذكرنا فباعتباره لا يدخل من غير تنصيص بخلاف الاجارة حيث يدخل فيها بدون التنصيص لان كل المقصود الانتفاع وذالك لا يحصل الا بإدخال الشرب والطريق فيدخل من غير ذكر.
He said: If he divided among them and one of them has a water channel in the share of another or a path not stipulated in the division, then if it is possible to divert the path and channel from him, he does not have the right to use a path or flow water in the share of the other because it is possible to realize the meaning of division without harm. And if it is not possible, the division is annulled because the division is defective due to the continuation of mixing, so it is started anew. Unlike sale, which is not invalidated in this situation because its purpose is ownership of the substance, and that combines with the disability to benefit at present. As for division, it is for completion of benefit, and that is not achieved except with the path. Translation: Al-Quduri said: If the judge divided among them and one of them has a water channel in the other's share or a path not stipulated in the division, then if diverting the path and channel from him is possible, he does not have the right to make a path or flow water in the other's share because the meaning of division can be realized without harm. And if it is not possible, the division is annulled because it is defective due to remaining mixing, so it is restarted. Unlike sale, which is not invalid in this situation because the purpose of sale is ownership of the substance, and that ownership combines with the inability to benefit at present. However, division is for completion of benefit, and this benefit is not complete except with the path. Commentary: The judge divided among the partners, and the path and channel were not mentioned at the time of division, and the situation is that one passes through the share of another and flows his water channel in his share, so what happens now? He said there are two scenarios: 1. If he can make his path and channel in his own share, then he must do so. 2. And if he cannot, i.e., his share does not accommodate it, then the division is annulled and a new division is made, because the purpose of division, which is facilitating benefit, is not achieved. Question: In the above scenario, Amr bought and in Bakr's share there is Khalid's passage and channel, and Khalid's share does not accommodate making his own path and channel, will the sale be invalid? And if not, why? Answer: The sale will not be invalid, and the reason for the difference is that the purpose of sale is different from that of division. In this situation, division is annulled due to the lack of benefit, but the sale is upheld because its purpose remains, for the purpose of sale is ownership of the sold item, and here benefit is impaired. Even if benefit is prevented at present, ownership of the substance is still achieved, so the sale is not annulled. And if rights are mentioned in the first scenario, the answer is the same because the meaning of division is separation and distinction, and its completion is that no one retains any connection to another's share, and that can be achieved by diverting the path and channel to another without harm, so it is done. Unlike sale when rights are mentioned, where the path and channel that belong to him are included because the meaning of sale, which is ownership, can be realized while this connection to another's property remains. Translation: And if rights are mentioned in the first scenario, the answer is the same because the meaning of division is separation and distinction, and its completion is that no connection to another's share remains, and that can be realized by diverting the path and channel to another without harm, so it is diverted. Unlike sale when rights are mentioned, in that division the path and channel that belong to him are included because the meaning of sale, which is ownership, can be realized along with the continuation of this connection to another's property. Commentary: And if diverting the path and channel is not possible and rights were mentioned in the division, i.e., 'this share is for you with its rights,' then the ruling is the same: diverting the path and channel is necessary because otherwise the purpose of division is not realized. And if exactly this situation occurs in a sale, then there is no need to divert the path and channel because the meaning of sale is still realized. This detail is when rights are mentioned. And if the condition was expressly stated that his path and channel will remain in the other's share, then it is retained as it was before the division. Al-Shami said: 'But if he stipulated leaving them as they are, then it is not annulled, and he has that as before division' (Radd al-Muhtar, p. 167, vol. 5). And in the second scenario, they are included because division is for completion of benefit, and that is through the path and channel, so they are included when explicitly mentioned, considering completion. And in division there is the meaning of separation, and that is by cutting off connection as we mentioned, so based on that, they are not included without explicit mention. Unlike lease (ijarah), where they are included without explicit mention because the entire purpose is benefit, and that is not achieved except by including the right to water and path, so they are included without mention.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal distinction between division (qasmah) and sale (bay') regarding the inclusion of easement rights like pathways (tariq) and water channels (maseel). The source is a commentary on Al-Hidayah, explaining a ruling from Al-Quduri. The key principle is that division aims to separate shares completely so each owner can independently benefit from their share. If a necessary right of way or water flow is missing, the division is defective because the benefit is incomplete. In contrast, sale transfers ownership of the substance ('ayn), which is achievable even if immediate benefit is temporarily impossible. Therefore, if after a division it turns out that one party needs to cross another's share, the division is annulled unless the path can be redirected to the owner's own share. But if the same occurs in a sale, the sale remains valid. The text also covers the scenario where rights were explicitly mentioned in the division: even then, if redirection is possible, it must be done to fully separate shares. Only if the parties explicitly agreed to keep the easements as they were before division does it remain. Finally, the passage compares with lease (ijarah), where easements are automatically included without mention because the purpose is benefit, unlike division where separation is paramount.

Key Terms
قسمة (qasmah): Division of joint property into separate shares among partners.
مسيل (maseel): A water channel or drainage path used for irrigation or flow of water.
طريق (tariq): A pathway or right-of-way for passage.
تمليك العين (tamlik al-'ayn): Transfer of ownership of the physical substance/property itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when after a division, a party's necessary pathway passes through the other's share and cannot be redirected?
A) The party has the right to continue using the pathway without permission.
B) The division is annulled because the purpose of independent benefit is not achieved.
C) The party must buy the pathway from the other party.
D) The division remains valid, and the party must build a new pathway on his own share.

Key Takeaway
In division, if a necessary easement cannot be redirected, the division is invalid because its purpose—independent benefit—is defeated.

Why Sale Survives Where Division Fails: The Legal Basis for the Distinction
Ruling on easement rights in division when not mentioned, compared to sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a sale remains valid despite missing easements while a division does not, and apply this reasoning to new contracts like lease.

Core Idea
Sale transfers ownership alone; division transfers independent benefit. That single purpose difference changes the rule on missing easements.

You buy a house, but the driveway is on your neighbor's property. In Hanafi law, your purchase is still valid because you own the house, even if you can't use it immediately. But if you had inherited the house with a co-owner and divided it, the division would be defective without the driveway. Why? The answer lies in the purpose of each contract. This lesson explores the legal reasoning behind this distinction, including a comparison with lease contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Contracts: Division (Qasmah) and Sale (Bay')
Recognize that both involve transfer of rights but with different ultimate purposes. Division eliminates co-ownership to allow independent benefit; sale transfers ownership of the substance ('ayn).
Lease (ijarah) is also contrasted as its sole purpose is benefit.
2
State Each Contract's Purpose ('illa)
The passage explicitly states: 'the purpose of sale is ownership of the substance, and that combines with the disability to benefit at present. As for division, it is for completion of benefit.'
This purpose difference is the key to the legal distinction.
3
Apply to Easement Scenario
When a missing easement (path/water) prevents immediate benefit, sale is unaffected because ownership is achieved. Division is invalid because benefit is not complete.
If the easement can be redirected, division is saved; sale never needs redirection.
4
Note the Exception: Explicit Mention of Rights in Sale
If rights are explicitly mentioned in the sale contract, the easement is included. But even if not mentioned, the sale is valid without it. In division, explicit mention does not incorporate the easement; redirection is still required to achieve separation.
The division's purpose of separation overrides any general mention of rights.
5
Compare with Lease (Ijarah)
In lease, easements are automatically included without explicit mention because the entire purpose is benefit, which requires them. This contrasts with division where separation is prioritized over benefit availability.
Lease and division both aim at benefit, but division also requires separation, which can override benefit inclusion.

قال فان قسم بينهم ولأحدهم مسيل في نصيب الآخر او طريق لم يشترط في القسمة فان امكن صرف الطريق والمسيل عنه ليس له ان يستطرق ويسيل في نصيب الاخر لانه امكن تحقيق معنى القسمة من غير ضرر وان لم يمكن فسخت القسمة لأن القسمة مختلة لبقاء الاختلاط فتستانف بخلاف البيع حيث لا يفسد في هذه الصورة لان المقصود منه تملك العين وانه يجامع تعذر الانتفاع في الحال اما القسمة لتكميل المنفعة ولا يتم ذالك الا بالطريق. ترجمه: قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر قاضی نے ان کے درمیان تقسیم کر دی اور ان میں سے ایک کی مسیل ہے دوسرے کے حصہ میں یا راستہ ہے جو تقسیم میں مشروط نہیں ہوا پس اگر راستہ اور مسیل کو اس سے پھیرنا ممکن ہو تو اس کو حق نہیں کہ وہ دوسرے کے حصہ میں راستہ بنائے اور پانی بہائے اس لئے قسمت کے معنی کو ثابت کرنا بغیر ضرر کے ممکن ہے اور اگر ممکن نہ ہو تو قسمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی اس لئے قسمت مختل ہے اختلاط کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے تو شروع از سر نو ہوگا۔ بخلاف بیع کے اس حیثیت سے کہ بیع اس صورت میں فاسد نہ ہو گی اس لئے کہ بیع کا مقصود عین کا تملیک ہے اور یہ تملیک مع تعذر الانتفاع فی الحال جمع ہو جاتا ہے بہر حال قسمت منفعت کی تکمیل کے لئے ہے اور یہ منفعت تام نہیں ہوگی مگر راستہ کے ساتھ۔ تشریح: قاضی نے شرکاء کے درمیان بٹوارہ کر دیا اور راستہ اور مسیل کا کوئی تذکرہ بوقت قسمت نہیں ہوا اور حال یہ ہے کہ ایک دوسرے کے حصہ میں کو گذرتا ہے اور اس کے حصہ میں اپنی نالی بہاتا تو اب کیا ہوگا؟ تو فرمایا کہ اب دو صورتیں ہیں: ا۔ اگر وہ اپنا راستہ اور نالی اپنے حصہ میں کر سکتا ہے تو پھر کرنا ضروری ہے۔ ۲۔ اور اگر نہیں کر سکتا یعنی اس کا حصہ اس کو متحمل نہیں تو پھر قسمت کو فسخ کر کے دوبارہ تقسیم ہوگی، کیونکہ اس صورت میں قسمت کا مقصود جو تحمیل منفعت ہے حاصل نہیں ہوا۔ سوال: زیر بر امکان خریدا اور بکر کے حصہ میں خالد کی گذرگاہ اور مسیل ہے اور خالد کا حصہ اس کو متحمل نہیں ہے کہ وہ اپنے راستہ اور مسیل کو اس میں کر سکے تو کیا بیع فاسد ہوگی اور اگر نہ ہوگی تو کیوں؟ جواب: بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی، اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ بیع کا مقصود اور ہے اور قسمت کا اور ہے۔ اس صورت میں قسمت کو فسخ کیا گیا ہے، قسمت کی منفعت کے مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور بیع کو برقرار رکھا جائے گا اس کے مقصود کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے، اس لئے کہ بیع کا مقصود مبیع کا مالک ہونا ہے اور یہاں تو انتفاع مختل ہی ہے۔ اگر انتفاع فی الحال محذوف بھی ہو جائے تب بھی تملیک عین حاصل ہے اس وجہ سے بیع فسخ نہ ہوگی۔ ولو ذكر الحقوق فى الوجه الأول فكذلك الجواب لان معنى القسمة الافراز والتمييز وتمام ذلك بان لا يبقى لكل واحد تعلق بنصيب الآخر وقد امكن تحقيقه بصرف الطريق والمسيل الى غيره من غير ضرر فيصار اليه بخلاف البيع اذا ذكر فيه الحقوق حيث يدخل فيه ما كان له من الطريق والمسيل لانه امكن تحقيق معنى البيع وهو التمليك مع بقاء هذا التعلق بملك غيره. ترجمہ: اور اگر پہلی صورت میں حقوق کا ذکر کیا گیا ہو تو ایسے ہی جواب ہے اس لئے کہ قسمت کے معنی افراز اور تمیز ہے اور افراز کی تمامیت یہ ہے کہ کسی دوسرے کے حصہ کے ساتھ کچھ تعلق باقی نہ رہے اور اس کا اثبات ممکن ہے راستہ اور مسیل کو پھیرنے کے ساتھ اس کے غیر کی جانب بغیر ضرر کے تو پھیر دیا جائے گا اس کی جانب بخلاف بیع کے جبکہ حقوق ذکر کئے گئے ہوں اس حیثیت سے کہ تقسیم میں وہ راستہ اور مسیل داخل ہوں گے جو اس کے لئے ہیں کہ بیع کے معنی کا اثبات اور وہ تملیک ہے ممکن ہے اس تعلق کے باقی رہنے کے ساتھ ساتھ اس کے غیر کی ملک کے ساتھ۔ تشریح: اور اگر راستہ اور مسیل کو پھیرنا ممکن نہ ہو اور قسمت میں حقوق کا ذکر آیا ہو کہ یہ حصہ تمہارے لئے ہے مع اس کے حقوق کے تو اب بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ راستہ اور مسیل کو پھیرنا ضروری ہوگا کیونکہ اس کے بغیر قسمت کا مقصود متحقق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر بعینہ یہی صورت بیع میں ہوئی ہو تو راستہ اور مسیل کے پھیرنے کی ضرورت نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ بیع کے معنی اب بھی متحقق ہیں۔ یہ تفصیل ذکر حقوق میں ہے اور اگر بہ قاعدہ یہ شرط ہوگئی کہ اس کا راستہ اور مسیل دوسرے کے حصہ میں رہے گی تو اس کو بدستور رکھا جائے گا۔ قال الشامی: اما لو اشترط تركهما على حالها فلا تفسخ ويكون له ذالك على ما كان قبل القسمة (رد المختار ص 167 ج 5) وفى الوجه الثانى يدخل فيها لان القسمة لتكميل المنفعة وذالك بالطريق والمسيل فيدخل عند التنصيص باعتبار وفيها معنى الافراز وذالك بانقطاع التعلق على ما ذكرنا فباعتباره لا يدخل من غير تنصيص بخلاف الاجارة حيث يدخل فيها بدون التنصيص لان كل المقصود الانتفاع وذالك لا يحصل الا بإدخال الشرب والطريق فيدخل من غير ذكر.
He said: If he divided among them and one of them has a water channel in the share of another or a path not stipulated in the division, then if it is possible to divert the path and channel from him, he does not have the right to use a path or flow water in the share of the other because it is possible to realize the meaning of division without harm. And if it is not possible, the division is annulled because the division is defective due to the continuation of mixing, so it is started anew. Unlike sale, which is not invalidated in this situation because its purpose is ownership of the substance, and that combines with the disability to benefit at present. As for division, it is for completion of benefit, and that is not achieved except with the path. Translation: Al-Quduri said: If the judge divided among them and one of them has a water channel in the other's share or a path not stipulated in the division, then if diverting the path and channel from him is possible, he does not have the right to make a path or flow water in the other's share because the meaning of division can be realized without harm. And if it is not possible, the division is annulled because it is defective due to remaining mixing, so it is restarted. Unlike sale, which is not invalid in this situation because the purpose of sale is ownership of the substance, and that ownership combines with the inability to benefit at present. However, division is for completion of benefit, and this benefit is not complete except with the path. Commentary: The judge divided among the partners, and the path and channel were not mentioned at the time of division, and the situation is that one passes through the share of another and flows his water channel in his share, so what happens now? He said there are two scenarios: 1. If he can make his path and channel in his own share, then he must do so. 2. And if he cannot, i.e., his share does not accommodate it, then the division is annulled and a new division is made, because the purpose of division, which is facilitating benefit, is not achieved. Question: In the above scenario, Amr bought and in Bakr's share there is Khalid's passage and channel, and Khalid's share does not accommodate making his own path and channel, will the sale be invalid? And if not, why? Answer: The sale will not be invalid, and the reason for the difference is that the purpose of sale is different from that of division. In this situation, division is annulled due to the lack of benefit, but the sale is upheld because its purpose remains, for the purpose of sale is ownership of the sold item, and here benefit is impaired. Even if benefit is prevented at present, ownership of the substance is still achieved, so the sale is not annulled. And if rights are mentioned in the first scenario, the answer is the same because the meaning of division is separation and distinction, and its completion is that no one retains any connection to another's share, and that can be achieved by diverting the path and channel to another without harm, so it is done. Unlike sale when rights are mentioned, where the path and channel that belong to him are included because the meaning of sale, which is ownership, can be realized while this connection to another's property remains. Translation: And if rights are mentioned in the first scenario, the answer is the same because the meaning of division is separation and distinction, and its completion is that no connection to another's share remains, and that can be realized by diverting the path and channel to another without harm, so it is diverted. Unlike sale when rights are mentioned, in that division the path and channel that belong to him are included because the meaning of sale, which is ownership, can be realized along with the continuation of this connection to another's property. Commentary: And if diverting the path and channel is not possible and rights were mentioned in the division, i.e., 'this share is for you with its rights,' then the ruling is the same: diverting the path and channel is necessary because otherwise the purpose of division is not realized. And if exactly this situation occurs in a sale, then there is no need to divert the path and channel because the meaning of sale is still realized. This detail is when rights are mentioned. And if the condition was expressly stated that his path and channel will remain in the other's share, then it is retained as it was before the division. Al-Shami said: 'But if he stipulated leaving them as they are, then it is not annulled, and he has that as before division' (Radd al-Muhtar, p. 167, vol. 5). And in the second scenario, they are included because division is for completion of benefit, and that is through the path and channel, so they are included when explicitly mentioned, considering completion. And in division there is the meaning of separation, and that is by cutting off connection as we mentioned, so based on that, they are not included without explicit mention. Unlike lease (ijarah), where they are included without explicit mention because the entire purpose is benefit, and that is not achieved except by including the right to water and path, so they are included without mention.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal distinction between division (qasmah) and sale (bay') regarding the inclusion of easement rights like pathways (tariq) and water channels (maseel). The source is a commentary on Al-Hidayah, explaining a ruling from Al-Quduri. The key principle is that division aims to separate shares completely so each owner can independently benefit from their share. If a necessary right of way or water flow is missing, the division is defective because the benefit is incomplete. In contrast, sale transfers ownership of the substance ('ayn), which is achievable even if immediate benefit is temporarily impossible. Therefore, if after a division it turns out that one party needs to cross another's share, the division is annulled unless the path can be redirected to the owner's own share. But if the same occurs in a sale, the sale remains valid. The text also covers the scenario where rights were explicitly mentioned in the division: even then, if redirection is possible, it must be done to fully separate shares. Only if the parties explicitly agreed to keep the easements as they were before division does it remain. Finally, the passage compares with lease (ijarah), where easements are automatically included without mention because the purpose is benefit, unlike division where separation is paramount.

Key Terms
قسمة (qasmah): Division of joint property into separate shares among partners.
مسيل (maseel): A water channel or drainage path used for irrigation or flow of water.
طريق (tariq): A pathway or right-of-way for passage.
تمليك العين (tamlik al-'ayn): Transfer of ownership of the physical substance/property itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a sale valid even if the buyer cannot immediately benefit from the property due to a missing right-of-way?
A) Because sale is a stronger contract than division.
B) Because the purpose of sale is ownership of the substance, not immediate benefit.
C) Because the seller is obligated to provide an easement later.
D) Because the buyer can always sue for access.

Key Takeaway
Sale survives missing easements because its purpose is ownership; division fails because its purpose is complete benefit and separation.

Determining the Width of a Shared Pathway Among Co-Owners
Ruling on pathway width when co-owners dispute and condition for permissibility of variation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for setting the width and height of a disputed pathway in a partitioned property and explain the validity of mutual variation.

Core Idea
A disputed pathway is set to the door's dimensions; mutual consent allows any variation.

When co-owners partition a property, a common pathway is often left for access. Disputes may arise over its dimensions. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: the pathway is set to the width and height of the main door of the house, as that fulfills the essential need. However, if all co-owners agree, they may vary the proportions—even unequally—because mutual consent permits any partition arrangement. This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains both the default rule and the condition for its exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute
The passage begins with a scenario: co-owners disagree about the quantity (width/length) of a pathway created by partition. Recognize that this dispute triggers the default rule.
The default rule applies only when there is a dispute; if all agree, no judicial intervention needed.
2
Understand the Default Ruling
The judge sets the pathway to the width of the house door and its length (height). This is because the primary need is access, and the door is the measure that fulfills it.
The text uses 'length' to mean 'height' as clarified in the note.
3
Grasp the Proportionality Principle
The pathway is not partitioned as a separate share; each co-owner's right in the pathway remains proportional to their share in the rest of the property.
Partition (qismat) applies to the main property, not the pathway itself.
4
Recognize the Exception: Mutual Consent
If all co-owners willingly agree to allocate the pathway in unequal proportions, that is valid. This follows the general Hanafi rule that variation with consent is permissible in partition.
Example: even if both own equally, they can agree one gets 1/2 the pathway and the other 1/3.
5
Apply the Clarification on 'Length'
The note explains that 'length' in this context means height (vertical clearance). The judge looks at the height of the main gate to decide.
This prevents confusion: the pathway's vertical dimension is set by the door height, not the house length.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان اصل الدار نصفين لان القسمة على التفاضل جــائـزة بــالتـــراضـــي ترجمہ اور اگر شرکاء نے اختلاف کیا راستہ کی مقدار میں تو اس کو گھر کے دروازے کی چوڑائی اور اس کے طول کے مطابق کر دیا جائے گا اسلئے کہ حاجت اس سے پوری ہو جائے گی اور راستہ ان کے سہام کے بقدر ہو گا جیسا کہ قسمت سے پہلے تھا اس لئے کہ قسمت راستہ کے علاوہ میں ہے نہ کہ راستہ میں اگر انہوں نے شرط کی کہ راستہ ان کے درمیان تین تہائی ہوگا تو جائز ہے اگر چہ اصل گھر دوحصوں میں ہواس لئے کہ کمی بیشی کے ساتھ قسمت رضامندی کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔ تشریح شرکاء میں اختلاف ہے کہ راستہ کتنا ہو؟ تو گھر کے دروزاہ کے بقدر رکھدیا جائے گا اور ہر شریک کی زمین راستہ میں اس کے حصہ کے تناسب سے چھوڑی جائے گی ۔ اور یوں کہا جائے گا کہ ہو راہ میں راستہ کے علاوہ باقی اجزاء میں ہے نہ کہ راستہ میں ۔ تو ان کی ملکیت باقی اجزاء میں جس حساب سے ہے یہاں بھی وہی تناسب رکھا جائے گا۔ ہاں۔ اگر وہ راضی ہو کر کم و بیش کرلیں کہ زید آدھا حصہ چھوڑے اور خالد ثلث ، حالانکہ دونوں کی ملکیت برابر ہے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ کمی بیشی رضا مندی سے ہو رہی ہے اور رضامندی سے کمی بیشی قسمت میں جائز ہوتی ہے۔
تنبیہ یہاں طول سے مراد ارتفاع ہے یعنی اس میں اختلاف تھا کہ کہاں تک راستہ کو بلند کیا جائے تو اس صورت میں قاضی فیصلہ کرے گا کہ دار کے صدر گیٹ کی بلندی دیکھی جائے اور اس کے مطابق ارتفاع و بلندی کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے اور چوڑائی میں اس گیٹ کو دیکھا جائے گا ۔ (ملاحظہ ہود مختار مع الشامی ص ۱۶۷ ج ۵)
If the original house was half and half, because partition by variation is permissible with mutual consent. Translation: And if the co-owners dispute about the quantity of the pathway, then it will be set to the width of the house door and its length, because the need will be fulfilled by that. And the pathway will be according to their shares, just as it was before partition, because partition is regarding other than the pathway, not in the pathway. If they stipulated that the pathway among them will be a third each, it is permissible even if the original house is in two halves, because partition with increase and decrease is permissible with mutual consent. Explanation: The co-owners disagree about how much the pathway should be? Then it will be kept according to the house door, and each partner's land in the pathway will be left in proportion to his share. And it will be said: 'The pathway is in the remaining parts, not in the pathway.' So their ownership in the remaining parts in whatever proportion it is, the same proportion will be maintained here. Yes, if they are willing to decrease or increase, such that Zaid leaves half his share and Khalid one third even though both own equally, it is permissible because this variation is happening by mutual consent, and variation with mutual consent is permissible in partition. Note: Here 'length' means height; i.e., there was dispute about how high the pathway should be raised, then in that case the judge will decide by looking at the height of the main gate of the house and decide the height accordingly, and in width, that gate will be considered. (See Mukhtar ma'a al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 167)
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Al-Hidayah regarding the determination of a shared pathway among co-owners when they disagree. The ruling: if co-owners dispute the width and height of a compulsory pathway (created by partition), the judge sets it to the width and height of the main house door, because the need for access is fulfilled by that. The pathway itself is not partitioned among them as separate property; rather, each co-owner's right in the pathway is proportional to his share in the remaining parts of the property. The passage adds a permission: if the co-owners mutually agree to allocate the pathway in unequal proportions (e.g., one gives up half his share, another gives less), it is valid because variation by mutual consent is allowed in partition. The 'tanbih' clarifies that 'length' in this context means height (i.e., vertical clearance). This is a standard Hanafi position: the pathway is a necessary accessory to the partitioned shares, and its dimensions are determined by the dominant need (the door). The mutual agreement exception follows the principle that in voluntary partitions, any arrangement is valid as long as all parties consent.

Key Terms
راستہ (raastah): The pathway or right of way created in a partition for access to the co-owned property.
قسمت (qismat): Partition of jointly owned property into separate shares.
طول (toul): Height (vertical dimension) in the context of the pathway, as clarified by the note.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If co-owners dispute the width of a pathway created by partition, how is it determined according to the Hanafi school?
A) By the average width of the co-owners' houses.
B) By the width of the main door of the house.
C) By the largest share owner's preference.
D) By the judge's arbitrary decision.

Key Takeaway
The default width and height of a disputed pathway is set to the main house door; mutual consent allows any deviation.

Dividing a Building With Separate Floor Ownership: By Measurement or Value?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partition method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two Shaykhs on dividing floors, and state the mufta bihi position: building by value, land by measurement.

Core Idea
When floors are separately owned, building is divided by value, land by measurement – a Hanafi compromise.

The partition of a multi-story building becomes complex when co-owners hold different floors separately. Imam al-Quduri's matn states that each floor is valued and divided by value. However, this masks a deeper intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue for division by physical area (measurement), while Imam Muhammad insists on valuation due to the differing utilities of floors. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and the later juristic preference that harmonizes both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios and the ruling in the matn
Read Quduri's statement: when a lower floor has no upper, an upper has no lower, or a lower has an upper – each is valued and divided by value. Note that the matn presents Imam Muhammad's view.
The commentary illustrates three ownership patterns.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad argues that the lower floor has unique utilities (well, cellar, stable) that the upper lacks, so equality (the goal of partition) cannot be achieved without valuation.
He prioritizes functional equivalence over physical equality.
3
Analyze the two Shaykhs' proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf counter that partnership is in the measured property (madhru'), not in value, and the aim is equality in dwelling (sukna), not in auxiliary benefits. They insist on division by measurement as the original principle.
They consider the building as a location for residence, not a bundle of utilities.
4
Understand the later compromise (mufta bihi)
Later authorities like Shami and Majma' al-Anhar clarify: the building (the structure) is divided by value, but the land (the site) is divided by measurement (yards). This harmonizes both proofs.
This is the operative position for fatwa.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Take a case: Zaid owns the upper floor of a house, Umar the lower. The land area is 200 sq m. The building value is 100k. Partition: land split 100 sq m each; building compensated by value (e.g., Umar pays Zaid if lower is more valuable).
The distinction between building and land is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ اور شیخین فرماتے ہیں کہ گروں کے ذریعہ ہی قسمت اصل ہے اس لئے کہ شرکت مزروع میں ہے نہ کہ قیمت میں تو اس کی ( قسمت بالذراع) جانب رجوع کیا جائے گا جہاں تک ممکن ہو اور جس کی رعایت کی گئی ہے وہ سکنی میں برابری ہے نہ کہ منافع میں پھر شیخین نے آپس میں اختلاف کیا ہے پیمائش کے ذریعہ بنوارہ کی کیفیت میں۔
Method of division in upper floor (attic) and lower floor (basement)
He said: And when there is a lower floor with no upper floor above it, and an upper floor with no lower floor, and a lower floor with an upper floor, each one is valued separately and divided by value, and nothing else is considered.
Translation: Quduri said: And when there is a lower storey with no upper storey above it, and an upper storey with no lower storey, and such a lower storey for which there is an upper storey, then each one's value will be fixed separately and partition will be done by value, and nothing else will be considered.
Explanation: Zaid and Umar have joint ownership in the following scenarios: This is a complete house. Separate upper floor? This upper floor belongs to someone else. There is also joint ownership here. This [؟] belongs to someone else. Separate lower floor? There is also joint ownership here. That is, in the first house, Zaid and Umar are partners in the upper floor, and the lower floor belongs to someone else. In the second house, Zaid and Umar are partners in the lower floor, and the upper floor belongs to someone else. In the third house, both are jointly owned. Now both of them demanded partition from the judge, so what should the judge do?
Then Imam Muhammad said that each house should be valued separately and divided according to value. This is the statement of Imam Muhammad which the author (the compiler) is now explaining, and according to this is the fatwa. But from the apparent wording, it seems that absolutely division will be by value. But in Shami, Majma' al-Anhar etc., it is clarified that the building will be valued, and the pure land and area will be divided by yards. 'The difference is in the area, but as for the building, it is divided by value by agreement' as in al-Jawhara, Shami vol. 5 p. 167, Sakk al-Anhar vol. 2 p. 422, Majma' al-Anhar vol. 2 p. 476.
He said (may Allah be pleased with him) — Statements of the jurists: This is according to Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) said that it is divided by measurement.
Translation: The respected author said that this is according to Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said that it will be divided by measurement. Explanation: That is, according to Imam Muhammad, partition will be by value, and according to the two shaykhs, by yards.
Proof of Imam Muhammad: According to Muhammad, the lower floor is suitable for things for which the upper floor is not suitable, such as making a well of water, a cellar, a stable, or the like; thus equality is not achieved except by value.
Translation: Muhammad's proof is that the lower floor has the capacity for that which the upper floor does not, i.e., making a well of water, a cellar, a stable, etc., so equality will not be realized except with value.
Explanation: This is Imam Muhammad's proof: that in the lower floor, a well can be made, a cellar, stable etc. can be made, which cannot be made in the upper floor, and in partition equality is intended. When there is such inherent difference between them, then without value equality cannot be achieved.
Proof of the two shaykhs: And they both say that division by the yard is the original, because partnership is in the measured property, not in value, so that (division by measurement) is resorted to as much as possible. And what is observed is equality in dwelling, not in facilities. Then they differed among themselves regarding the method of division by the yard.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on how to partition a multi-story building when co-owners own different floors (e.g., one owns upper, other lower, or they co-own one floor and the other is owned by a third party). The text first quotes Quduri's matn stating that each floor is valued separately and divided by value. The commentary then explains three scenarios: (1) a lower floor without an upper, (2) an upper floor without a lower, (3) a lower with an upper. It then states that Imam Muhammad's position is to value each floor and divide by value, and this is the basis of fatwa. However, later authorities (Shami, Majma' al-Anhar) clarify that the building is valued but the land (the site) is divided by measurement (yards). The dispute: Imam Muhammad argues that the lower floor has unique uses (well, cellar, stable) not possible in the upper, so only valuation ensures equality. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf counter that partnership is in the measured property (the land and building area), not in value, and the goal is equality in dwelling (utility for living), not in auxiliary facilities. They also differed among themselves on the method of division by measurement. The passage thus gives both sides' reasoning and notes that the operative position (mufta bihi) is a combination: building by value, land by measurement. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) applied to property division.

Key Terms
سفل (sifl): Lower floor or ground floor of a building.
علو ('ulu): Upper floor or attic of a building.
قسمة بالذرع (qismah bi al-dhira'): Division by measurement (e.g., square yards or meters), i.e., physical area.
قسمة بالقيمة (qismah bi al-qimah): Division by monetary value, where the property is valued and shares adjusted monetarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core reason for Imam Muhammad's position that partition of different floors (sifl and 'ulu) should be by value rather than measurement?
A) The building is too tall to measure accurately.
B) The lower floor has unique uses (well, cellar, stable) that the upper floor lacks, so equality requires valuation.
C) The co-owners cannot agree on a measurement standard.
D) The upper floor is less valuable due to access difficulty.

Key Takeaway
When floors are separately owned, the building is partitioned by value but the land by measurement — a Hanafi compromise that respects both physical equality and functional utility.

Division of Multi-Story Buildings: Measurement vs. Value
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division of upper/lower floors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on dividing shared multi-story buildings and identify which is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When dividing joint property with unequal utility, Hanafi masters differ: measure area or value utility? The fatwa follows value.

How should co-owners divide a building when one floor is more useful than another? The Hanafi school has three positions from its founding imams. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and shows which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the context: two partners share a building with different floors, and they demand division from the Qadi.
The scenario assumes the land is jointly owned but the building has separate floors.
2
State the three positions
List the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on how to divide.
Abu Hanifa: measurement with 2:1 ratio (lower:upper). Abu Yusuf: measurement with 1:1. Muhammad: division by value.
3
Analyse each proof
Examine the evidence (dalil) for each imam. Focus on the concept of 'ta'dil' (equalization) and whether it applies to measurement or value.
Imam Muhammad's proof emphasizes the lower floor's additional utility (well, stable, etc.).
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
See how the different methods lead to different practical outcomes for the co-owners.
The practical difference: if using measurement, Abu Hanifa gives lower floor owner 2/3, upper 1/3; Abu Yusuf gives each half; Muhammad uses value assessment.
5
Determine mufta bihi
Identify which position is relied upon for fatwa and why.
The text states that Imam Muhammad's value-based division is mufta bihi.

Sharaf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 13
Book of Division
They are partners and the upper floor belongs to someone else, and in the third house both are partners. Now both of them demanded division from the Qadi, what should the Qadi do?
Imam Muhammad said: assess each house separately and divide according to value. This is the statement of Imam Muhammad which the author is about to mention, and the fatwa is upon it. However, the apparent wording here indicates that the division will be absolutely by value, but in Shami, Majma' al-Anhar etc. it is explicitly stated that the building's value will be assessed, while the pure land/area will be divided by cubits.
He (the author) said, may Allah be pleased with him:
Statements of the jurists
This is according to Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) said it is divided by measurement.
Translation: The author said: This is according to Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said that division will be by measurement.
Explanation: That is, according to Imam Muhammad, division is by value, and according to the two shaykhs, by cubits.
Imam Muhammad's proof
For Muhammad: the lower floor is suitable for what the upper floor is not suitable for, such as making it a well of water, a cellar, a stable, or other than that, so equalization cannot be achieved except by value.
Translation: Muhammad's proof is that the lower floor has capacity for what the upper floor does not, i.e., making a well for water, a basement, a stable, etc., so equality cannot be achieved except by value.
Explanation: This is Imam Muhammad's proof: in the lower floor a well can be dug, a basement, stable, etc. can be made, which cannot be done in the upper chamber. In division, equality is intended. When there is such a difference between them, then equality cannot be achieved without value.
Proof of the two shaykhs
And they say that division by cubit is the original, because partnership is in the measured thing, not in value, so one should refer to it as much as possible, and what is considered is equality in dwelling, not in amenities. Then they disagreed between themselves regarding the manner of division by cubit.
Translation: And the two shaykhs say that division by cubits is the original, because partnership is in the measured (area), not in value, so one should resort to it as much as possible, and what is taken into account is equality in residence, not in conveniences. Then they disagreed between themselves regarding the method of division by cubits.
Explanation: In the previous section, the proof Imam Muhammad gave, here the two shaykhs give the same proof: here the partnership is in land and building, not in value; the division should be of that in which the partnership exists. In terms of residence itself, both floors are equal, and the difference in comfort is not considered. In any case, division will be by measurement; on this the two shaykhs agree, but they differ on the method to be adopted.
Abu Hanifa's method
Abu Hanifa said: one cubit of the lower floor is in exchange for two cubits of the upper floor. Abu Yusuf said: one cubit for one cubit. It is said that each responded according to the custom of their time or their city's people regarding preference of lower over upper, or their equality, or sometimes preference of lower and sometimes upper. And it is said that this is a difference of meaning.
Translation: So Abu Hanifa said: one cubit of lower is equivalent to two cubits of upper. And Abu Yusuf said: one cubit for one cubit. It is said that each gave an answer according to the custom of their era or their city's people, in preferring the lower over the upper, or their equality, and sometimes preferring the lower and sometimes the upper. And it is said that this is a difference of meaning.
Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one yard of the lower floor equals two yards of the upper floor. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, each one yard equals one yard of the other. Some scholars commented: is the difference among the three imams real or a verbal difference based on different eras? Some said it is a real and meaningful difference: each gave preference based on what he deemed preponderant in light of evidence. Others said that each looked at the custom of their own time and city and issued a ruling accordingly. For example, Imam (Abu Hanifa) saw the custom of the people of Kufa: they preferred the lower over the upper, so he said one cubit for two cubits. Imam Abu Yusuf saw the customs of the people of Baghdad: they considered them equal, so he said one cubit for one cubit. Imam Muhammad saw that people's customs differ: some prefer upper, some lower, especially the difference of seasons affects it, so he considered value.
The author indicated, by his words 'preferring the lower', Imam Abu Hanifa's proof; by 'their equality', Imam Abu Yusuf's proof; and by 'preferring the lower sometimes and the upper other times', Imam Muhammad's proof.
Abu Hanifa's proof
And the basis of Abu Hanifa's statement is that the benefit of the lower floor exceeds that of the upper by double, because it remains after the upper is lost, and the benefit of the upper...
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division (qismah) of a multi-story building shared between two partners, where one partner owns the lower floor (sufl) and the other the upper floor ('ulu). The central question is whether to divide by measurement (dhirā') or by value (qimah).

The commentator begins by setting up a scenario: two partners share a building with a third floor owned by someone else. They demand division from the qadi. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) says the qadi should assess each house separately and divide by value. The author notes that the fatwa is upon this view, though the apparent wording suggests absolute division by value. However, later sources specify that only the building's value is assessed, while the land area is divided by cubits.

The text then quotes the matn: 'This is according to Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said it is divided by measurement.' The commentary explains the positions: Imam Muhammad by value, the two shaykhs by measurement.

Imam Muhammad's proof is given: the lower floor can be used for purposes not possible in the upper floor, such as digging a well, making a cellar, or a stable. Thus, equalization (ta'dil) cannot be achieved except through value. The commentary expands: since equality is the goal of division, and there is a clear difference in utility, value must be used.

The two shaykhs' proof follows: division by measurement is the original because partnership is in the measured thing (land and building area), not in value. The aim is equality in residence (suknā), not in amenities (marāfiq). They agree on the principle but differ on the method of measurement.

Imam Abu Hanifa holds that one cubit of the lower floor equals two cubits of the upper floor, based on the greater benefit and permanence of the lower floor. Imam Abu Yusuf holds equality: one cubit for one cubit. The commentator notes that some scholars attribute this difference to the customs of Kufa and Baghdad respectively, while others see it as a genuine difference in legal reasoning. Imam Muhammad, observing varying customs and seasonal effects, opts for value.

The author (Marghinani) then indicates how his phrasing in the matn points to each imam's proof: 'preferring the lower' hints at Abu Hanifa's view, 'their equality' at Abu Yusuf's, and 'preferring the lower sometimes and the upper other times' at Imam Muhammad's.

The passage concludes with a partial quote of Abu Hanifa's proof: the benefit of the lower floor exceeds that of the upper by double because it remains after the upper is lost (i.e., lower floor foundations are more durable). This reinforces his two-to-one ratio.

In summary, this passage presents a complete intra-Hanafi dispute with positions, proofs, and the mufta bihi (Imam Muhammad's view). It illustrates how the Hanafi school accommodates differences among its founding imams while ultimately settling on a relied-upon position.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
سفل (sufl): Lower floor or ground floor of a building.
علو ('ulu): Upper floor or upper chamber of a building.
ذرع (dhirā'): Cubit measurement; in this context, the measurement of area by cubits.
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value or price; in division, proportional value assigned to each share.
تعديل (ta'dil): Equalization; making shares equal in value or utility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, how should a multi-story building be divided between co-owners?
A) By measurement of cubits, with the lower floor worth twice the upper.
B) By measurement of cubits, with both floors equal.
C) By assessing the value of each floor and dividing proportionally.
D) By lottery without regard to value or measurement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when dividing property with unequal utility, the relied-upon position is to divide by value, ensuring fair compensation.

intermediate

Dispute on Dividing Upper and Lower Stories
Intra-Hanafi dispute over division ratio

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on dividing co-owned multi-story property, explain the reasons behind each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Division of co-owned stories: Abu Hanifa's 2:1 ratio, Abu Yusuf's 1:1, but fatwa follows Muhammad's market value approach.

When co-owners disagree on dividing a building with upper and lower floors, how should shares be equated? The Hanafi school has three classic views from its founding imams. This lesson explores their reasoning—based on benefit, custom, and structural rights—and shows why the later fatwa adopted Muhammad al-Shaybani's value-based method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Recognise that the issue is about the method of equating shares when dividing co-owned upper and lower floors. The three imams agree on compulsory division (qismat al-ijbar) but differ on the ratio.
2
State each imam's position
Memorise the three positions: Abu Hanifa: 1 cubit lower = 2 cubits upper. Abu Yusuf: 1:1. Muhammad: divide by market value.
The ratio refers to the linear measurement of the floor area.
3
Analyse the proofs (talil)
For each imam, extract the reasoning: Abu Hanifa emphasises greater benefit of the lower floor (persistence, building right). Abu Yusuf stresses equality in dwelling purpose and mutual non-harm. Muhammad argues that benefit varies with climate and custom, so value is the only just measure.
The underlying principle also involves the right to build on top of one's share.
4
Identify the root difference
Note that this dispute is linked to another: whether the owner of the upper floor has the right to build without the lower owner's consent. Abu Hanifa denies it; Abu Yusuf allows it if no harm. This affects the perceived benefit.
Refer to the text: 'و الخلاف في هذه المسئلة بين ابي حنيفة و بين ابي يوسف مبنى على الخلاف في مسئلة اخرى'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text explicitly states: 'wal-fatwa al-yawm 'ala qawl Muhammad' – the fatwa today is on Muhammad's view. This avoids arbitrary ratios and adapts to changing circumstances.
Muhammad's view is regarded as the most practical and just.

امام صاحب کے ہاں طریقہ کار
فقال ابو حنيفة ذراع من سفل بذراعين من علو و قال ابو يوسف ذراع بذراع قيل اجاب كل منهم على عادة اهل عصره او اهل بلده فى تفضيل السفل على العلو واستوائهما وتفصيل السفل مرة والعلو اخرى وقيل هو اختلاف معنی
ترجمہ پس ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا سفل کا ایک ذراع علو کے دو ذراع کے بدلہ میں۔ اور فرمایا ابو یوسف نے ایک ذراع ایک ذراع کے بدلے میں کہا گیا ہے کہ جواب دیا ہے ۔ ان میں سے ہر ایک نے اپنے اپنے زمانہ یا اپنے اہلِ شہر کی عادت کے مطابق علو پر شغل کو فضیلت دینے اور ان کی برابری میں اور کبھی شغل کو فضیلت دینے میں اور کبھی علم کو۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ معنوی اختلاف ہے۔ تشریح امام صاحب کے نزدیک تحتانی منزل کا ایک گز فوقانی منزل کے دو گز کے برابر ہو گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہر ایک کا ایک گز دوسرے کے ایک گز کے برابر ہوگا۔ اس پر بعض حضرات نے تبصرہ کیا ہے کہ آئمہ ثلاثہ کا یہ اختلاف حقیقی ہے یا اختلاف لفظی ہے جو غیر اعصار پر بنی ہے؟ تو بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اختلاف حقیقی اور معنوی ہے دلائل کی روشنی میں جس نے جس کو راج سمجھا اس کو ترجیح دی۔ ور بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ ہر ایک نے اپنے زمانے اور اپنے اپنے شہر والوں کی عادت دیکھی اس کے مطابق حکم بیان کر دیا ۔ مثلاً ۔
امام صاحب نے اہل کوفہ کی عادت یہ دیکھی کہ وہ تختانی کوفوقانی پر ترجیح دیتے ہیں تو انہوں نے ذرائع بذراعین فرمایا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے بغداد میں لوگوں کی عادات دیکھی کہ ان دونوں میں مساوات و برابری سمجھتے ہیں تو انہوں نے ذراع بذراع فرمایا۔ اور امام محمدؐ نے دیکھا کہ اس میں لوگوں کی عادت مختلف ہیں، کچھ لوگ فوقانی کو ترجیح دیتے ہیں اور کچھ لوگ تحتانی کو ترجیح دیتے ہیں خصوصا اختلاف موسم کا اس میں کافی دخل ہے لہذا انہوں نے قیمت کا اعتبار کیا۔
مصنف نے فی تفضیل السفل سے امام صاحب کی دلیل کی جانب اور استوائھما سے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کی جانب وتفضیل اسفل مرةً وَالعُلو اخری سے امام محمد کی دلیل کی جانب اشارہ کیا ہے۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل
ووجه قول ابي حنيفة ان منفعة السفل تربو على منفعة العلو بضعفه لانها تبقى بعد فوات العلو ومنفعة العلو لا تبقى بعد فناء السفل وكذا السفل فيه منفعه البناء والسكنى وفى العلو السكني لا غير إذ لا يمكنه البناء على علوه الأبرضاء صاح السفل فيعتبر ذراعان منه بذراع من السفل
ترجمہ اور ابو حنیفہ کے قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مغل کی منفعت علو کی منفعت پر دوگنی بڑھی ہوئی ہے اسلئے کہ مغل کی منفعت علو کے فوات کے بعد باقی رہتی ہے اور علو کی منفعت نسل کے فتاء ہونے کے بعد باقی نہیں رہتی ۔ اور ایسے ہی سفل اس میں بناء اور سکنی کی منفعت ہے اور علوم میں سکنی ہے نہ کہ غیر اس لئے کہ اس کو اپنے علو پرتعمیر مکن نہیں، مگر صاحب مغل کی رضا مندی سے تو اعتبار کیا جائے گا علو کے دوگروں کا سفل کے ایک گز کے ساتھ ۔
تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ سنل کی منفعت علو سے دوگنی ہے لہذا اسی اعتبار سے تقسیم بھی ہو گی ۔ باقی بات ظاہر ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل .
ولابي يوسف ان المقصود اصل السكنى وهما يتساويان فيه والمنفعتان متماثلتان لان لكل واحد منهما ان يفعل ما لا يضر بالآخر على اصله
ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود اصل سکتی ہے اور وہ دونوں (سفل وعلو) سکنی میں برابر ہیں اور دونوں منفعتیں برابر ہیں اسلئے کہ ابو یوسف کی اصل کے مطابق ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو یہ حق حاصل ہے کہ وہ کام کرے جو دوسرے کو مفر نہ ہو۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے کہ مکان کا مقصود سکتی ہے اور اس میں علو و سفل دونوں مساوی ہیں اور منفعت کے اندر بھی دونوں برابر ہیں کیونکہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہر ایک کو یہ حق ہے کہ وہ اپنے حصہ میں ایسا تصرف کر سکتا ہے۔ جو دوسرے کے لئے مضر نہ ہو۔ لہذا صاحب علو کو بھی حق ہوگا کہ وہ اوپر عمارت بنائے بشر طیکہ مضر نہ ہو اور صاحب سفل کو بھی عمارت بنانے کا حق اسی وقت ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ وہ صاحب علو کیلئے مضر نہ ہو۔ گویا یہ اختلاف اس اصل کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے ہے۔
امام صاحب کے یہاں صاحب علو کو تصرف کا حق نہیں اور صاحب سفل کو ہے اسلئے انہوں نے ذرائح بذار عین فرمایا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک دونوں کو حق ہے اسلئے انہوں نے ذرائع بذراع فرمایا۔ بدائع ص ۲۷ ج سے میں ہے والخلاف في هذه المسئلة بين ابي حنيفة و بين ابى ويوسف مبنى على الخلاف في مسئلة اخرى وهى الصاحب العلو ليس له ان يبنى على

الخ -
امام محمد کی دلیل .
ولمحمد ان المنفعة تختلف باختلاف الحر والبرد بالاضافة اليهما فلا يمكن التعديل الابالقيمة والفتوى اليوم على قول محمد وقوله لا يفتقر الى التفسير
Book of Division. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 13. Explanation: The proof that Imam Muhammad gave earlier, here Sheikhayn [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] gave the same proof: here the partnership is in land and building, not in value, and the division should be of that in which there is partnership. And in the essence of dwelling, both floors are equal, and there is no difference in comfort; in any case, division will be by measurement; on this Sheikhayn agree; the method to be adopted is where they differ. Imam's method: So Abu Hanifa said: one cubit of lower (floor) is equivalent to two cubits of upper (floor). And Abu Yusuf said: one cubit for one cubit. It was said: each of them answered according to the custom of their time or the people of their city, preferring the lower over the upper, or treating them equally, or preferring the lower sometimes and the upper other times. And it was said: this is a real difference. Translation: So Abu Hanifa said: one cubit of lower equals two cubits of upper. And Abu Yusuf said: one cubit for one cubit. It is said that each answered according to the custom of his time or his city's people, in preferring the lower over the upper, or their equality, or sometimes preferring the lower and sometimes the upper. And it is said that this is a real difference. Explanation: According to Imam, one yard of the lower floor equals two yards of the upper floor. And according to Abu Yusuf, each one yard equals the other one yard. Some commentators have observed: Is this difference among the three imams real or verbal, based on different eras? Some said it is real and substantive; each gave preference to what he considered stronger in light of evidence. Others said that each looked at the custom of his time and his city and gave a ruling accordingly. For example, Imam saw that the people of Kufa preferred the lower over the upper, so he said one cubit for two cubits. Abu Yusuf saw that in Baghdad people considered them equal, so he said one cubit for one cubit. Imam Muhammad saw that customs vary; some prefer the upper, some the lower, especially with seasonal differences; so he considered market value. The author indicated Imam's proof by 'preferring lower', Abu Yusuf's proof by 'their equality', and Muhammad's proof by 'preferring lower sometimes and upper sometimes'. Imam's proof: And the proof of Abu Hanifa's statement: The benefit of the lower exceeds that of the upper by double, because it remains after the upper perishes, and the benefit of the upper does not remain after the lower is destroyed. Also, the lower has the benefit of building and dwelling, while the upper has only dwelling, because one cannot build on top of it without the consent of the owner of the lower. So two cubits of upper are equivalent to one cubit of lower. Translation: And the proof of Abu Hanifa's statement is that the benefit of the lower is double that of the upper, because the lower's benefit remains after the upper perishes, and the upper's benefit does not remain after the lower is destroyed. Similarly, the lower has the benefit of building and dwelling, while the upper has only dwelling, not other, because one cannot build on top of it without the consent of the owner of the lower. So two cubits of upper will be considered equal to one cubit of lower. Explanation: This is the proof of Abu Yusuf; its summary is that the benefit of the lower is double that of the upper, so division will be accordingly. The rest is obvious. Proof of Abu Yusuf: And for Abu Yusuf: The objective is essentially dwelling, and they are equal in that, and the two benefits are similar, because each of them has the right to do whatever does not harm the other according to his principle. Translation: And Abu Yusuf's proof is that the objective is essentially dwelling, and both (lower and upper) are equal in dwelling, and the two benefits are equal, because according to Abu Yusuf's principle, each of them has the right to do what does not harm the other. Explanation: This is Abu Yusuf's proof: the purpose of a house is dwelling, and in that both upper and lower are equal, and in benefit both are equal, because according to Abu Yusuf, each has the right to make such disposition in his share that does not harm the other. Therefore, the owner of the upper also has the right to build on top of it provided it does not harm the lower, and the owner of the lower can build only if it does not harm the upper. So this difference stems from another difference: according to Imam, the owner of the upper has no right to build on top; according to Abu Yusuf, both have the right. (From Bada'i'...). Proof of Imam Muhammad: And for Muhammad: The benefit varies with heat and cold relative to them, so equalization is only possible by value. And the fatwa today is on Muhammad's statement, and his statement does not require interpretation.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of co-owned multi-story property. The three imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—differ on how to equate the shares of the lower floor (sifl) and the upper floor (uluww) when dividing by measurement. Abu Hanifa holds that one unit of lower floor equals two units of upper floor because the lower floor's benefit is greater: it can be used for dwelling and building, its utility persists even if the upper floor collapses, and it is more valuable. Abu Yusuf holds that both floors are equal in the primary purpose of dwelling and that each owner can use their share without harming the other, so one unit of each should be treated equally. Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that benefits vary with climate and custom, so no fixed ratio can be applied; thus division should be based on market value. The text also notes that this difference is rooted in another issue: whether the owner of the upper floor has the right to build on top without consent. Abu Hanifa denies that right, while Abu Yusuf grants it as long as it does not harm the lower. The fatwa today follows Muhammad's view, which avoids arbitrary ratios and adapts to varying circumstances.

Key Terms
سفل (sifl): Lower floor or ground floor of a building.
علو (uluww): Upper floor or story above the ground floor.
ذراع (dhira'): Cubit, a unit of length measurement used for dividing property.
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit, utility, or usufruct derived from property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which imam's view is followed in fatwa today regarding the division of upper and lower floors?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) All three equally

Key Takeaway
When dividing co-owned multi-story property, the operative Hanafi ruling follows Muhammad al-Shaybani's value-based method, not a fixed area ratio.

Partition of Upper and Lower Floors: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on equalizing shares in partition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on equalizing shares in partitioning floors, and identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling) with its rationale.

Core Idea
Three Hanafi imams differ on how to value floors; today, we follow Muhammad's simple valuation method.

When two people co-own a building with an upper and lower floor, how do you partition it fairly? The Hanafi school has three answers. This lesson unpacks the proofs of each Imam — Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad — and explains why the fatwa eventually settled on valuation (qimat).

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the legal problem: how to equalize shares when the building has an upper and lower part, both of which are structurally connected but independent in benefit.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says 2 cubits of upper = 1 cubit of lower. Understand his reasoning: lower floor benefit persists after upper collapses; lower has building and dwelling, upper only dwelling.
Key concept: manfa'ah (benefit) as a measure of value.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf says 1:1 ratio. His premise: both floors are for dwelling, each can use without harming the other, so benefits are equal.
He differs on the underlying principle: upper owner has right to build on his part if not harmful.
4
Examine Muhammad's position and proof
Muhammad rejects fixed ratios. Benefit varies by season and climate, so only market valuation (qimat) can achieve true equality.
This view is adopted for fatwa because it is easy and interpretation-free.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Confirm that the fatwa today is on Imam Muhammad's opinion. Understand why: it avoids arbitrary ratios and accommodates variation.
Tarjih authority: the text states 'الفتوى اليوم على قول محمد'.

امام محمد کی دلیل .
ولمحمد ان المنفعة تختلف باختلاف الحر والبرد بالاضافة اليهما فلا يمكن التعديل الابالقيمة والفتوى
اليوم على قول محمد وقوله لا يفتقر الى التفسير
ترجمہ اور محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منفعت بدل جاتی ہے گرمی اور سردی کے اختلاف سے اضافت کرتے ہوئے علو اور سفل کی جانب تو برابری ممکن نہ ہوگی مگر قیمت کے ساتھ اور فتوی آج کل محمد کے قول پر ہے اور ان کا قول محتاج تفسیر نہیں ہے۔
تشریح گرمیوں میں رات کو فوقانی عمدہ معلوم ہوتا ہے اور دو پہر میں تحتانی اور سردیوں میں رات کو تحتانی اور دن میں دو پہر میں دھوپ کی وجہ سے فوقانی۔
خلاصہ کلام .. اختلاف موسم کی وجہ سے منفعت بدل جاتی ہے تو قیمت کے بغیر برابری ممکن نہیں۔ اور امام محمد کے قول ہی پر فتوی ہے اور یہ قول آسان ہے تفسیر کا محتاج نہیں ہے۔
اور امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول تفسیر طلب ہے چونکہ ان کے نزدیک ذراع بذراعین کا اصول ہے تو جب ایک طرف علو مجرد ہو اور دوسری طرف بیت کامل ہو تو بیت کامل ۳۳ گز اور ۳/ اگر علو مجرد کے سو گز کے برابر ہوں گے کیونکہ دونوں علو۳ /۳۳۱ گز مساوی ہوں گے اور بیت کامل میں جو نیچے کے حصہ میں ۳۳۱/۳ گز ہے اس کا دو گنا کیجئے جو ۳/ ۶۶۲ گز ہوا جس کے بدلہ میں علو کا ۳/ ۶۶۲ ہو گا اور ۳/ ۳۳۱ علو کا مقابل پہلے ہو چکا ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں علو مجرد کا بدل بیت کامل اس تناسب سے ہو گا کہ اول کے سوگز ثانی کے ۳۳ گز کے مقابلے میں ہوں گے جس سے برابری نہو جائے گی۔
اور اگر سفل مجرد میں سو گز ہو تو بیت کامل کے اس کے مقابلہ میں چھیاسٹھ گز اور دو ثلث ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ دونوں کے نیچے حصہ میں ۶۶۲/۳ کا بدل ۶۶۲/۳ ہو گیا اور اوپر بیت کامل میں ۳/ ۶۶۲ باقی بچا تو سفل مجرد میں حسب قاعده مذکوره ۶۶۲/۳ کا بدل ۳۳۱/۳ ہوا لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ سفل محجرد کے سو گز بیت کامل کے چھیاسٹھ گز کا مقابل ہوگا۔
اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تغییر آسان ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک حساب ذراع بذراع سے ہے۔ لہذا ان کے نزدیک بیت کامل کے پچاس گز سفل مجرد کے سو گز کے مقابل ہوں گے اور اسی طرح بیت کامل کے پچاس گز سفل مجرد کے سو گز کے برابر ہوں گے۔ اس تفسیر کو مصنف اپنے الفاظ میں اس طرح بیان کرتے ہیں۔
امام صاحب کے قول کی تفسیر
وتفسير قول ابى حنيفة في مسألة الكتاب ان يجعل بمقابلة مائة ذراع من العلو المجرد ثلثة وثلثون وثلث ذراع من البيت الكامل لان العلو مثل نصفه السفل فثلثة وثلثون وثلث من السفل ستة وستون وثلثان من العلومعه ثلثة وثلثون وثلث ذراع من العلو فبلغت مائة ذراع تساوى مائة من العلو المجرد ويجعل بمقابلة مائة ذراع من السفل المجرد من البيت الكامل ستة وستون وثلثا ذراع لان علوه مثل نصف سفله فبلغت مائة ذراع كما ذكرنا
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے قول کی تفسیر جو قول کتاب میں مذکور ہے یہ ہے کہ علو مجرد کے سو گز کے مقابلہ میں بیت کامل کے ۳۳ گز اور ایک تہائی گز کر دیا جائے اسلئے کہ علومغل کے نصف کے مثل ہے تو سفل کے ۳۳ اور تہائی علو کے چھیاسٹھ اور دو ثلث ہوں گے اور اس کے ساتھ ( بیت کامل کے ) علو کے ۳۳ اور ٹکٹ ہے تو بیت کامل کے تمام گز سو کی تعداد کو پہنچ گئے جو مجرد کے.. اگز کے مساوی ہے اور سفل مجرد کے سو گر کے مقابلہ میں بیت کامل کے چھیاسٹھ اور دو ثلث کو کر دیئے جائیں گے۔ اسلئے کہ اس کا علو اس کے سفل کے نصف کے مثل ہے تو یہ تمام
Book of Partition. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 13. [Abu Hanifa's proof:] The lower floor's benefit is double that of the upper because the lower floor's benefit remains after the upper's demise, and the lower has the benefit of building and dwelling, while the upper has only dwelling, since he cannot build on top without the owner of the lower's consent; so two cubits of the upper are considered equal to one cubit of the lower. Commentary: This is Abu Yusuf's proof? [Error in text] Actually this is Abu Hanifa's proof.

Abu Yusuf's proof: The purpose is original dwelling, and both are equal in that; the two benefits are similar because each can do what does not harm the other, according to his principle. 

Imam Muhammad's proof: The benefit varies with heat and cold relative to them, so equality cannot be achieved except by value; and the fatwa today is on Muhammad's statement, and his statement does not require interpretation.

[Then a long explanatory section with calculations for Abu Hanifa's view and a tafsir of Abu Hanifa's statement in the text.]
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on how to equalize shares when partitioning a building that has an upper floor (uluww) and a lower floor (sufl). The core issue is the valuation of the benefit (manfa'ah) of each part. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the lower floor's benefit is double that of the upper, so the ratio of exchange is 2:1 (two cubits of upper for one cubit of lower). His reasoning: the lower floor's benefit persists even after the upper floor is destroyed, and the lower floor has the benefit of both building and dwelling, whereas the upper floor has only dwelling (since one cannot build on top without the permission of the lower owner). 

Imam Abu Yusuf argues that both floors are primarily for dwelling, and since each owner can use his share without harming the other, the benefits are equal. Thus the exchange should be cubit for cubit (ذراع بذراع). He considers that the upper owner also has the right to build on his part as long as it does not harm the lower. 

Imam Muhammad takes a different approach: the benefit varies with seasons—heat and cold affect the desirability of upper vs. lower floors. Therefore, a fixed ratio is impossible, and equality can only be achieved by valuation (قيمة) based on market price. The text explicitly states that the fatwa today is on Imam Muhammad's opinion because it is easy and does not require interpretation. 

The passage then elaborates on Abu Hanifa's method with a detailed calculation example: if an upper floor only (uluww mujarrad) is 100 cubits, it is equal to 33 1/3 cubits of a complete house (bayt kamil) because the upper is half of the lower in size? Actually the calculation is based on the principle that the upper floor is like half of the lower floor in the complete house? The explanation is complex and involves solving proportions. 

This passage is typical of the technical legal reasoning in the Hanafi school, where the difference in underlying principles (usul) leads to differences in furu' (branches). The commentary clarifies each imam's reasoning and shows how the fatwa has settled on Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
سفل (sufl): The lower floor or ground level of a building
علو (uluww): The upper floor or storey above the ground level
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit, a unit of length used for measuring land or building area
منفعت (manfa'at): Benefit, utility, or use-value of a property
بیت کامل (bayt kamil): A complete house consisting of both upper and lower floors
قیمت (qimat): Market value or monetary valuation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which imam's opinion is the basis for fatwa today regarding the partition of upper and lower floors?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) All three equally

Key Takeaway
When partitioning a building with upper and lower floors, the Hanafi school today relies on market valuation (qimat) rather than a fixed ratio.

Equating Upper and Lower Floors in Partition: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on equating different floor types during partition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on equating pure upper/lower floors with a complete house during partition and identify which position is the basis for fatwa today.

Core Idea
Partition of multi-story buildings requires valuation by price, not just area, due to changing seasonal benefits.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the partition of properties with upper and lower floors. The core problem is that the benefit of a floor varies with seasons, making pure area-based division inequitable. The three principal Hanafi imams each propose a different method of equating a pure upper floor (ʿuluww mujarrad), a pure lower floor (sufl mujarrad), and a complete house (bayt kāmil). Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances equity, simplicity, and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property types
Recognize that the dispute involves three types: a pure upper floor (علو مجرد), a pure lower floor (سفل مجرد), and a complete house (بیت کامل) containing both. Understanding these terms is essential.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
List the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the proportional equivalencies. For example, under Abu Hanifa, 100 yards of pure upper = 33 1/3 yards of complete house; under Abu Yusuf, 100 yards of either pure floor = 50 yards of complete house; under Muhammad, equality is by price, not area.
3
Analyze each imam's reasoning (talil)
Examine why each imam arrived at his position. Abu Hanifa uses an arm's length (ذراع بذراعين) principle; Abu Yusuf treats upper and lower as equal in value; Muhammad emphasizes changing benefit with seasons.
The text states Muhammad's argument that benefit changes with heat and cold, so area alone cannot guarantee fairness.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Determine the real-world difference. Under Abu Hanifa, a partner with pure upper floor gets a smaller portion of the complete house than under Abu Yusuf. Under Muhammad, a price-based valuation must be agreed upon.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and reasoning for tarjih
The text states that fatwa today is on Muhammad's view because it is simple and does not require elaborate interpretation. This reflects the later Hanafi preference for ease and avoidance of dispute.
