Translation: And Muhammad's proof is that benefit changes due to heat and cold, in relation to height and depth, so equality is not possible except with price. And fatwa today is on Muhammad's saying, and his saying does not require interpretation. Explanation: In summers, at night the upper floor is good, and at midday the lower; in winters, at night the lower, and at midday the upper due to sun. Conclusion: Benefit changes due to season, so equality without price is impossible. And fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's saying, which is easy and does not need interpretation. And Imam Abu Hanifa's saying requires interpretation because his principle is arm's length comparison. When one side is pure upper floor and the other is a complete house, then a complete house of 33 1/3 yards equals 100 yards of pure upper floor, because the two upper halves are equal? ... (detailed calculation). And according to Abu Yusuf, the change is easy because his calculation is by arm's length. Thus, 50 yards of a complete house equals 100 yards of pure upper or pure lower floor. The author expresses this interpretation in his words: The interpretation of Abu Hanifa's saying in the book's issue is that in exchange for 100 yards of pure upper floor, 33 1/3 yards of a complete house are placed, because the upper is like half of the lower. So 33 1/3 of lower becomes 66 2/3 of upper, and with 33 1/3 of upper, it totals 100 yards equal to 100 of pure upper floor. And in exchange for 100 yards of pure lower floor from a complete house, 66 2/3 yards are placed, because its upper is like half of its lower, so it totals 100 yards as we mentioned. And the remaining detail has passed earlier. And the interpretation of Abu Yusuf's saying: that in exchange for 50 yards of a complete house, 100 yards of pure lower floor or 100 yards of pure upper floor are placed, because lower and upper are equal according to him. So 50 yards of a complete house are equivalent to 100 yards: 50 of them lower, 50 of them upper. Translation: And the interpretation of Abu Yusuf's saying is that 100 yards of pure lower floor or pure upper floor are placed in exchange for 50 yards of a complete house, because lower and upper are equal in his view, so 50 yards of a complete house are placed at the level of 100 yards: 50 of them lower, 50 of them upper. The remaining details have passed.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the partition of multi-story buildings. The core issue is how to equitably divide property when one partner has a pure upper floor (علو مجرد) and another has a complete house (بیت کامل) comprising both upper and lower sections. The problem arises because the benefit of different floors changes with seasons: in summer, upper floors are preferable at night, lower during the day; in winter, the opposite. Thus, simple area-based division is unjust. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani argues that since benefit changes, equality cannot be achieved without valuation by price. His view does not require elaborate interpretation and is the basis of fatwa today. Imam Abu Hanifa, adhering to an arm's length principle, provides a detailed proportional calculation: 100 yards of pure upper floor equate to 33 1/3 yards of a complete house (because the upper half is half the lower, so the complete house's lower half's 33 1/3 yards correspond to 66 2/3 yards of upper, plus its own 33 1/3 yards upper, totaling 100 yards). Similarly, 100 yards of pure lower floor equate to 66 2/3 yards of a complete house. Imam Abu Yusuf simplifies by treating upper and lower equally: 50 yards of a complete house (25 lower + 25 upper) equal 100 yards of either pure upper or pure lower floor. The text then quotes the Arabic original from the Hidayah and provides its Urdu translation. The passage demonstrates the madhhab's internal debate on ta'dil (equitable adjustment) in partition and clarifies that the mufta bihi position is Imam Muhammad's simpler rule.

Key Terms
علو مجرد (ʿuluww mujarrad): A property consisting only of an upper floor, without any lower portion.
سفل مجرد (sufl mujarrad): A property consisting only of a ground floor, without any upper portion.
بیت کامل (bayt kāmil): A complete house that includes both an upper and lower floor.
قسمة (qisma): Partition or division of jointly owned property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which imam's view is the basis of fatwa today?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Imam al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partition of multi-floor properties, equality is achieved through price valuation (Muhammad's view), not mere area equivalence.

Testimony of Arbitrators After Partition: Acceptance in Disputes
Presents the ruling and dispute on accepting testimony of two arbitrators after partition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement among the Hanafi imams regarding the acceptance of arbitrators' testimony after partition and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Whether the arbitrators' testimony is accepted after a division dispute divides the Hanafi school between the Shaikhayn and Imam Muhammad.

Imagine a property is divided by two appointed arbitrators. Later, a partner claims he did not receive his share, but the arbitrators testify that he did. Is their testimony admissible? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a clear intra-madhhab dispute: the Shaikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) accept it, while Imam Muhammad (and al-Shafi'i) do not. The commentator clarifies the positions and indicates the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Legal Issue
Read the opening: the two arbitrators divide property among partners, then a partner disputes, claiming his share was not given. The arbitrators testify he took it. The core question: is their testimony accepted?
Note that the dispute arises after the division is complete.
2
State the Position of the Shaikhayn (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
According to the matn of al-Quduri, the testimony is absolutely accepted. The author explains this is the saying of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
Abu Yusuf had two opinions; his later view agrees with Abu Hanifa.
3
State the Opposing Position of Imam Muhammad (and al-Shafi'i)
Imam Muhammad holds that the testimony is not accepted. This was also al-Shafi'i's view, and it was Abu Yusuf's earlier opinion.
Al-Khassaf recorded both positions.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Nuance
Note that Abu Yusuf changed his view. The two shaykhs together represent the majority Hanafi position, but the school has a credible dissenting view from Imam Muhammad.
This nuance affects how a mufti weighs the evidence.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Relied-upon Position)
Al-Quduri's text did not mention any difference, implying he considered the acceptance view as standard. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah supports this, confirming that the mufta bihi is acceptance.
Thus, in practice, a qadi should accept the arbitrators' testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاسمین نے شرکاء کے درمیان تقسیم کر دی پھر شرکاء میں اختلاف ہوا کسی نے کہا کہ میرا حصہ مجھے نہیں ملا حالانکہ میرا حصہ میں فلاں کمرہ داخل ہے اور دو قاسموں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نے اپنا لے لیا ہے تو گواہی قبول کی جائے گی قال واذا اختلف المتقاسمون وشهد القاسمان قبلت شهادتهما قال رضى الله عنه هذا الذي ذكره قول ابى حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد لا تقبل وهو قول أبي يوسف ولا وبه قال الشافعي وذكر الخصاف قول محمد مع قولهما وقاسما القاضي وغيرهما سواء ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب شرکاء متقاسمین آپس میں اختلاف کریں اور دو قاسم گواہی دیں تو ان کی گواہی قبول کرلی جائے گی ۔ حضرت مصنف نے فرمایا یہ جس کو قدوری نے ذکر کیا ہے شیخین کا قول ہے اور محمد نے فرمایا گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور یہی ابو یوسف کا پہلا قول ہے اور اسی کے مطابق شافعی نے فرمایا ہے اور خصاف نے محمد کے قول کو شیخین کے قول کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے اور قاضی کی جانب سے دو قاسم اور ان کے علاوہ برابر ہیں۔ تشریح قاسمین نے شرکاء کے درمیان تقسیم کر دی اب شرکاء میں اختلاف ہوا ان میں کسی نے کہا کہ میرا حصہ مجھ تک نہیں پہنچا۔ حالانکہ میرے حصہ میں فلاں کمرہ بھی تھا اور دو قاسموں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ اس نے اپنا حصہ لے لیا ہے تو کیا ان کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ تو امام قدوری نے مطلقا فرمایا کہ قبول کی جائے گی یعنی اس میں اختلاف نقل نہیں کیا جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قدوری کے نزدیک خصاف کا قول معتبر ہے جس میں اختلاف نہ ہو نا مذکور ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ یہ مسلہ اختلافی ہے امام محمد کے نزدیک گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی اور امام شافعی کا قول بھی یہی ہے اور امام ابو یوسف کا پہلا قول بھی یہی ہے اور شیخین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ گواہی قبول کی جائے گی ۔
Translation: The two arbitrators divided among the partners, then the partners disputed – someone said 'my share has not been given to me, although my share includes such-and-such room' – and the two arbitrators testified that he had taken his share, then their testimony will be accepted. He (al-Quduri) said: 'And when the partners (mutāqāsimūn) differ and the two arbitrators testify, their testimony is accepted.' He (the author) said: 'This which he mentioned is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: It is not accepted, and it is a former saying of Abu Yusuf, and al-Shafi'i said likewise. Al-Khassaf mentioned Muhammad's saying along with their saying. And the two arbitrators appointed by the judge and others are equal.' Translation: Quduri said: And when the partner-dividers disagree among themselves and two arbitrators testify, their testimony is accepted. The author said: This which Quduri mentioned is the saying of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: Their testimony is not accepted, and this is also the first saying of Abu Yusuf, and al-Shafi'i agreed with it. Al-Khassaf mentioned Muhammad's saying along with the saying of the two shaykhs. And the two arbitrators from the side of the judge and others are equal. Explanation: The two arbitrators divided among the partners, then the partners disagreed – one of them said his share had not reached him, although his share included such-and-such room – and the two arbitrators testified that he had taken his share. Then should their testimony be accepted? Imam Quduri said absolutely that it will be accepted, meaning he did not report a difference, indicating that in his view the saying of al-Khassaf is reliable, which does not mention a difference. The author of al-Hidaya said that this issue is disputed: according to Imam Muhammad, testimony is not accepted, and Imam Shafi'i's saying is the same, and Imam Abu Yusuf's first saying is also this, and the madhhab of the two shaykhs is that testimony is accepted.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses a dispute after partition: if the two appointed arbitrators (qāsimān) have divided the property and later one partner claims he did not receive his share, but the arbitrators testify that he did, is their testimony accepted? According to the matn of al-Quduri, the testimony is absolutely accepted. However, the commentator (the author of Ashraf al-Hidaya) clarifies that this is a disputed issue. The ruling attributed to al-Quduri represents the position of the two shaykhs—Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf—who accept the testimony. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it is not accepted, and this was also a former opinion of Abu Yusuf and the view of Imam al-Shafi'i. Al-Khassaf recorded Muhammad's saying alongside the two shaykhs'. The text also notes that whether the arbitrators were appointed by the judge or by the parties themselves, the ruling is the same. The practical consequence: in a dispute, if the arbitrators testify, a qadi following the Sahibayn would accept it, while one following Muhammad or Shafi'i would reject it. The relied upon position, as indicated by al-Quduri and the later fatwa, is acceptance, aligning with the two shaykhs.

Key Terms
قاسم (qāsim): An arbitrator or divider appointed to partition jointly owned property among partners.
متقاسمون (mutāqāsimūn): The partners or co-owners among whom the property is divided.
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in a legal dispute to establish a fact.
شیخین (shaykhayn): Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, as a pair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, whose testimony is disputed in the context of partition?
A) The testimony of the partners
B) The testimony of the two arbitrators (qāsimān)
C) The testimony of witnesses to the agreement
D) The testimony of the judge

Key Takeaway
The Shaikhayn's position that arbitrators' testimony is accepted after partition is the relied-upon view, though Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i disagree.

Ruling on Opponent's Word in Claim of Satisfaction After Division
Ruling on accepting the opponent's claim with oath when one partner alleges partial taking after full satisfaction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one partner claims full satisfaction and accuses the other of taking some, and apply the principle that the denier's word with oath is accepted.

Core Idea
In claim of partial taking after full satisfaction, the opponent's word with oath is accepted.

This lesson examines a procedural ruling from Kitab al-Qismah regarding disputes after partition. The key principle is that the burden of proof lies on the claimant, and the denier's word with oath is accepted. Understanding this helps clarify the Hanafi approach to judicial evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Read the passage carefully: one partner claims he fully received his right and that the other took some of it. The other denies.
This sets up a claim of ghasb (usurpation).
2
Identify claimant and denier
The one making the accusation is the claimant (mudda'i). The one denying is the denier (munkir). Here, the opponent of the speaker is the denier.
In Hanafi law, the denier's word with oath is given precedence.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
Apply the principle 'al-munkir qawluhu ma'a yaminihi' (the denier's word with his oath is accepted). The qadi must accept the opponent's statement with oath, and the claimant must provide evidence.
The ruling is based on established usul and is part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال قد استوفيت حقى واخذت بعضه فالقول قول خصمه مع يمينه لانه يدعى عليه الغصب وهو منكر

ترجمہ اور اگر کہا اس نے کہ میں اپنا حق وصول کر چکا تھا اور تو نے اس میں سے کچھ لے لیا تو مع یمین کے اسکے خصم کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
اسلئے کہ وہ اس پر خصب کا دعویٰ کر رہا ہے اور وہ منکر ہے۔
تشریح اور منکر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے لہذا خصم کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
And if he said 'I have already received my right and you took some of it', then the word of his opponent is accepted with his oath because he is being accused of usurpation and he is denying. Translation: And if he said that I had already received my right and you took some of it, then the word of his opponent with his oath will be considered valid. Because he is accusing him of usurpation and he is the denier. Explanation: And the denier's word with oath is considered valid, therefore the opponent's word will be considered valid.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Qismah provides a ruling on a dispute after partition. One partner claims he fully received his share and the other took some of it. The other denies. The ruling: the opponent's (the accused) statement is accepted with his oath. The reason: the claimant is alleging usurpation (ghasb), and the opponent is the denier. In Hanafi law, the denier's word is given credence with oath, following the principle al-munkir qawluhu ma'a yaminihi. No evidence is required from the opponent; the burden of proof lies on the claimant. This ruling is based on established Hanafi usul and is found in the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): The opponent or adverse party in a dispute
یمین (yamin): An oath taken by a party to affirm their claim or denial
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful taking of another's property
منکر (munkir): The denier; the party who denies the claim

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The claimant's word with oath
B) The opponent's word with oath
C) Both must provide evidence
D) The case is dismissed

Key Takeaway
The denier's word with oath is accepted in claims of ghasb after division, placing the burden of proof on the claimant.

Dispute Over Share Delivery: Mutual Oaths and Rescission of Division
Ruling on mutual oaths and rescission of division when one partner claims non-delivery up to a point

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of mutual oaths (tahaluf) to a dispute over the quantity of a share in a division and state that the division is rescinded.

Core Idea
A dispute over quantity of a share in division is treated like a sale dispute: both lead to mutual oaths and rescission.

In the Hanafi school, division of jointly owned property is considered a type of exchange. When a partner claims the other did not deliver his full share and the other denies, with no evidence, the dispute is over the amount received. This passage from Al-Hidayah teaches us that the qadi must order both partners to take an oath and then rescind the division, by analogy to the rules governing sale disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
One partner claims the other delivered only up to a point and did not give the rest. No acknowledgment of receipt. The other denies.
This triggers the rules of tahaluf.
2
Recognize the absence of evidence
Neither party has proof or confession. The dispute hinges on the amount received.
Lack of evidence is a prerequisite for tahaluf.
3
Locate the legal analogy
The text states this is analogous (nazir) to a dispute over quantity in a sale contract.
Division is treated as an exchange (mu'awadah).
4
Apply the rule of tahaluf in sales
In a sale, when seller and buyer dispute quantity, both swear oaths and the sale is rescinded.
The rules of tahaluf are already established in the school.
5
Derive the ruling
Similarly here, both swear oaths (tahaluf) and the division is rescinded (faskh).
The qadi must enforce this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال اصابني إلى موضع كذا فلم يسلمه الى وسلم ولم يشهد على نفسه بالاستيفاء وكذبه شريكه تحالفا وفسخت القسمة لان الاختلاف فى مقدار ما حصل له بالقسمة فصار نظير الاختلاف في مقدار المبيع على ما ذكرنا من احكام التحالف فيما تقدم

ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے کہا کہ مجھ کوفلاں جگہ تک پہنچا تھا پس اس نے مجھے نہیں دیا اور اس نے اپنے نفس پر وصولیابی کا اقرار نہیں کیا اور اس کے شریک نے اس کی تکذیب کی تو دونوں قسم کھائیں گے اور قسمت کو نسخ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ اختلاف اس مقدار میں ہے جو اس کو ہیم سے حاصل ہوئی ہے تو یہ اس اختلاف کی نظیر ہو گئی جو بیع کی مقدار میں ہو اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم قبل میں تخالف احکام کے سلسلہ میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح یہاں مدعی نے قبضہ کا اقرارنہیں کیا بلکہ یوں کہا کہ میری جگہ وہاں تک ہے جو مجھے نہیں دی گئی اور دوسرا شریک منکر ہے اور اس کو جھٹلاتا ہے تو چونکہ یہاں اس مقدار میں اختلاف ہے جو قسمت سے حاصل ہوگی۔
تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے بائع اور مشتری مقدار مبیع میں اختلاف کریں تو باب التخالف میں ذکر کردہ حکم کے مطابق جیسے بیع میں دونوں سے قسم لے کر بیع کو فسخ کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ یہاں بھی تقسیم کو فسخ کر دیا جائے گا۔
And if he said 'He reached me to such a place but did not give to me' and he did not confess to receipt and his partner denied him, they take mutual oaths and the division is rescinded, because the dispute is over the amount he received by division, so it becomes analogous to the dispute over the amount of a sale as per the rules of mutual oaths mentioned earlier. Translation: And if he said that he had reached me to a certain place but he did not give me, and he did not acknowledge receipt, and his partner denied him, then both will take oaths and the division will be rescinded. Because the dispute is over the amount he obtained by division, so it becomes similar to the dispute over the amount of a sale according to the details we mentioned earlier in the chapter on mutual oaths. Explanation: Here the claimant did not acknowledge possession but said that my place is up to there which was not given to me, and the other partner denies and contradicts him. Since the dispute is over the amount obtained by division, it becomes like when a seller and buyer dispute over the amount of the sold item, so according to the rules in the chapter on mutual oaths, just as in a sale both take oaths and the sale is rescinded, here too the division will be rescinded.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where one partner claims that the other only delivered his share up to a certain point and did not give the rest. The partner does not acknowledge receipt. The other denies. The ruling: they perform mutual oaths (tahaluf) and the division is rescinded. The reason: the dispute is over the quantity of what was obtained by division. This is analogous to a dispute over the quantity of a sold item in a sale contract (bay'). In such a case, both parties take oaths (one swearing to his claim, the other to his denial) and the contract is voided. Similarly here, since the division is a type of exchange, the same principle applies. This ruling is based on Qiyas (analogy) to the rules of tahaluf in sales, as established in the Hidayah.

Key Terms
تحالف (tahaluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties in a dispute when each swears to their respective claim
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract or transaction

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Both take oaths and the division is rescinded
C) The division is rescinded without oaths
D) The matter is referred to a valuation expert

Key Takeaway
Dispute over quantity of a share in a division triggers mutual oaths and rescission, analogous to sale.

Ruling on Dispute Over Valuation After Division
Ruling that a claim of ghabn in valuation is not considered unless the division was by qadi's decree with excessive ghabn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a claim of ghabn after division is accepted and explain the rationale based on qiyas with sale.

Core Idea
A ghabn claim after division is ignored if mutually agreed, but accepted if decreed by a qadi and excessive.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario in property division: can a partner contest the valuation after the division is complete? The rule draws an analogy from sale, where mutual consent negates ghabn claims. An exception arises when the division was ordered by a qadi, because the qadi's act is bound by justice – if the valuation is manifestly unfair, the affected party may challenge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the claim
Recognize that the passage deals with a claim of ghabn (cheating in valuation) made after a division of jointly owned property has taken place.
2
Understand the general rule
The general rule is that if the division was done by mutual consent, a subsequent claim of ghabn is not considered (لا يلتفت إليه).
This applies regardless of whether the ghabn is minor or excessive.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The text analogizes division to sale: in a sale, ghabn is not considered because the price was fixed by mutual consent. Similarly, in division, mutual consent blocks the claim.
The illa (effective cause) is the existence of mutual consent (تراضي).
4
Identify the exception
The exception occurs when the division was executed by the qadi's decree (بقضاء القاضي) and the ghabn is excessive (فاحش). In that case, the claim is heard.
Excessive ghabn is determined by custom and scholarly estimation.
5
Analyse the rationale for the exception
The qadi is bound by justice (عدل). A manifestly unjust valuation indicates the qadi's decision deviated from justice, so the claim is admissible.
The affected party may potentially rescind the division (see Shami).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اختلفا فى التقويم لم يلتفت اليه لانه دعوى الغبن ولا معتبر به فى البيع فكذا فى القسمة لوجود التراضى الا اذا كانت القسمة بقضاء القاضى والغبن فاحش لان تصرفه مقيد بالعدل

ترجمہ اور اگر وہ دونوں قیمت لگانے میں اختلاف کریں تو اس کی جانب التفات نہیں کیا جائے گا اسلئے کہ یہ نین کا دعویٰ ہے اور اس کا بیج میں اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا تو ایسے ہی قسمت میں نہ ہو گا تراضی کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے۔ مگر جبکہ تقسیم قاضی کے فیصلہ سے ہو ۔ اور نبین فاحش ہو اسلئے کہ قاضی کا تصرف عدل کے ساتھ مقید ہے ۔ تشریح مثلا زید اور عمرو کے درمیان سو بکری مشترک تھیں اب انہوں نے بڑارہ کیا ان کی قیمت لگا کر تو زید کے حصہ میں پینتالیس اور

كتاب القسمة
عمر د کے حصہ میں پچپن بکریاں آئیں۔
اب زید کہتا ہے کہ قیمت غلط لگائی گئی تو زید کا قول مسموع نہ ہوگا اسلئے کہ وہ مقومین پر نہین کا الزام عائد کرتا ہے اور اس کا تو بیع میں بھی اعتبار نہیں ہوتا تو قسمت کے اندر بھی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ طرفین کی رضامندی سے قیمت لگائی گئی تھی۔ مثلا بیع میں شمن معلوم کے ساتھ کچھ خریدا
پھر کہتا ہے کہ اس میں نہین ہے تو اس کا دعویٰ قبول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ دونوں کی رضامندی سے ثمن مقرر ہوا ہے۔ سیه ساری تفصیل اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ خود بنوارہ کر لیں۔ اور اگر قاضی کے فیصلہ سے تقسیم ہوئی ہو اور غبن فاحش ہو۔ مثلاً ایک بکری جو ہیں روپے کا مال ہو اس کی قیمت پندرہ سو روپے لگا دی گئی ہو تو یہاں اس کا دعویٰ قبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا کام عدل سے لینا ہے اور جب غبن فاحش ظاہر ہو گیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ قاضی کا فیصلہ عدل سے ہٹا ہوا ہے لہذا اب دعوی قبول ہو گا ۔ قلت اگر تقسیم بتر اضی ہو تب بھی تعین فاحش کی صورت میں قیمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی تفصیل کیلئے ملاحظہ ہو، شامی ص ۱۶۹ ج ۵ ۔
And if they differ in valuation, it is not heeded because it is a claim of ghabn (cheating), and it is not considered in sale, so similarly in division due to the existence of mutual consent, except when the division is by qadi's decree and the ghabn is excessive, because his action is bound by justice. Translation: And if both differ in valuation, then it will not be paid attention to, because this is a claim of ghabn, and it is not considered in sale, so similarly in division due to the presence of mutual consent. Except when the division is by the qadi's decree and the ghabn is excessive, because the qadi's action is bound by justice. Explanation: For example, Zaid and Amr had 100 sheep in common. They divided by valuation, so Zaid got 45 and Amr got 55 sheep. Now Zaid says the valuation was wrong, so Zaid's statement will not be heard because he accuses the evaluators of ghabn, and that is not considered even in sale, so in division it will also not be considered because the valuation was done with mutual consent. For example, in a sale, one buys something for a known price, then says there is ghabn, his claim will not be accepted because the price was fixed by mutual consent. All this detail is when they divide among themselves. But if the division was by the qadi's decree and the ghabn is excessive—e.g., a goat worth 100 rupees was valued at 1500 rupees—then his claim will be accepted. Because the qadi's duty is to act with justice, and when excessive ghabn appears, it shows the qadi's decision deviated from justice, so the claim will be accepted. Note: If the division is by mutual consent, even in case of excessive ghabn, the division will be rescinded? For details, see Shami, vol. 5, p. 169.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage discusses a claim of ghabn (cheating in valuation) after a division. The general rule: if partners themselves agreed on the valuation, a subsequent claim of ghabn is not heard. This is because in a sale, ghabn is not considered if the price was mutually agreed; similarly here. The rationale is that mutual consent negates the claim. However, there is an exception: if the division was executed by a qadi's decree and the ghabn is excessive (fahish), then the claim is admissible. This is because the qadi is bound by justice; if his valuation is manifestly unjust, the affected party can contest it. The commentary provides an example: 100 sheep divided into 45 and 55; the one getting 45 claims ghabn. His claim is not heard because they both agreed on the valuation. But if a qadi valued a 100-rupee goat at 1500 rupees, that is excessive ghabn, and the affected party's claim is accepted, potentially leading to rescission of the division. The note at the end references Shami for a nuance: even in consensual division, excessive ghabn might allow rescission.

Key Terms
غبن (ghabn): Cheating or deception in valuation; a significant disparity between actual value and agreed price
تقویم (taqwim): Valuation or appraisal of property for the purpose of division
فاحش (fahish): Excessive or manifestly large (referring to ghabn that is beyond normal tolerance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a claim of ghabn (cheating in valuation) after division accepted?
A) Always, if the claimant swears an oath
B) Only if the division was by mutual consent and the ghabn is minor
C) Only if the division was by the qadi's decree and the ghabn is excessive
D) Never, because division is final

Key Takeaway
After a consensual division, a claim of ghabn is not entertained; it is only considered if the division was by a qadi's decree and the ghabn is excessive.

Post-Division Dispute: Evidence and Oaths
Ruling on post-division dispute over a room

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two scenarios (acknowledgment vs denial of possession) after division and state the rule for evidence and oaths.

Core Idea
After division, if possession is acknowledged, the claimant's evidence as an outsider trumps the possessor's evidence.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common post-division dispute: one partner claims a specific room fell to his share, but the other denies. The ruling pivots on whether possession of that room has been acknowledged. The text provides two distinct scenarios with different legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Post-Division Dispute
Recognize that the partners have already divided the house, and one now claims a specific room belongs to him from the division, while the other denies. The dispute is not about the division itself but about a specific item within the divided portions.
2
Classify Possession Status
Determine whether the possessor (the one currently holding the room) acknowledges that the claimant had possession at the time of division or denies it. This classification directs the ruling.
The text says 'if before acknowledging possession' vs. 'if after', but the commentary clarifies: denial of possession vs. acknowledgment.
3
Apply Ruling for Denial of Possession
If the possessor denies that the claimant ever had possession of the room, the dispute is about the division itself. Both parties take oaths (tahaluf) and the division is rescinded.
4
Apply Ruling for Acknowledged Possession
If the possessor acknowledges that at the time of division the room was in the claimant's share (i.e., the division is valid but the room is now in his hand), then the claimant must produce evidence (bayyinah) that the room is his.
5
Prefer the Outsider's Evidence
If both parties produce evidence, the claimant's evidence is taken because he is an outsider (kharj) to the possession, and the principle is that the outsider's evidence outweighs the possessor's evidence.
This is a well-known Hanafi rule: bayyinah al-kharj tarjah ala bayyinah dhi al-yad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اقتسما داراً وأصاب كل واحد طائفة فادعى احدهما بيتاً في يد الآخرانه مما اصابه بالقسمة وانكر الآخر فعليه اقامة البيئة لما قلنا وان اقام البيئة يوخذ ببيئة المدعى لانه خارج وبيئة الخارج تترجح على بينة ذى اليد وان كان قبل الاشهاد على القبض تحالفا وترادا

ترجمہ اور اگر دو شریکوں نے گھر کا بٹوارہ کیا اور ہر ایک کو ایک ایک ٹکڑا پہنچا پہیں ان میں سے ایک نے ایک بیت کا دعوی کیا جو دوسرے کے قبضہ میں ہے کہ یہ اس میں سے ہے جو تقسیم میں مجھے پہنچا تھا اور دوسرے نے انکار کیا تو اس پر اقامت بینہ ہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر دونوں نے بینہ قائم کر دی تو مدعی کا بینہ معتبر ہو گا۔ اسلئے کہ یہ خارج ( یعنی غیر قابض ہے) اور خارج کا بینہ قبضہ والے کے بینہ پر غالب ہوتا ہے۔ اگر یہ قبضہ کے اقرار سے پہلے ہو تو دونوں قسم کھا ئیں گے اور ایک دوسرے پر واپس کریں گے۔
تشریح و شریک ہیں انہوں نے گھر کا بٹوارہ کیا اورگھر کا ایک ایک حصہ دونوں کوئل گیا۔ اب ان میں سے ایک کہتا ہے کہ فلاں کمرہ بھی دو قسمت میں میرے حصہ میں آیا تھا اور دوسرا منکر ہے تو کیا حکم ہے۔
تو فرمایا کہ اس میں اب دو صورتیں ہیں۔
ا۔ قبضہ کا انکار ہے۔
قبضہ اور وصولیابی کا اعتراف ہے۔
پہلی صورت میں دونوں قسم کھائیں گے اور تقسیم مسخ کر دی جائے گی۔ دوسری صورت میں مدعی کے ذمہ اقامت بینہ ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ وقوع تقسیم کے بعد اس کے فسخ کا مدعی ہے جس کیلئے حجت درکار ہے جو اقامت بینہ ہے۔ بہر حال اگر اس نے بعینہ قائم کر دیا تو فبہا نعمت ۔ اور اگر دونوں نے بعینہ قائم کر دیا تو مدعی کا بینہ معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس گھر پر قابض نہیں۔ اور اصول یہ ہے کہ بینہ کا مقصد غیر ثابت شدہ کو
And if two partners divided a house and each got a portion, then one claimed a room in the hand of the other that it is from what he got by division, and the other denied, then upon him is to produce evidence (bayyinah) for what we said. And if he produces evidence, the claimant's evidence is taken because he is an outsider, and the outsider's evidence prevails over the possessor's evidence. And if before acknowledging possession, they take mutual oaths and return to each other. Translation: And if two partners divided a house and each got a piece, then one of them claimed a room that is in the possession of the other, that it is from what came to him in the division, and the other denied, then upon him is to produce evidence. For the reason we stated. And if both produce evidence, the claimant's evidence is considered valid because he is an outsider (i.e., not in possession), and the outsider's evidence prevails over the evidence of the possessor. If this is before acknowledging possession, they both take oaths and return to each other. Explanation: They are partners, they divided the house and each took a portion. Now one of them says 'such and such room also came to my share in the division' and the other denies. What is the ruling? So he said: there are two cases here: (1) denial of possession, (2) acknowledgment of possession. In the first case, both take oaths and the division is rescinded. In the second case, the claimant must produce evidence, because he is claiming rescission after the division, for which proof is needed, which is producing evidence. In any case, if he produces evidence, then well and good. And if both produce evidence, the claimant's evidence is considered valid because he is not in possession of that room. And the principle is that the purpose of evidence is for the unproven.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage covers a dispute over a specific room after a house division. The ruling differentiates based on whether possession has been acknowledged. If the possessor denies the claimant's possession (i.e., the room is still in the joint phase), they perform mutual oaths (tahaluf) and the division is rescinded, as earlier. However, if possession is acknowledged (i.e., the possessor admits the claimant had possession at division but now claims his right is lost?), the claimant must produce evidence. The text says: if both produce evidence, the claimant's evidence is preferred because he is an outsider (kharj) to the possession, and the principle that the outsider's evidence outweighs the possessor's. This is a known rule: bayyinah al-kharj tarjah ala bayyinah dhi al-yad (the evidence of one not in possession prevails over that of the possessor). The commentary explains there are two scenarios: denial of possession (case 1) and acknowledgment of possession (case 2). In case 1, mutual oaths and rescission. In case 2, the claimant must bring evidence; if he does, his evidence is accepted; if both bring evidence, the claimant's prevails because he is the outsider. The text cuts off but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females
خارج (kharj): An outsider; one who is not in possession of the disputed property
ذوالید (dhu al-yad): The possessor; the one who holds the property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both take oaths and the division is rescinded
B) The claimant must provide evidence; if he does, it is accepted over the possessor's evidence
C) The possessor's word is accepted with oath
D) The matter is dismissed as a frivolous claim

Key Takeaway
The key is to distinguish whether possession of the disputed item is acknowledged or denied, as the ruling flips from mutual oaths to preferring the claimant's evidence.

Ruling on Boundary Disputes After Division with Evidence
Ruling and explanation of boundaries dispute after division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios in boundary disputes after division based on evidence possession and apply the Hanafi ruling when both parties have evidence.

Core Idea
When both have evidence, each gets the part in the other's possession — the outsider's evidence prevails.

This lesson examines a judgment rule from Al-Hidayah regarding disputes over boundaries after a property division. The rule turns on which party presents evidence (bayyinah). Understanding this rule requires knowing the principle that the evidence of the non-possessor (kharij) outweighs the possessor's evidence. We will walk through the three scenarios and their underlying proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Context
Recognize that the dispute occurs after a valid division (qasmah) of jointly owned property. The division has been executed, but boundaries are contested.
The dispute is about specific parts that each party claims falls within their share.
2
State the Three Scenarios
From the text, list the three possibilities: (1) only one party has evidence, (2) neither has evidence, (3) both have evidence.
3
Analyze the Scenario Where Both Have Evidence
Focus on the ruling: each party is given the part in the possession of the other. Understand that this is based on the principle that the evidence of an outsider (non-possessor) prevails over the possessor's evidence.
The 'outsider' here is the party not in possession of the disputed part.
4
Apply the Principle
In the example: Zayd possesses room A, Khalid possesses room B. Both claim each other's room. Both have evidence. Zayd's evidence for room B (which he does not possess) is considered 'outsider' evidence and prevails over Khalid's possessor evidence, so Zayd gets room B. Similarly, Khalid gets room A.
The result is a swap of the disputed parts.
5
Contrast with Other Scenarios
Note: if only one has evidence, that party wins the specific part. If neither has evidence, both take oaths and the division is annulled.
The oaths are yamin (solemn oaths) as in sale disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا اذا اختلفا في الحدود واقاما البينة يقضى لكل واحد بالجزء الذي هو في يد صاحبه لما بينا وان قامت لاحدهما بينة قضى له وان لم تقم لواحد منهما تحالفا كما فى البيع.
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جبکہ دونوں نے حدود کے اندر اختلاف کیا ہو اور دونوں نے بینہ قائم کر دیا ہو تو فیصلہ کیا جائے گا ہر ایک کیلئے اس جزء کا جو اس کے ساتھی کے قبضہ میں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے بعینہ ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے بعینہ قائم ہوا تو اس کیلئے فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی کیلئے بینہ قائم نہ ہوا تو دونوں قسم کھائیں گے جیسا کہ بیچ میں ۔

And similarly, when they differ in boundaries and both establish evidence, judgment is given to each for the part that is in the possession of his partner, due to what we have explained. And if evidence is established for one of them, judgment is given for him. And if evidence is not established for any of them, they both take an oath, as in sale.
Translation: And similarly, when both differ in the boundaries and both have established evidence, judgment will be given to each for the part that is in the possession of his partner, due to the reason we have stated. And if evidence is established specifically for one of them, judgment will be given for him. And if evidence is not established for any of them, they both will take an oath, as in sale.
Explanation: For example, Zayd and Khalid have a jointly owned house. For ease, its layout is as follows: (diagram description). Now they have divided it, and the division occurred according to this map. The line in between is included in their boundary, and there are two rooms whose layout is shown. Zayd is in possession of one, and Khalid of the other. Now Zayd claims that the room in Khalid's possession falls within my boundary, i.e., it is mine. And Khalid claims that the room in Zayd's possession is within my boundary and is mine. Each denies the other's claim. So what will happen? It is said that there are three scenarios: 1) One of them establishes evidence for his claim, then judgment will be given in his favor. 2) If neither can establish evidence specifically, then both will be made to take an oath, and the division will be annulled. 3) If both establish evidence specifically, then the room in Zayd's possession will be given to Khalid, and the room in Khalid's possession will be given to Zayd, because the evidence of the outsider prevails over the evidence of the possessor, as mentioned previously.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains the ruling when co-owners dispute the boundaries of their respective shares after a division (qasmah). The author presents three scenarios based on the presence of evidence (bayyinah). If only one party provides evidence, that party wins the disputed part. If neither provides evidence, both take oaths (yamin) and the division is rescinded. If both provide evidence, each is given the part in the possession of the other. This last ruling is based on the principle that the evidence of the outsider (kharij) – the one not in possession – prevails over the evidence of the possessor, because the possessor's claim is weaker due to his apparent control. This principle was established earlier in the book. The example with Zayd and Khalid in a house with two rooms illustrates the application of these rules.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Clear evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females, as per Hanafi law, used to prove claims in court.
قسمة (qasmah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners, either by mutual consent or by court order, to assign each a specific share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two co-owners dispute boundaries after division and both provide evidence, what is the ruling?
A) The division is annulled and both take oaths.
B) Each is given the part in the possession of the other.
C) The one who provides stronger evidence wins the entire disputed area.
D) The judge decides based on preponderance of evidence.

Key Takeaway
When both co-owners present evidence after division, the Hanafi rule awards each the part in the other's possession, based on the principle that the outsider's evidence outweighs the possessor's.

Istihqaq After Division: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf on Partial Claims
Explaining the ruling on third-party claim to a specific part of a share after division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish three scenarios of post-division istihqaq and apply Abu Hanifa's ruling to each, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A post-division claim annuls the division only if the claimed part is an undivided share of the whole.

When a third party proves ownership of part of a divided property, does the division dissolve? The answer depends on whether the claimed part is specific (mu'ayyan) or undivided (shai'), and whether it belongs to one partner's share or the whole. This lesson unpacks the apparent disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, showing that their ikhtilaf is limited to one scenario only.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent dispute
Read the passage to see that Abu Hanifa holds the division is not annulled, while Abu Yusuf holds it is annulled. This seems contradictory.
The commentary reveals this is not the full picture.
2
Distinguish the three scenarios
The claim can be: (a) a specific part of one partner's share, (b) an undivided part of one partner's share, or (c) an undivided part of the whole property. Identify each from the text.
Each scenario has a different ruling.
3
Apply consensus vs. ikhtilaf
For (a) and (c), there is consensus: (a) no annulment, (c) annulment. Only (b) is disputed. Map the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf onto scenario (b).
The ikhtilaf is narrow.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator declares Abu Hanifa's view (with Abu Hafs) as the most correct (asahh). Thus in scenario (b), the division stands and the affected partner recovers compensation.
This is the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.

فصل قال واذا استحق بعض نصيب احدهما بعينه لم تفسخ القسمة عند ابي حنيفة ورجع بحصة ذالك في نصيب صاحبه وقال ابو يوسف تفسخ القسمة قال رضى الله عنه ذكر الاختلاف في استحقاق بعض بعينه وهكذا ذكر في الاسرار والصحيح ان الاختلاف في استحقاق بعض شائع من نصيب احدهما فاما في استحقاق بعض معين لا تفسخ القسمة بالاجماع ولو استحق بعض شائع فى الكل تفسخ بالاتفاق فهذه ثلثة اوجه ولم يذكر قول محمد و ذكر ابو سليمان مع ابي يوسف وابو حفص مع ابي حنيفة وهو الاصح
ترجمه ی فصل ہے ( استحقاق کے بیان میں ) امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا معین بعض حصہ کا مستحق نکلے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک قسمت فسخ نہ ہوگی اور وہ اپنے حصہ کے بقدر اپنے ساتھی کے حصہ میں رجوع کرے گا۔ اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ قسمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی۔ حضرت مصنف نے فرمایا کہ قدوری نے بعض معین کے اندر استحقاق میں اختلاف ذکر کیا ہے اور ایسے ہی اسرار میں مذکور ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ اختلاف ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے حصہ میں سے بعض شائع کے اندر ہے پس بہر حال بعض معین کے استحقاق میں بالا جماع قسمت فسخ نہیں کی جائے گی اور اگر ایسا بعض مستحق ثابت ہوا جو کل میں شائع ہے تو بالا تفاق قدمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی تو یہ تین صورتیں ہیں اور امام قدوری نے امام محمد کا قول ذکر نہیں کیا۔ اور قول امام محمد و ابوسلیمان نے امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے اور امام ابو حفص نے امام ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ اور یہی زیادہ صحیح ہے۔
تشریح زید اور خالد کے درمیان یہ پورا دارمشترک تھا جو مثلا تین سو گز مربع ہے۔ زید اور خالد نے بنوارہ کیا تو زید کے حصہ میں راستہ کی جانب کا حصہ آیا جو قیمتی ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال زید کے سوگز خالد کے دوسو گز کے برابر ہیں قیمت اور مالیت کے اعتبار سے۔ جس کی صورت مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔ علشان خالد

مستحق
مستحق (۱)
دونوں اپنے اپنے حصوں پر قابض ہو گئے کہ ساجد نے ، قاضی کی عدالت میں استحقاق کا دعویٰ کر دیا اور اس پر گواہ پیش کر دئیے۔ لہذا
جتنا اس کا استحقاق تھا وہ ساجد کومل گیا اب تقسیم کا کیا حکم ہوگا؟
یہاں اس کو بیان فرمایا گیا ہے۔
خلاصہ کلام اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں،
ا۔ ساجد زید کے حصہ میں صرف ایک کمرے کا دعوی کرے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ساجد نے زید کے حصہ میں ایک معین جزء میں دعویٰ
Section: He said, 'And if a specific part of the share of one of them is claimed (by a third party), then according to Abu Hanifa the division is not annulled, and he recovers the amount of that portion from the share of his partner. And Abu Yusuf said: The division is annulled.' The author (may God be pleased with him) said: 'He (al-Quduri) mentioned the difference of opinion regarding the claim of a specific part, and likewise it is mentioned in al-Asrar. But the correct view is that the difference of opinion concerns the claim of an undivided part (shai') from the share of one of them. As for the claim of a specific part (mu'ayyan), the division is not annulled by consensus. And if a part that is undivided in the whole is claimed, the division is annulled by agreement. So these are three aspects. He (al-Quduri) did not mention the statement of Muhammad. Abu Sulayman mentioned it with Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hafs with Abu Hanifa, and this is the more correct.'
Translation: This is a section concerning istihqaq (claim). Imam al-Quduri said: When a specific part of one of the two's share is claimed by a third party, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the partition is not annulled, and he recovers to the extent of his share from the share of his partner. And Abu Yusuf said that the partition will be annulled. The author (may God be pleased with him) said that al-Quduri mentioned the difference regarding the claim of a specific part, and similarly it is mentioned in al-Asrar. But the correct view is that the difference concerns an undivided part (shai') from the share of one of them. So in any case, for the claim of a specific part, the partition is not annulled by consensus. And if a part that is undivided in the whole is proven, then the partition is annulled by agreement. So these are three scenarios. Imam al-Quduri did not mention the statement of Imam Muhammad. And Abu Sulayman mentioned Imam Muhammad's statement with Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hafs with Abu Hanifa, and this is the more correct.
Explanation: For example, Zayd and Khalid jointly owned a house which is, say, 300 square yards. They divided it, and Zayd got the portion on the street side which is more valuable. Nevertheless, Zayd's 100 yards is equal to Khalid's 200 yards in value. The layout is as follows: (diagram). Both took possession of their respective shares. Then Saajid filed a claim of entitlement in the judge's court and produced witnesses. So whatever he proved entitlement to, he took it. Now what is the ruling on the division? This is explained here. Summary: There are three scenarios: 1) Saajid claims only one room in Zayd's share, meaning he claims a specific part (mu'ayyan) of Zayd's share...
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage deals with istihqaq (third-party claim of ownership) after a division (qasmah) has taken place. The author clarifies the apparent ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf by distinguishing three cases based on the nature of the claimed part. First, if the claimed part is specific (mu'ayyan) – like a particular room – then by consensus (ijma), the division is not annulled; the claimant takes that part, and the affected partner recovers its value from the other partner's share. Second, if the claimed part is an undivided share (shai') in the entire property (i.e., a fraction of the whole), then by agreement (ittifaq), the division is annulled. Third, if the claimed part is an undivided portion of one partner's share only (not the whole), then there is ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa holds the division is not annulled, while Abu Yusuf holds it is annulled. The correct view (asahh) according to the commentator is Abu Hanifa's, supported by Abu Hafs. This resolution shows the precision of Hanafi usul in reconciling apparently conflicting statements.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): A legal claim by a third party proving ownership of part of the divided property, based on evidence.
بعض معين (ba'd mu'ayyan): A specific, identifiable part of a property, e.g., a particular room or plot.
بعض شائع (ba'd shai'): An undivided, fractional share in a property, not physically demarcated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, what is the ruling when a third party proves ownership of an undivided part (shai') of one co-owner's share after division?
A) The division is annulled by consensus.
B) The division is not annulled, and the affected partner recovers from the other.
C) The division is annulled only if the claim covers the entire property.
D) The matter is left to the judge's discretion.

Key Takeaway
The ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on post-division istihqaq is limited to undivided claims on one share; the mufta bihi position maintains the division and compensates the affected partner.

Post-Division Property Claims: Three Scenarios and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining three scenarios of a third party claiming a share after division and the rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios of a third-party claim after division and state the Hanafi ruling for each, including the intra-madhhab dispute for the second scenario.

Core Idea
A claim of an unspecified share in one partner's portion provokes an intra-Hanafi dispute; the mufta bihi preserves the division with compensation.

The division of jointly owned property is meant to finalize each partner's share, but what happens when a third party later proves ownership of a part? The Hanafi school classifies such claims into three distinct scenarios, each with its own ruling. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the correct application, resolving a common textual confusion between the imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three possible claims: a specific part from one partner's share, an unspecified (shā'i') fraction from one partner's share, and an unspecified share in the whole property.
Scenario 1: mu'ayyan; Scenario 2: shā'i' min nasīb aḥadihimā; Scenario 3: shā'i' fī al-kull.
2
State the consensus rulings
For scenario 1 (specific part) and scenario 3 (unspecified in the whole), note the unanimity: division is not dissolved in scenario 1, but is dissolved in scenario 3.
Consensus (ijmā') applies to both.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement in scenario 2
Identify the positions of Abu Hanifa (with Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf on whether the division is dissolved. Abu Hanifa holds it is not dissolved; Abu Yusuf holds it is dissolved.
The text clarifies that the dispute belongs only to scenario 2, not scenario 1.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The practical consequence: if the division stands, the affected partner compensates the claimant and recovers from the other partner; if dissolved, a new division including the third party is required.
This avoids unnecessary re-division and preserves stability.

كتاب القسمة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ وهكذا ذكر في الاسرار والصحيح ان الاختلاف في استحقاق بعض شائع من نصيب احدهما فاما في استحقاق بعض معين لا تفسخ القسمة بالاجماع ولو استحق بعض شائع فى الكل تفسخ بالاتفاق فهذه ثلثة اوجه ولم يذكر قول محمد و ذكر ابو سليمان مع ابي يوسف وابو حفص مع ابي حنيفة وهو الاصح
ترجمه ی فصل ہے ( استحقاق کے بیان میں ) امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا معین بعض حصہ کا مستحق نکلے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک قسمت فسخ نہ ہوگی اور وہ اپنے حصہ کے بقدر اپنے ساتھی کے حصہ میں رجوع کرے گا۔ اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ قسمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی۔ حضرت مصنف نے فرمایا کہ قدوری نے بعض معین کے اندر استحقاق میں اختلاف ذکر کیا ہے اور ایسے ہی اسرار میں مذکور ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ اختلاف ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے حصہ میں سے بعض شائع کے اندر ہے پس بہر حال بعض معین کے استحقاق میں بالا جماع قسمت فسخ نہیں کی جائے گی اور اگر ایسا بعض مستحق ثابت ہوا جو کل میں شائع ہے تو بالا تفاق قدمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی تو یہ تین صورتیں ہیں اور امام قدوری نے امام محمد کا قول ذکر نہیں کیا۔ اور قول امام محمد و ابوسلیمان نے امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے اور امام ابو حفص نے امام ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ اور یہی زیادہ صحیح ہے۔
تشریح زید اور خالد کے درمیان یہ پورا دارمشترک تھا جو مثلا تین سو گز مربع ہے۔ زید اور خالد نے بنوارہ کیا تو زید کے حصہ میں راستہ کی جانب کا حصہ آیا جو قیمتی ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال زید کے سوگز خالد کے دوسو گز کے برابر ہیں قیمت اور مالیت کے اعتبار سے۔ جس کی صورت مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔
مستحق (۱)
مستحق (۲)
دونوں اپنے اپنے حصوں پر قابض ہو گئے کہ ساجد نے ، قاضی کی عدالت میں استحقاق کا دعویٰ کر دیا اور اس پر گواہ پیش کر دئیے۔ لہذا جتنا اس کا استحقاق تھا وہ ساجد کومل گیا اب تقسیم کا کیا حکم ہوگا؟
یہاں اس کو بیان فرمایا گیا ہے۔
خلاصہ کلام اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں،
۱۔ ساجد زید کے حصہ میں صرف ایک کمرے کا دعوی کرے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ساجد نے زید کے حصہ میں ایک معین جزء میں دعویٰ کیا ہے جس کو میں نے نقشہ مذکورہ میں مستحق (۱) سے تعبیر کیا ہے۔
۲۔ ساجد زید کے حصہ میں غیر معین جزء کا دعوی کرے یعنی کہے کہ اس میں میراثلث ہے یا ربع وغیرہ اس کو میں نے نقشہ مذکورہ میں مستحق (۲) ثلث سے تعبیر کیا ہے۔
۳۔ ساجد دعوی کرے کہ پورے دار میں سے میرا نصف ہے۔ یعنی اس کا حصہ شائع ہے زید اور خالد دونوں کے حصوں میں۔ بہر حال یہ تین صورتیں ہیں ہر ایک کا حکم جدا گانہ ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں تقسیم فسخ نہیں ہوگی ۔ جس پر سب کا اتفاق ہے۔ البتہ ساجد نے جتنا حصہ زید سے لیا ہے اس کا حساب وہ خالد سے کر کے اپنے حساب کے بقدر خالد سے واپس لے گا اور اعادہ قسمت کی حاجت نہ ہوگی۔
اور تیسری صورت میں بالا تفاق قسمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی۔ اور دوسری صورت اختلافی ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک قسمت فسخ نہ ہو گی ۔ اور قسم اول کے مثل زید خالد سے اپنے حساب کے بقدر واپس لے گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک قسمت فسخ کر دی جائے گی۔ اور امام محمد بقول اصبح امام صاحب کے ساتھ ہیں ۔ یہ ہے اصل مسئلہ اور اس میں اختلاف کی تفصیل ۔ مگر امام قدوری نے پہلی صورت ذکر کر کے اس میں وہ نقل کر دیا جو دوسری صورت میں ہے تو امام قدوری کی یہ نقل خلاف حقیقت ہے۔ اور قاضی ابو زید الد بوی متوفی ۳۰ ھ نے بھی اپنی کتاب اشارات الاسرار میں یہی غلطی کی ہے حالانکہ اختلاف صرف دوسری صورت میں ہے۔ تنبیہ صاحب ہدایہ نے اسرار کا جو حوالہ دیا ہے یہ کہو ہے جبکہ اسرار میں یہ اختلاف دوسری صورت میں مذکور ہے اسی لئے اس مسئلہ کو بیان کرتے ہوئے لفظ شائع متعدد مرتبہ استعمال ہوا ہے۔
تنبیہ - - صاحب عنایہ نے مصنف کے اعتراض پر اعتراض کیا ہے اور کہا ہے کہ شیخ کا قد وری پر اعتراض بے جا ہے کیونکہ قدوری کا قول پہلی صورت کو بیان کرنے میں نص نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان کی عبارت یوں ہے: و اذا استحق بعض نصب احدهما بعينيه توبعينيه کا تعلق اگر بعض سے جوڑا جائے تو یہ پہلی صورت کی ترجمانی ہوگی۔ جس میں اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر نصیب احد هما، سے جوڑا جائے تو اب تقدیر عبارت ایسے ہوگی : واذا استحق بعض شائع في نصيب احدهما بعینیہ ۔ تو اب یہ دوسری صورت کی ترجمانی ہوگی جس میں اختلاف ہے۔
نتائج الانفکار وغیرہ میں صاحب عنایہ کی تردید کی گئی ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ کلام قدوری اگر چہ پہلی صورت کو بیان کرنے میں نص نہیں مگر ظا ہر یہی ہے کہ وہ پہلی صورت کی ترجمانی ہے۔ لہذا شیخ کا اعتراض درست ہے۔ کیونکہ اصول یہ ہے کہ اس جیسی ترکیبوں میں قید کا تعلق مضاف سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مضاف الیہ سے۔ اور تاسیس تاکید سے اولی ہے اور صاحب عنایہ کے قول کے مطابق یہ تاکید ہوگی اور دوسری صورت میں تاسیس بہر حال صاحب عنایہ کا اعتراض غلط ہے۔
خلاصه کلام دوسری صورت اختلافی ہے۔ اب دونوں فریق اپنے اپنے دلائل پیش کریں گے۔
Chapter of Division. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 13. And likewise mentioned in al-Asrar. And the correct [view] is that the disagreement is regarding the claim of an unspecified part from the share of one of them. As for the claim of a specific part, the division is not dissolved by consensus. And if an unspecified part in the whole [property] is claimed, it is dissolved by agreement. So these are three aspects. And he did not mention the saying of Muhammad. And Abu Sulayman is mentioned with Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hafs with Abu Hanifa, and it is the most correct. Translation: This is a section concerning the claim of entitlement. Imam al-Quduri said: When a specific part of the share of one of them is found to be claimed, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the division is not dissolved, and he will revert to his partner's share to the extent of his own share. And Abu Yusuf said that the division shall be dissolved. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said that al-Quduri mentioned disagreement in the case of a specific part, and likewise mentioned in al-Asrar. But the correct [view] is that the disagreement is regarding an unspecified part from the share of one of them. So in any case, in the claim of a specific part, by consensus the division will not be dissolved. And if a part is established as claimed which is unspecified in the whole [property], then by agreement the division is dissolved. So these are three scenarios. And Imam al-Quduri did not mention the saying of Imam Muhammad. And the saying of Imam Muhammad: Abu Sulayman mentioned him with Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hafs mentioned him with Abu Hanifa, and that is more correct. Explanation: Zayd and Khalid owned a shared house, for example three hundred square yards. They divided it. Zayd got the portion near the road, which is more valuable. Nevertheless, Zayd's one hundred yards equal Khalid's two hundred yards in value and worth. The diagram is as follows. (Diagram labels: Mustahiq (1), Mustahiq (2)). Both took possession of their shares. Then Sajid (a third party) filed a claim of entitlement in the qadi's court and presented witnesses. Thus what was his entitlement went to Sajid. Now what is the ruling on the division? This is explained here. Summary: There are three scenarios: 1. Sajid claims only one room in Zayd's share, i.e., he claims a specific part in Zayd's share, expressed in the diagram as Mustahiq (1). 2. Sajid claims an unspecified part in Zayd's share, i.e., he says that he has one-third or one-quarter, etc., expressed in the diagram as Mustahiq (2), one-third. 3. Sajid claims that half of the entire house is his, i.e., his share is unspecified and spread over both Zayd's and Khalid's shares. In any case, these are three scenarios, each with a distinct ruling. In the first scenario, the division is not dissolved, on which all agree. Rather, Sajid takes the portion he claimed from Zayd, then Zayd accounts with Khalid and takes back equivalent from Khalid, and there is no need for a fresh division. In the third scenario, by agreement, the division is dissolved. The second scenario is disputed. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the division is not dissolved, and similar to the first scenario, Zayd will take back from Khalid to the extent of his account. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the division is dissolved. And Imam Muhammad, according to the more correct view, is with Imam Abu Hanifa. This is the core issue and the detail of the disagreement. However, Imam al-Quduri mentioned the first scenario and then narrated what belongs to the second scenario, so his narration is contrary to reality. And Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabbusi (d. 430 AH) also made the same mistake in his book Isharat al-Asrar, whereas the disagreement is only in the second scenario. Note: The author of al-Hidayah cited al-Asrar, but in al-Asrar the disagreement is mentioned regarding the second scenario. For this reason, when discussing this issue, the word “shai‘” (unspecified) is used multiple times. Note: The author of al-‘Inayah objected to the author's criticism and said that the Shaykh's objection to al-Quduri is misplaced because al-Quduri's statement is not explicit regarding the first scenario. For his expression is: “And when a part of the share of one of them is claimed, ‘specifically’ (bi-‘aynayhi).” If “specifically” is attached to “part” (ba‘d), then it represents the first scenario, in which there is no disagreement. If it is attached to “the share of one of them” (nasib ahadihima), then the expression is estimated as: “And when an unspecified part in the share of one of them is claimed specifically,” then it represents the second scenario, in which there is disagreement. In Nata’ij al-Afkar and other works, the author of al-‘Inayah is refuted. The summary is that although al-Quduri's statement is not explicit in describing the first scenario, the apparent meaning is that it represents the first scenario. Therefore, the Shaykh's objection is correct. Because the principle is that in such constructions, the restriction (qayd) is attached to the first noun (mudaf), not to the second (mudaf ilayh). And establishing a new meaning (ta’sis) is preferable to repetition (ta’kid). According to the author of al-‘Inayah's view, it would be repetition, whereas in the second scenario, it is establishing a new meaning. In any case, the author of al-‘Inayah's objection is wrong. Summary: The second scenario is the one in dispute. Now both parties will present their proofs.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, discusses the legal effects on a pre-existing division (qisma) when a third party (mustahiq) proves entitlement to a portion of the divided property. The passage identifies three distinct scenarios and provides the Hanafi rulings on each, highlighting a well-known intra-madhhab disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, with Imam Muhammad reportedly siding with Abu Hanifa according to the preferred view.

**The Three Scenarios:**
1. **Claim of a specific (mu‘ayyan) part from one partner's share:** For example, Sajid proves he owns one specific room that was in Zayd's share after the division. By consensus (ijma‘), the division is not dissolved. Instead, Zayd compensates Sajid for that room, and then Zayd takes an equivalent amount from Khalid's share, as the original division was based on an incorrect assumption. No fresh division is needed.
2. **Claim of an unspecified (shā‘i‘) fraction (e.g., one-third) from one partner's share:** Sajid claims an undivided share of Zayd's portion. This scenario is disputed among the Hanafi imams. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the division is not dissolved (like scenario 1), and Zayd compensates Khalid. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the division is dissolved entirely. Imam Muhammad, according to the more correct position, agrees with Abu Hanifa.
3. **Claim of an unspecified share in the whole property:** Sajid claims a half-share in the entire undivided property, which means his share permeates both Zayd's and Khalid's portions. By agreement (ittifāq), the division is dissolved entirely, and the property must be re-divided including Sajid.

The passage also clarifies a textual confusion: Imam al-Quduri's original statement seemed to place the disagreement in scenario 1, but the correct understanding is that the disagreement belongs only to scenario 2. The author of al-Hidayah notes that the word 'shā‘i‘' (unspecified) is repeatedly used to indicate the second scenario. A further debate with the author of al-‘Inayah is settled by principles of Arabic syntax: the phrase 'bi-‘aynayhi' attaches to 'ba‘d' (part), making it specific (scenario 1), not to 'nasīb' (share), which would make it unspecified (scenario 2). The principle that 'ta’sīs (establishing a new meaning) is preferable to ta’kīd (repetition)' supports the view that al-Quduri intended the first scenario.

Thus, the passage provides a complete exposition of the rulings on post-division claims, including the disputed case. The student should note that the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) on scenario 2 is the one attributed to Abu Hanifa (division not dissolved), as supported by the majority of later Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqāq): A third party proving legal ownership or entitlement to a portion of property that was already divided between partners.
شائع (shā‘i‘): An undivided, unspecified share in a property; a fraction of the whole without physical boundaries.
معين (mu‘ayyan): A physically specific and delineated part of a property, such as a particular room.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a disputed scenario where a third party proves entitlement to an unspecified fraction (e.g., one-third) of one partner's share after division, what is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) Hanafi position?
A) The division is dissolved and must be re-done entirely.
B) The division is not dissolved; the affected partner compensates the third party and recoups from the other partner.
C) The division is void ab initio (batil).
D) The division stands only if both original partners agree.

Key Takeaway
When a third party claims an unspecified share from one partner after division, the Hanafi mufta bihi holds the division remains valid with compensation, not dissolution.

The Validity of Partition When an Undivided Share is Reclaimed: Abu Yusuf vs. the Two
Abu Yusuf's and the Two's proof on partition annulment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and the Two regarding partition with a reclaimed undivided share and state the relied-upon position with its rationale.

Core Idea
Partition remains valid if the reclaimed share is confined to one portion; harm to the claimant dictates voidness.

This lesson explores an important intra-Hanafi dispute in the law of partition (qismah). When a third party reclaims an undivided share from one of the partitioned portions, do the partitioners need to redo the division? Imam Abu Yusuf argues yes, while Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad argue the partition stands. The key is whether the claimant suffers harm from scattered shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the specific scenario? Partition has occurred, then an undivided share (juz' shayi') from one portion is reclaimed by a third party. The question is whether the partition is void.
The dispute is about the effect of subsequent claim, not the initial validity.
2
State Abu Yusuf's view and proof
Abu Yusuf argues the partition is void by qiyas to the case where the undivided share is reclaimed from both portions, which is void by consensus. He reasons that ifraz is lost.
His dalil: appearance of a third partner without consent nullifies the partition.
3
State the Two's view and proof
The Two argue that ifraz remains because the claim is confined to one portion. They cite an initial example where a partition involving a third party is valid.
Their dalil: the meaning of ifraz is not nullified; they provide a counterexample showing validity.
4
Analyze the distinction
The Two distinguish based on harm: if the claim is in both portions, the claimant's share would be scattered (tafarruq al-nasib), causing harm; if in one portion, no harm, so partition stands.
The illa (effective cause) for voidness is harm to the claimant.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Two: partition remains valid, and the claimant only seeks compensation from the partner whose portion contains the reclaimed share.
This view avoids unnecessary nullification of completed transactions.

Source Text

كتاب القسمة

امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
لابي يوسف ان باستحقاق بعض شائع ظهر شریک ثالث لهما والقسمة بدون رضاه باطلة كما اذا ستحق بعض شائع فى النصيبين وهذا لان باستحقاق جزء شائع ينعدم معنى القسمة وهو الافراز لانه يوجب الرجوع بحصته صيب الاخر شائعا بخلاف المعي
ترجمہ 14 ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعض شائع کے استحقاق کی وجہ سے ان دونوں کا تیسرا شریک ظاہر ہو گیا اور اس کی رضامندی کے بغیر قسمت باطل ہے جیسا کہ دونوں حصوں میں بعض شائع کا استحقاق ثابت ہوتا ہے اور یہ اسلئے کہ جزء شائع کے استحقاق کی وجہ سے قسمت کے معنی معدوم ہو گئے اور وہ افراز ہے اسلئے کہ یہ (استحقاق جزء شائع ) واجب کرے گا رجوع کو اس کے حصہ کے بقدر دوسرے کے حصہ میں شیوع کے طریقہ پر بخلاف معین کے۔ تشریح لیکر ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر دونوں حصوں میں مستحق کا استحقاق بطریق شیوع ہوتا تو قسمت بالا جماع فسخ ہوتی کیوں؟ اسلئے کہ شریک ثالث ہے اور شریک کی رضامندی کے بغیر قسمت ہوئی تھی جو اصولاً باطل ہوتی ہے اور بالکل یہی صورت، جز ء شائع میں بھی ہے لہذا یہ قسمت بھی فسخ ہو گی۔ اب رہی یہ بات کہ مقیس اور مقیس علیہ میں کیا مناسبت ہے تو اس کو مصنف نے وهذا لان .. الخ سے بیان کیا ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ صورت مذکورہ میں زید خالد کے حصہ میں سے ربع بطریق شیوع لے گا تو قسمت کے معنی جو افراز ہے معدوم ہو گئے تو قسمت پھر کیسے برقرار رہے گی۔ اور معتق علیہ صورت میں چونکہ استحقاق جزء معین میں ہے تو زید کا رجوع بھی جزء معین میں ہوگا تو قسمت کا معنیٰ برقرار ہیں اسلئے بالا جماع قسمت فسخ نہ ہوگی۔

طرفین کی دلیل
ولهما ان معنى الافراز لا ينعدم باستحقاق جزء شائع فى نصيب احدهما ولهذا اجازت القسمة على هذا الوجه فى الابتداء بان كان النصف المقدم مشتركا بينهما وبين ثالث والنصف المؤخر بينهما لاشركة لغيرهما فيه فاقتسما على ان لاحدهما ما لهما من المقدم وربع المؤخر يجوز فكذا في الانتهاء وصار کاستحقاق شئی معین بخلاف الشائع فى النصيبين لأنه لوبقيت القسمة لتضرر الثالث بتفرق نصيبه في النصيبين اما ههنا لا ضرر بالمستحق فافترقا

ترجمہ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ افراز کے معنی ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے حصہ میں جزء شائع کے استحقاق کی وجہ سے معدوم نہیں ہوئے اور اسی وجہ سے ابتداء میں اس طریقہ پر تقسیم جائز ہے کہ نصف مقدم ان دونوں اور ثالث کے درمیان مشترک ہو اور نصف آخران دونوں کے درمیان ہو جس میں ان کے غیر کی شرکت نہ ہو تو ان دونوں نے بٹوارہ کیا اس طریقہ پر کہ جو ان دونوں کیلئے متقدم میں ہے ہے
وہ اور مؤخر کار بع ۱/۴ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کیلئے ہے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ تو ایسے ہی انتہا میں ( جائز ہوگا ) اور یہ جز معین کے استحقاق کے مثل ہو گیا۔ بخلاف اس کے جو دونوں حصوں میں شائع ہو اسلئے کہ اگر قسمت باقی رہے تو تیسرے ( مستحق) کو ضر ر ہو گا۔ اس کے حصہ کے متفرق ہو جانے کی وجہ سے دونوں حصوں میں بہر حال یہاں مستحق کا کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے تو دونوں صورتیں الگ الگ ہوگئیں ۔ تشریح یہ حضرات طرفین کی دلیل ہے، فرماتے ہیں:۔ زید اور ساجد اور خالد ایک دار میں شریک ہیں اسکے اگلے حصہ میں زید اور خالد اور ساجد تینوں کا اشتراک ہے اور پچھلے حصہ میں صرف زید اور خالد کا اشتراک ہے اس میں ساجد کا کوئی حصہ نہیں ہے۔ اب زید اور خالد بٹوارہ کرتے ہیں جن میں یہ طے پایا کہ اگلے حصہ میں سے خالد نے اپنا حصہ زید کو دے دیا اور زید کو پچھلے حصہ میں بجائے نصف کے ربع دے دیا۔ تو اب صورت یہ ہو گئی کہ نصف مقدم میں زید اور ساجد آدھے آدھے کے شریک ہو گئے اور نصف مؤخر میں خالد کا ۳/۴ اور زید کا ۱/۴ ہو گیا اور یہ تقسیم مذکور بالکل درست ہے جس میں افراز کے معنی کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے تو جب ابتداء اس طرح تقسیم ہوسکتی ہے تو اگر انتہاء میں بعینہ یہی صورت نکل کر آجائے تو وہ کیوں جائز نہ ہوگی اور یہاں کیوں افراز زائل ہو جائے گا۔ حالانکہ یہاں جب کہ زید کے حصہ میں ساجد کا استحقاق جزء شائع میں ثابت ہوا بالکل یہی صورت ہے۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ اس صورت میں قسمت کے معنی برقرار ہیں تو پھر فسخ قسمت کی ضرورت نہ ہوگی لہذا جیسے جز معین کے استحقاق کی صورت میں افراز کے معنی موجود ہیں ایسے ہی یہاں بھی موجود ہیں۔ سوال یہ صورت تو دونوں حصوں میں استحقاق کی صورت میں بھی نکل سکتی ہے تو اس کو کیوں فسح کیا گیا ہے؟ جواب یہاں فسخ قسمت کی ضرورت مستحق کو ضرر اور نقصان سے بچانے کیلئے ہے ورنہ اس کا حصہ متفرق و منتشر ہو جائے گا کچھ اول میں اور کچھ مؤخر میں ملے گا اور صورت مذکورہ میں مستحق کا کوئی نقصان نہیں ،اسلئے دونوں مسئلوں میں فرق ہو گیا۔
[Translation of Arabic quotes:]
Abu Yusuf's proof: Because by reclaiming an undivided share, a third partner appears for them, and partition without his consent is invalid, as if an undivided share was reclaimed in both shares. This is because the meaning of partition (ifraz) ceases with the reclaiming of an undivided share, as it necessitates returning his share in the other's share on an undivided basis, unlike a specific thing.

The two's proof: The meaning of ifraz is not nullified by reclaiming an undivided share in the portion of one of them. Hence partition was allowed initially in this manner: if the front half is shared among them and a third, and the back half only between them, and they partitioned such that one gets what they have in the front and a quarter of the back, it is permissible. So likewise at the end. It becomes like reclaiming a specified thing, unlike undividedness in both shares because then if partition remained, the third party would be harmed due to his share being scattered in two shares. Here there is no harm to the claimant, so they differ.
[The Urdu commentary explains and illustrates these arguments.]
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and the two (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) regarding the validity of a partition when an undivided share (juz' shayi') is reclaimed from one of the portions after partition. Abu Yusuf argues that since the partition created a third partner (the claimant) without their consent, the partition is void, analogous to the case where an undivided share is reclaimed from both shares. The two respond that the essence of partition (ifraz) remains intact because the claimant's share is only in one portion, so there is no harm to them—their share is not scattered. They support this with an initial example where partition is valid in a similar scenario. Thus, the ruling depends on whether the third partner suffers harm (tafarruq al-nasib).

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Partition or division of jointly owned property into separate shares.
افراز (ifraz): Separation or segregation of shares; the essential purpose of partition.
شائع (shayi'): Undivided share; a part that is not physically separated from the whole.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Claim or right to property; the emergence of a third party's ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling on partition when an undivided share is reclaimed from one of the portions?
A) The partition is void.
B) The partition remains valid, and the claimant can only seek compensation.
C) The partition is void, but the claimant must consent to a new one.
D) The partition stands only if the claimant agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, partition is not automatically void when an undivided share is reclaimed; it depends on whether the claim is confined to one portion, preserving the meaning of ifraz.
