Case Study: Reclaiming Half of Front Portion After Partition
Specific example of post-partition reclamation with calculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) to a case of partial reclamation after partition, identifying the options of annulment or compensation and calculating the compensation amount.

Core Idea
Partial reclamation after partition does not void it; the affected partner chooses annulment or proportional compensation.

This passage presents a concrete numerical example to illustrate the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding post-partition reclamation. Understanding this case helps you see how the defect of tashqis (splitting) is avoided by giving the affected partner a choice. The calculation demonstrates the principle of proportionality: compensation is based on the reclaimed fraction relative to the whole.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial partition
Two partners own a house. They partition so that Partner A takes the front third and Partner B takes the back two-thirds. The values are equal.
Equal values mean the front third is worth exactly one-third of the total, and the back two-thirds worth two-thirds.
2
Understand the reclamation event
After partition, a third party reclaims half of the front portion (i.e., half of Partner A’s allocated share). This means Partner A loses half of what he received.
3
Apply the two's ruling: options
According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the partition is valid but Partner A has two options: annul the entire partition (to avoid the defect of splitting, tashqis) or seek compensation from Partner B.
Abu Yusuf would void the partition automatically, but the relied-upon position is the two's.
4
Calculate the compensation amount
If the entire front was reclaimed, Partner A would claim half of what Partner B has (since front = 1/3, back = 2/3, losing front entitles A to half of B's share). Since only half is reclaimed, the compensation is half of that half, i.e., a quarter of Partner B's back portion (1/4 × 2/3 = 1/6 of the whole house).
The quarter refers to a quarter of Partner B's holding, not of the whole house.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصور
اصل صورت مسئلہ
صورة المسألة اذا اخذ احدهما الثلث المقدم من الدار والاخر الثلثين من المؤخر وقيمتهما سواء ثم استحق نصف المقدم فعندهما ان شاء نقض القسمة دفعا لعيب التشقيص وان شاء رجع على صاحبه بربع ما في يده من المؤخر لأنه لو استحق كل المقدم رجع بنصف مافى يده فاذا استحق النصف رجع بنصف النصف وهو الربع اعتباراً للجزء بالكل :

ترجمہ اور مسئلہ کی صورت ( یہ ہے ) جبکہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے دار کا ثلث مقدم لے لیا اور دوسرے نے موخر کے دو ثلث اور ان دونوں کی قیمت برابر ہے پھر مقدم کا نصف مستحق ثابت ہوا تو طرفین کے نزدیک اگر وہ (زید) چاہے تو قسمت کو توڑ دے ٹوٹن کے عیب کو دور کرنے کیلئے اور اگر چاہے اپنے ساتھی ( خالد ) پر رجوع کرے اس کے چوتھائی کے ساتھ جو اسکے قبضہ میں ہے یعنی مؤخر اسلئے کہ اگر متقدم کا کل مستحق نکلتا تو یہ رجوع کرتا اس کے نصف کے ساتھ جو اس کے ( خالد ) قبضہ میں ہے۔ پس جب کہ نصف مستحق نکلا تو نصف کے
[Arabic:] Case: If one of them takes the front third of the house and the other takes the back two-thirds, and their values are equal, then half of the front is reclaimed. So according to them, if he wishes, he can annul the partition to avoid the defect of splitting, and if he wishes, he can claim from his partner a quarter of what is in his hand from the back. Because if the entire front was reclaimed, he would claim half of what is in his hand. So if half is reclaimed, he claims half of that half, which is a quarter, considering the part as related to the whole.
[Urdu translation:] The case is that one took the front third, the other the back two-thirds, values equal. Then half of the front is reclaimed. According to the two, if he wishes, he can annul the partition to remove the defect of splitting, or if he wishes, he can claim from his partner a quarter of what he possesses from the back. Because if the whole front was reclaimed, he would claim half. Since half is reclaimed, he claims half of that half, which is a quarter.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage provides a specific application of the two's ruling. It presents a numerical case: two partners (Zayd and Khalid) own a house. They partition such that Zayd takes the front third (one-third of whole house) and Khalid takes the back two-thirds. The values are equal (so the front third is worth one-third of total, back two-thirds worth two-thirds). After partition, a claimant reclaims half of the front portion. Since the front portion was entirely assigned to Zayd, half of it is reclaimed. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the partition is not automatically void. Instead, Zayd has an option: he can either annul the entire partition (due to the defect of splitting—'aib al-tashqis) or he can seek compensation from Khalid. The compensation is calculated as follows: if the entire front was reclaimed, Zayd would be entitled to half of what Khalid has (since the front was one-third and back two-thirds; losing the front would mean Zayd gets half of back to equalize). But only half is reclaimed, so he gets half of that half, i.e., a quarter of what Khalid holds. Thus, Zayd can claim a quarter of the back portion (which is 1/4 of 2/3 = 1/6 of the whole house). This example illustrates the practical operation of the two's rule.

Key Terms
تشقيص (tashqis): The defect of splitting or fragmenting a share; a reason to annul the partition.
رجوع (ruju'): Recourse or claim for compensation from the partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where Zayd takes the front third and Khalid takes the back two-thirds, and half of the front is reclaimed, what can Zayd do?
A) He must accept the partition as is.
B) He can only claim compensation.
C) He can either annul the partition or claim a quarter of Khalid's back portion.
D) He must annul the partition.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a valid partition is not automatically nullified by a partial reclamation; the affected partner retains the option to annul or seek proportional compensation.

Sale of Portion Before Istihqaq: Effect on Right to Annul Division
Ruling on the option to annul when part of property is sold before istihqaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the khiyar (option to annul division) when a partner sells part of his share before istihqaq, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Sahibayn and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Selling part of your share before the remaining portion is claimed extinguishes your option to annul the division.

This lesson examines a variation of the qismah (partition) scenario: after division, one partner sells part of his share before the remaining portion is claimed (istihqaq). The key question is whether the partner still has the right to annul the division (khiyar naqd al-qismah). The Hanafi school has an intra-madhhab difference: Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule the option is lost, while Imam Abu Yusuf alone holds the division becomes void. We will explore the proofs, practical consequences, and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Zaid and Khalid divide a property. Zaid sells half of his front portion before the remaining half is claimed by a third party. Determine what legal rights Zaid retains.
Assume the division was valid and the sale occurred before any istihqaq.
2
State the Sahibayn ruling
According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Zaid loses the option to annul the division because he sold part of his share. He can only claim a quarter of the back portion from Khalid as compensation.
The ruling is based on protecting the buyer from harm.
3
State the Abu Yusuf ruling
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the division becomes void (fāsid) upon istihqaq. The property reverts to joint ownership half-and-half. Zaid is liable for the value of half of what he sold to his partner.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on the principle that possession under a void contract transfers ownership but with liability for value.
4
Contrast the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Sahibayn, the division stands and Zaid gets a quarter. Under Abu Yusuf, the division is annulled, shares are equal, and Zaid must compensate. The practical outcome differs significantly.
Know which view is mufta bihi in your context.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Sahibayn: the option is lost, and compensation is limited to a quarter. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
This preserves the sale and protects the buyer.

Source Text

And if the owner of the front sold half of it, then the remaining half is claimed, he shall have recourse for a quarter of what is in the hand of the other according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), for the reason we mentioned, and his option is voided by the sale of a part. Translation: And if the owner of the front sold his half, or then the remaining half is claimed, he shall have recourse for a quarter of what is in the hand of the other, according to the two, for the reason we mentioned, and his option is voided due to selling a part. Commentary: If Zaid sold half of his front portion, then the remaining half is claimed, what happens? The two (Sahibayn) said: Zaid takes a quarter of the back from Khalid and that's it; the option to annul the division that he had is now gone because he sold half. So only this one possibility remains, so that the buyer is not harmed. The view of Imam Abu Yusuf: And according to Abu Yusuf, what is in the hand of his partner is divided half and half between them, and (Zaid) is liable to his partner for the value of half of what he sold, because according to him the division becomes void, and what is taken possession of by a void contract is owned (by the taker), so the sale is effective in it, and it is liable for value, so he is liable for half of its value to his partner.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage addresses a variation of the previous case: after the division, the partner (Zaid) sells half of his front portion before the remaining half is claimed by a third party. According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Zaid's option to annul the division is lost because selling part of his share extinguishes that right. He can only claim a quarter of the back portion from Khalid as compensation—the same amount as in the previous case. The reason is to protect the buyer, who should not be harmed by a subsequent annulment. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, holds a different view: the division becomes void altogether (fāsidah) due to the claim, so the shares revert to joint ownership. What Khalid holds is now half for each, and Zaid is liable for the value of half of what he sold to the buyer (or to Khalid?). The passage explains that Abu Yusuf considers the division to be void, so the sale took place during a void contract, but since possession under a void contract still transfers ownership in movable property (mamlūk), the sale is valid. However, Zaid must guarantee the value (ḍamān al-qīmah) to his partner (or to the claimant?). The passage contrasts the two positions: Sahibayn preserve the division and limit compensation, while Abu Yusuf annuls the division and imposes liability. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) in the Hanafi school generally follows Sahibayn in this scenario, as the option is lost by the sale.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): The option to annul the division (naqd al-qismah) that a partner has upon istihqaq.
فاسد (fasid): Voidable contract; here, the division becomes fasid (void) according to Abu Yusuf upon istihqaq.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation (value) for property taken under a defective contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the partner sells half of his share before the remaining half is claimed, what is the ruling according to Sahibayn?
A) The division is automatically annulled.
B) The partner can still annul the division.
C) The partner loses the option to annul and can only claim a quarter from the other.
D) The partner must compensate the buyer.

Key Takeaway
Selling part of your share before istihqaq extinguishes your right to annul the division, and you can only claim a quarter from the other partner—this is the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Muhaya'ah: Permissibility and Rules of Alternate Use
Defines muhaya'ah and its permissibility by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of muhaya'ah, explain its permissibility by istihsan, and apply the rule of judicial compulsion (jabr) in cases of dispute between co-owners.

Core Idea
Muhaya'ah is a permissible division of usufruct by istihsan, but physical division (qismah) takes precedence when possible.

After covering the division of physical assets (qismah), this passage introduces muhaya'ah — the division of usufruct through alternate use. While physical division is ideal, it is often impractical for jointly owned property. The Hanafi school, using istihsan (juristic preference), allows a judge to enforce an alternation arrangement when needed. However, if physical division is possible, it overrides muhaya'ah. This lesson unpacks the definition, ruling, and comparative strength of these two forms of partition.

Guided Path
1
Define muhaya'ah
Identify the term as a verbal noun indicating mutual exchange of usufruct. Distinguish it from qismah, which divides the physical asset itself.
Muhaya'ah divides the benefit (manfa'ah) by time or space, not the actual property.
2
Determine the ruling and its basis
State that muhaya'ah is permissible (ja'iz) by istihsan due to need. Recognize that istihsan overrides any strict qiyas that might deem it invalid.
The need arises because joint use of property can be practically impossible (ta'addhur al-ijtima').
3
Compare with qismah
Note that both involve judicial compulsion (jabr al-qadi), but qismah is stronger because it provides complete benefit at once, while muhaya'ah gives successive benefits.
If one partner demands qismah and the other muhaya'ah, the judge orders qismah.
4
Analyze the effect of death and subsequent demands
Understand that muhaya'ah does not become void upon the death of one or both parties. If it were rescinded, the judge would simply re-establish it, so the law treats it as continuing.
The rationale: rescinding and re-establishing serves no useful purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المهاياة ترجمہ فصل ہے مہایات کے بیان میں تشریح مباياة مفاعت کا اور تبایو فاعل کا مصدر ہے جس کے معنی ہیں منافع کی تقسیم کرنا۔ جب مصنف اعیان کی تقسیم سے فارغ ہو گئے تو اب اعراض کی تقسیم کا آغاز فرمارہے ہیں۔ اسلئے کہ اعراض اعیان کی فرع ہے۔ یہاں مصنف کیلئے مناسب تھا کہ اسکو باب سے تعبیر فرماتے ۔ اسلئے کہ پہلے باب دعوی الغلط و الاستحقاق فيها ، میں گفتگو تھی اور مہایات کا تعلق اس باب سے نہیں ہے البتہ یہ جواب دیا جا سکتا ہے کہ یہ کتاب القسمہ کی فصل ہے نہ کہ باب سابق کی۔ مہایاۃ کی تعریف المهايا ة جائزة استحسانا للحاجة اليه اذ يتعذر الاجتماع على الانتفاع فاشبه القسمة ولهذا يجرى فيه جبر القاضي كما يجرى فى القسمة الا ان القسمة اقوى منه فى استكمال المنفعة لانه جمع المنافع في زمان واحد والتها يؤ جمع على التعاقب ولهذا لو طلب احد الشريكين القسمة والآخر المهاياة يقسم القاضي لانه ابلغ فى التكميل ولو وقعت فيما يحتمل القسمة ثم طلب احدهما القسمة يقسم وتبطل المهاياة لانه ابلغ ولا يبطل التها يؤبموت احدهما ولا بموتهما لانه لو انتقض لاستانهفه الحاكم ولا فائدة في النقض ثم الاستيناف
Chapter on Muhaya'ah. Translation: Chapter on explanation of Muhaya'ah. Explanation: Muhaya'ah is the masdar (verbal noun) of mutual giving (mufā‘alah) and mutual taking (tabāyu‘), meaning the division of usufruct. When the author finished the division of physical items, he now begins the division of non-physical items (a‘rāḍ), because non-physical items are subsidiary to physical ones. Here it would have been appropriate for the author to call it a chapter (bāb), because the previous chapter was on 'Claim of Error and Entitlement', and muhaya'ah is not related to that chapter; however, it can be answered that this is a section (faṣl) of the Book of Division, not of the previous chapter. Definition of Muhaya'ah: Muhaya'ah is permissible by istihsan due to the need for it, because joint enjoyment of the usufruct becomes difficult, so it resembles division (qismah). Consequently, the judge's compulsion (jabr) applies in it as it applies in division, except that division is stronger than it in completing the benefit, because division collects the benefits in one time, while muhaya'ah collects them successively. Hence, if one partner demands division and the other demands muhaya'ah, the judge orders division because it is more complete. If muhaya'ah occurs in something that admits division, then one of them demands division, the judge orders division and the muhaya'ah becomes invalid, because division is stronger. And muhaya'ah does not become invalid by the death of one of them nor by the death of both, because if it were rescinded, the judge would reinstate it, and there is no benefit in rescission then reinstatement.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of muhaya'ah — the alternation of use of jointly owned property. It is a new section (faṣl) within the Book of Division (Kitab al-Qismah). The commentator notes that the author might have called it a separate chapter, but it is placed here as a section. The ruling: muhaya'ah is permissible (jā'iz) by istihsan (juristic preference) due to need, because joint usufruct is often impractical. It resembles physical division (qismah) in that the judge can compel it. However, physical division is stronger because it provides complete benefit in one time, whereas muhaya'ah provides successive benefits. Therefore, if one co-owner wants physical division and the other wants muhaya'ah, the judge will order physical division. If muhaya'ah has been arranged on property that can be physically divided, and then one party demands physical division, the judge will order physical division and muhaya'ah is voided. Importantly, muhaya'ah does not end with the death of either or both parties; it persists because rescinding and re-establishing it serves no purpose. The judge would simply re-establish it if it lapsed.

Key Terms
مهاياة (muhāyāh): Alternating use of jointly owned property, dividing the usufruct by time or space.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference, departing from qiyas for a stronger reason.
جبر القاضي (jabr al-qāḍī): Judicial compulsion to force a division or arrangement on unwilling co-owners.
قسمة (qismah): Physical division of jointly owned property into separate shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if two co-owners of a house cannot agree on using it jointly, and one demands physical division (qismah) while the other demands alternate use (muhaya'ah), what does the judge do?
A) The judge orders muhaya'ah since both cannot agree.
B) The judge orders physical division because it is more complete in fulfilling benefit.
C) The judge leaves them to settle privately.
D) The judge orders sale of the property.

Key Takeaway
Muhaya'ah is a permissible istihsan-based division of usufruct, but qismah is preferred when feasible, and death does not void it.

Permissibility of Leasing One's Share in Muhaya'ah
Ruling on each partner's right to lease their share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing a share in muhaya'ah and explain the rationale based on ownership of usufruct.

Core Idea
Your share's usufruct is yours to lease — no partner's consent needed.

In a muhaya'ah arrangement, partners take turns using common property. A natural question arises: can a partner lease his allocated share to a third party without the other's permission? This lesson examines the unconditional Hanafi ruling and its logical basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that each partner has the right to exploit (yastaghil) his share that came to him through muhaya'ah. The act is leasing or deriving benefit from one's allocated portion. The ruling is permissibility (mubah).
Exploitation can include leasing for rent or any lawful use.
2
Note the condition of stipulation
The text explicitly says 'whether this condition was stipulated in the contract or not' — meaning no prior agreement is required. The ruling is unconditional.
This removes any requirement of explicit consent in the original partnership contract.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The reason given is 'because the usufructs belong to his ownership.' Once the share is allocated via muhaya'ah, the partner owns the usufruct of that portion exclusively, so he may dispose of it freely.
Ownership of usufruct (manafi') is a key Hanafi principle that enables independent disposition.
4
Recognize the unconditional nature
The ruling does not depend on any external condition or the partner's approval. It is a straightforward permission based on property rights.
This position is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكل واحد ان يستغل ما اصابه بالمهاياة شرط ذالك فى العقد اولم يشترط لحدث والمنافع على م ملکه
And every one of them has the right to exploit what has come to him through muhaya'ah, whether this condition was stipulated in the contract or not, because the usufructs belong to his ownership.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage states a ruling (hukm) on the permissibility for each partner in a muhaya'ah (time-based or place-based partition of usufruct) to lease his allocated share to a third party. The ruling is unconditional: it does not matter whether the partners had agreed in the original contract (e.g., a joint purchase or inheritance) that each could lease or not. The reason (ta'lil) is that the usufruct (manafi') of each share belongs exclusively to that partner's ownership, so he has the right to dispose of it as he wishes. Some later scholars (muhaddithin) raised an objection regarding the issue of borrowing (ariyah), but that point is not elaborated here. The source is a commentary (sharh) expanding the matn of Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
المهاياة (al-muhāyā'ah): A mutual arrangement between partners to use the common property in turns (time) or in portions (place).
يستغل (yastaghil): To exploit or derive benefit from property, typically by leasing it for rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, permission must be stipulated.
B) Yes, because the usufruct belongs to his ownership.
C) Only after the partner's approval.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a partner in muhaya'ah may freely lease his allocated share because the usufruct is his exclusive property.

Muhaya'ah in Time for a Single Slave
Ruling on time-based muhaya'ah for a single slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on time-based muhaya'ah for indivisible property and identify when time-based division is appropriate.

Core Idea
Time-based muhaya'ah is valid for indivisible assets like a single slave or small house.

The Hanafi school permits partners who jointly own an indivisible asset, such as a single slave or a small house, to divide its usufruct by time. This lesson examines the ruling that such a time-based arrangement (muhaya'ah fi al-zaman) is legally valid and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is two partners making a muhaya'ah (partition of usufruct) for a single slave, agreeing that the slave serves each partner on alternating days. The ruling is 'jāz' (permissible).
2
Recognize the two forms of muhaya'ah
Muhaya'ah can be time-based (fi al-zaman) or place-based (fi al-makan). The text states both forms are recognized in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand why time-based is determined here
For a single slave or a small house, spatial division is not feasible because the asset is indivisible. Therefore, time-based muhaya'ah is the appropriate form.
The phrase 'al-awwal muta'ayyin hāhunā' indicates that time-based is the determined method for such cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تهايئا فى عبد واحد على ان يخدم هذا يوما وهذا يوما جاز وكذا هذا فى البيت الصغير لان المهاياة قد تكون في الزمان وقد تكون من حيث المكان والاول متعين ههنا
And if they made a muhaya'ah in a single slave, on the condition that he serves this one one day and that one one day, it is permissible. And similarly, this is [permissible] in a small house, because muhaya'ah can be in time (zaman) and in place (makan), and the first (i.e., time) is determined here.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage states a specific ruling (hukm) regarding muhaya'ah (partition of usufruct) in a single slave owned jointly by two partners. The partners agree that the slave will serve one partner for one day and the other partner for the next day, alternating. According to the Hanafi school, this is permissible (ja'iz). The commentator extends the same ruling to a small house (al-bayt al-saghir): if two partners own a small house, they may also arrange time-based muhaya'ah for its use. The rationale is that muhaya'ah can take two forms: time-based (fi al-zaman) and place-based (fi al-makan). In the case of a single slave or a small house, the time-based form is the appropriate one (first determined, muta'ayyin), since the property is indivisible spatially. This is a clear endorsement of the validity of time-based muhaya'ah for indivisible or hard-to-divide assets.

Key Terms
الزمان (al-zamān): Time-based muhaya'ah where partners use the entire asset in turns.
المكان (al-makān): Place-based muhaya'ah where each partner uses a specific part of the property simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is time-based muhaya'ah valid for a single slave owned by two partners?
A) No, because the slave cannot be divided in time.
B) Yes, but only if they also have a spatial division.
C) Yes, it is permissible.
D) Only if the qadi approves.

Key Takeaway
Time-based muhaya'ah is a valid and complete arrangement for indivisible jointly-owned property in Hanafi fiqh.

Resolving Disputes Over Time vs. Place in Muhaya'ah
Procedure for resolving dispute over muhaya'ah type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure when partners disagree on whether muhaya'ah was time-based or place-based, and explain why casting lots is used.

Core Idea
When partners dispute the type of muhaya'ah, the qadi orders agreement; if time-based is chosen, lots are cast to ensure fairness.

Imagine two partners sharing a large house. They had a muhaya'ah arrangement, but now one insists it was time-based (alternating months) while the other claims it was place-based (each gets separate rooms). How does a Hanafi qadi resolve this? This lesson explains the procedure, emphasizing the role of agreement and lots, and the wisdom behind preferring place-based division as more just.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The partners disagree on whether their muhaya'ah (division of usufruct) was based on time or place. The property must be capable of both forms (e.g., divisible into parts or time slots).
If the property can only support one form, the qadi would impose that form.
2
Understand the qadi's first order
The qadi does not decide immediately. He first orders the partners to come to an agreement, because both forms have merit: place is more just (simultaneous benefit), time is more complete (exclusive use).
The qadi cannot prefer one without agreement due to the different virtues.
3
Analyze the options
If they agree on place-based, the division is straightforward. If they agree on time-based, an additional step is needed: deciding who goes first.
Time-based requires a starting party.
4
Apply the procedure for time-based
If time-based is chosen, the qadi orders casting lots (qur'ah) to determine who begins, in order to eliminate any suspicion of bias (tuhmah).
Lots ensure procedural fairness and remove any hint of partiality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اختلفا فى التها يؤ من حيث الزمان والمكان فى محل يحتملها يامرهما القاضى بان يتفقا لان التها يؤفى المكان اعدل وفى الزمان اكمل فلما اختلفت الجهة لا بد من الاتفاق فان اختاراه من حيث الزمان يقرع في البداية نفيا للتهمة
And if they differ regarding muhaya'ah from the perspective of time and place in a place that can bear both, the qadi orders them to agree because muhaya'ah in place is more just and in time is more complete. So when the aspect differs, agreement is necessary. If they choose time-based, lots are cast at the beginning to eliminate suspicion.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage provides the legal procedure when two partners who previously made a muhaya'ah arrangement disagree on whether it was time-based or place-based. The property in question must be such that both forms are possible (e.g., a large house). The qadi (judge) does not decide by himself but orders the partners to come to an agreement because both forms have distinct merits: place-based (makan) is more just (a'dal) because both partners benefit simultaneously, while time-based (zaman) is more complete (akmal) because each gets full use during their turn. Since the aspects differ, the qadi cannot impose one; he insists on mutual agreement. If the partners then agree on time-based muhaya'ah, the qadi directs casting lots (qur'ah) to decide who starts first, in order to remove any suspicion of bias (tuhmah). This maintains procedural fairness.

Key Terms
القرعة (al-qur'ah): Casting lots to determine who begins first in a time-based muhaya'ah.
اعدل (a'dal): More just: place-based muhaya'ah allows simultaneous benefit, seen as more equitable.
المهاياة (al-muhaya'ah): A division of usufruct (right to use) of jointly owned property, either by time or by space.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He imposes place-based because it is more just.
D) He nullifies the muhaya'ah.

Key Takeaway
When partners dispute the type of muhaya'ah, the qadi orders agreement due to incomparable virtues; if time-based is chosen, lots decide the starting order to prevent bias.

Compulsory Muhaya'ah in Slaves: The Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imposing muhaya'ah by the qadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a qadi can impose muhaya'ah for two slaves and state the tarjih and its basis.

Core Idea
A qadi may impose muhaya'ah on two slaves if their service benefits are nearly equal; the correct Hanafi view prevails despite a contrary narration from Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the permissibility of a qadi imposing muhaya'ah (alternating use) on two slaves owned jointly by two partners. While the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) allow compulsion, a narration reports that Abu Hanifa denied it. The commentator resolves the ikhtilaf, declaring the correct view (al-ashah) that the qadi may impose, even according to Abu Hanifa, because the service benefits are seldom highly unequal. This lesson dissects the reasoning and the principle of jabr (compulsory division) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
Two partners own two slaves. They consider a muhaya'ah where each partner exclusively uses one slave. The question is: can the qadi impose this arrangement without mutual consent?
The arrangement itself is permissible; the dispute is about compulsion.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn hold that the qadi can impose it. Their proof is qiyas to compulsory division (qismah jabran) of property, which they allow when shares are equal or nearly so.
They consider muhaya'ah essentially a division of benefits.
3
State the opposing narration from Abu Hanifa and its basis
A reported view from Abu Hanifa says the qadi cannot impose because jabr (compulsion) does not apply to benefits (manafi'). Benefits are not physical assets, so forced division is unjust.
This view stresses the distinction between physical property and usufruct.
4
Explain the tarjih and the ratio decidendi
The commentator declares the correct view (al-ashah) that the qadi can impose, even according to Abu Hanifa. The reason is that service benefits are seldom highly differentiated (qallamā tatafāwatu), unlike the physical slaves themselves which vary greatly in value.
Since the difference in service is minimal, imposing the arrangement is not unjust.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical outcome is that the qadi has authority to enforce muhaya'ah when partners refuse, as long as the service benefits are roughly equal. This maintains harmony and prevents one partner from being unjustly deprived.
This ruling applies to jointly owned assets where usage benefits are similar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تهايئا في العبد ين على ان يخدم هذا هذا العبد والآخر الآخر جاز عندهما لان القسمة على هذا الوجه جائزة عندهما جبرا من القاضى وبالتراضى فكذا المهاياة وقيل عند ابي حنيفة لا يقسم القاضي وهكذا روى عنه لانه لا يجرى فيه الجبر عنده والاصح انه يقسم القاضى عنده ايضا لان المنافع من حيث الخدمة قلما تتفاوت بخلاف اعیان الرقيق لانها تتفاوت تفاوتا فاحشا على ما تقدم
And if they made muhaya'ah in two slaves, on the condition that this one serves this [partner] and the other serves the other, it is permissible according to them (the Two Companions) because division in this manner is permissible according to them, both by compulsion from the qadi and by mutual consent. So similarly is muhaya'ah. And it is said that according to Abu Hanifa the qadi does not impose division, and it is thus narrated from him, because compulsion does not apply in his view. But the correct view is that the qadi imposes division according to him as well, because the benefits (manafi') from the perspective of service are seldom highly differentiated, unlike the physical slaves themselves, which are highly differentiated as previously detailed.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (dispute) regarding the permissibility of the qadi imposing a muhaya'ah arrangement for two slaves owned jointly by two partners. The scenario is that partners agree (or the qadi imposes) that each slave serves exclusively one partner. The Two Companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that this is permissible and that the qadi can impose it even without mutual consent, by analogy (qiyas) to compulsory division of property (qismah jabran) which they allow in such cases. There is a narration that Abu Hanifa initially held that the qadi cannot impose such a muhaya'ah because compulsion (jabr) does not apply to benefits (manafi') in his view, given that benefits are considered distinct from physical assets. However, the commentator states that the correct view (al-ashah) is that even according to Abu Hanifa, the qadi can impose the arrangement. The reason is that the benefits of service are seldom significantly different (qallamā tatafāwatu), unlike the physical slaves themselves which are highly unequal (tafāwut fāhish). Since the difference in service value is minimal, imposing a muhaya'ah is not unjust. This aligns with the principle that where goods are roughly equal, the qadi may compel partition.

Key Terms
جبر (jabr): Compulsion by a qadi to enforce a division or muhaya'ah.
الصاحبين (al-Ṣāḥibayn): The Two Companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the chief disciples of Abu Hanifa.
المهايأة (al-muhāyā'ah): An arrangement where co-owners alternate the use of a jointly owned asset, especially slaves or real estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, only with mutual consent.
B) Yes, because the service benefits are not highly unequal.
C) Only if the slaves are of equal value.
D) No, because Abu Hanifa forbade it.

Key Takeaway
The qadi may impose muhaya'ah on jointly owned slaves when service benefits are nearly equal, even if the physical slaves differ in value.

Muhayat for Slaves' Provisions: Food vs Clothing by Istihsan
Ruling with proof by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muhayat for slaves' food and clothing, and apply the principle of istihsan to identify when a slight difference in usufruct makes the arrangement permissible.

Core Idea
Muhayat for food is permissible by istihsan; for clothing, it requires specification due to significant difference.

In Hanafi partnership law, co-owners may agree to partition the usufruct of jointly owned property without dividing the corpus—this is muhayat. This passage examines a specific case: two partners each own a share in two slaves. They agree that each partner will bear the provisions for the slave who serves him. Is this valid? The answer depends on whether the provisions are food or clothing, based on the concept of tolerance (musamaha) and significant difference (tafawut fahish).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that muhayat is a mutual assignment of usufruct. The text rules that for food, it is permissible (ja'iz) by istihsan; for clothing, it is not permissible unless specifically defined (ma'ruf).
The default ruling without istihsan would be impermissible due to uncertainty (gharar) in exchange.
2
Distinguish between food and clothing
Understand why food is treated leniently: the difference in food quality between partners is typically slight (tafawut qalil), and people are generally generous with food. In contrast, clothing can have significant difference (tafawut fahish), and people are stingy, so the arrangement resembles an uncertain exchange.
The key concept is 'tafawut fahish' which makes items non-homogeneous (different jins).
3
Understand the role of istihsan
Istihsan (juristic preference) overrides the strict analogy (qiyas) that would prohibit muhayat due to uncertainty. The impermissible aspect is overlooked based on customary tolerance and ease.
Istihsan is a fundamental source in the Hanafi school, especially for muamalat.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Earlier, there was a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding muhayat in corporeal property (a'yan). Here, for usufruct (manafi'), the correct view (asah) is that Imam Abu Hanifa agrees with permissibility, resolving the dispute.
This shows how later authorities harmonize differences within the school.

Source Text

And if they make muhayat in two houses on condition that each of them lives in a house, it is permissible by istihsan due to tolerance in feeding slaves, contrary to the stipulation of clothing because there is no tolerance in it. (Translation of Arabic matn only). Commentary: ... (as above in Urdu)
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of muhayat (mutual assignment of usufruct) regarding two jointly owned slaves. The default obligation is that both partners equally provide for the slaves' food and clothing. If they agree that each partner will bear the provisions for the slave who serves him, the ruling differs between food and clothing. Food is permissible by istihsan (juristic preference) because the difference in quality between partners' food is typically slight, and people are generally generous with food, so there is no substantial risk of injustice. Clothing, however, is not permissible unless the specific type of clothing is defined, because clothing differences can be significant (tafawut fahish), and people tend to be stingy with clothing; hence the arrangement involves an exchange of undefined halves, which contains gharar (uncertainty). The text also notes that the correct view (asah) is that Imam Abu Hanifa himself permits this muhayat for food, contrary to the earlier dispute regarding corporeal property (a'yan) where his view differed from the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
التهايؤ (al-muhayat): A mutual agreement among co-owners to partition the usufruct of a jointly owned property without dividing the corpus.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A juristic preference that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or ease.
تفاوت فاحش (tafawut fahish): A significant or excessive difference in value or quality that renders objects or rights non-homogeneous (different jins).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because clothing is considered a capital asset
D) Because slaves cannot wear clothes

Key Takeaway
Muhayat for usufruct is permissible when the difference in benefits is slight, by istihsan, but requires specification for significant items like clothing.

Muhayat in Two Houses: The Three Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on muhayat in two houses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on muhayat in two houses, explain the reasoning behind each, and identify the mufta bihi position with its dalil.

Core Idea
Muhayat in two houses is permissible and compellable when usufruct differences are slight; weightier difference turns it into an exchange.

When two people jointly own two houses, can they agree to each live in one house exclusively? And if one refuses, can a judge force such an arrangement? The Hanafi school has three positions on this issue, rooted in whether the arrangement is considered a mere separation of usufruct (ifraz) or a barter exchange (mubadala). This lesson unpacks the dispute and shows how the relied-upon view treats muhayat as a permissible, compellable division when the difference in benefits is minor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
What is the legal issue? Two co-owners of two houses want to each occupy one house exclusively. Is this muhayat (division of usufruct) valid? Can a judge compel it?
The dispute is about both permissibility and enforceability.
2
Map the three Hanafi positions
List each view: (1) Sahibayn: permissible by consent and compellable; (2) Abu Hanifa (narration): not permissible at all; (3) Abu Hanifa (al-Karkhi): permissible by consent only, not compellable.
The text mentions 'qila' for al-Karkhi and 'an Abi Hanifa' for total prohibition.
3
Analyze the evidence for each position
For Sahibayn: two houses are like one house, difference in usufruct is slight → ifraz. For total prohibition: it is a sale of dwelling for dwelling, which is batil due to gharar. For consent-only: it is an exchange, so no compulsion but consent waives the objection.
The key distinction is between ifraz (separation without exchange) and mubadala (exchange).
4
Identify the mufta bihi and its reasoning
The zahir al-riwaya (text relied upon) is the Sahibayn's view. Reason: the difference in usufruct is slight, so it is considered ifraz; compulsion is allowed because it is like partition of one house.
The text explicitly says 'وجہ الظاہر' (face of the apparent) and labels other narrations as nawadir.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Imagine Zayd and Amr own two houses. Zayd wants to live in house A, Amr in house B. If they agree, it is valid. If Zayd refuses, Amr can take him to court, and the judge can compel the muhayat based on the mufta bihi view.
If the houses are vastly unequal in value, the ruling may differ (treated as exchange, not ifraz).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنگیه
دو گھر وں میں مہایات اس طرح کی کہ ایک میں ایک دوسرے میں دوسرا ر ہے گا، اس کا حکم "
وَلَوْ تَهَايَأَا فِي دَارَيْنِ عَلَى أَنْ يَسْكُنَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا دَارًا جَازَ وَيُجْبِرُ الْقَاضِي عَلَيْهِ أَمَّا عِنْدَهُمَا فَظَاهِرٌ لِأَنَّ الدَّارَيْنِ عِنْدَهُمَا كَدَارٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَقَدْ قِيلَ لَا يُجْبِرُ عِنْدَهُ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْقِسْمَةِ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ التَّهَايُؤُ فِيهِمَا أَصْلًا بِالْجَبْرِ فَلِمَا قُلْنَا وَبِالتَّرَاضِي لِأَنَّهُ بَيْعُ السُّكْنَى بِالسُّكْنَى بِخِلَافِ قِسْمَةِ رِقْبَتِهِمَا لِأَنَّ بَيْعَ بَعْضِ أَحَدِهِمَا بَعْضَ الْآخَرِ جَائِزٌ وَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ التَّفَاوُتَ يَقِلُّ فِي الْمَنَافِعِ فَيَجُوزُ بِالتَّرَاضِي وَيَجْرِي فِيهِ جَبْرُ الْقَاضِي عُتِبِرَ إِفْرَازًا أَمَّا يَكْثُرُ التَّفَاوُتُ فِي أَعْيَانِهِمَا فَاعْتُبِرَ مُبَادَلَةً
ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں نے مہایات کی دوگھروں میں اس طریقہ پر کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک ایک گھر میں رہے گا تو جائز ہے اور قاضی  اس پر جبر کرے گا بہر حال صاحبین کے نزدیک پس ظاہر ہے اس لئے کہ دو گھر ان کے نزدیک ایک گھر کے مثل ہیں اور کہا گیا ہے کلام ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ دو گھروں میں مہایات بالکل جائز نہیں نہ جبر کے ساتھ۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور نہ تراضی کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ یہ سکنی کی سکنی کے بدلہ بیج ہے بخلاف ان دونوں کے رقبہ کی قسمت کے اس لئے کہ ان دو گھروں میں سے ایک کے کچھ حصہ کی بیع دوسرے کے بعض کے بدلہ جائز ہے ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع میں کم ہوتا ہے تو یہ تر اضی کے ساتھ جائز ہے اور اس میں قاضی کا جبر جاری ہوگا اور اس کو افر از اعتبار کیا جائے گا بہر حال ان دونوں کے اعیان میں تفاوت زیادہ ہوتا ہے تو اس کو مبادلہ اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح زید اور عمر کے درمیان دو گھر مشترک ہیں انہوں نے یہ طے کر لیا کہ ایک میں زیدر ہے اور دوسرے میں عمر تو یہ جائز ہے اور دونوں میں سے ایک کی طلب پر قاضی اس مہایات پر جبر کرے گا اس میں ائمہ ثلاثہ کا اتفاق ہے
سوال . یہ بات تو صرف صاحبین کے یہاں درست ہوسکتی ہے جو دارین کو دارین واحد کا درجہ دیتے ہیں اور اس میں تقسیم کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں جیسا کہ ہدایہ ص ۳۹۹ ج ۳ پر اس کی تفصیل گزر چکی ہے مگر ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تو یہ مہایات جائز نہ ہونی چاہیئے کیوں کہ جدا جدا ان کی تقسیم ان کے یہاں جائز نہیں ہے ( تمامر ) تو پھر اتفاق کیسے؟ جواب ... مہایات میں منافع کی تحصیل ہے جس میں تفاوت قلیل ہے تو یہ بتر اضی بھی جائز اور جب ابھی کیوں کہ یہ افراز کا درجہ ہے اور ان کی قسمت میں تفاوت فاحش ہے تو وہاں یہ مبادلہ ہے اور مبادلہ میں جبر جائز نہیں ہوتا۔
سوال ... امام صاحب سے تو اور بھی اقوال مذکور ہیں؟ جواب ظاہر الروایہ تو وہ ہے جو مذکور ہوا یعنی جواز اور دیگر اقوال نوادرات میں منقول ہیں ان میں سے تو ایک قول یہ ہے کہ بتراضی جائز ہے جبر جائز نہیں اور یہی کرخی کا قول ہے اور دوسرا قول یہ منقول ہے کہ یہ مہایات ہی جائز نہیں نہ جبرا اور نہ بتراضی۔ اول کی دلیل تو ذکر کی جاچکی ہے اور تراضی کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ سنی کی بیچ سکنی کے بدلہ میں ہے اور یہ باطل ہے اور قسمت میں گھر کے بعض حصہ کی بیع دوسرے کے بعض کے بدلہ میں ہے اور وہ جائز ہے ۔۔
And if they make muhayat in two houses on condition that each of them lives in a house, it is permissible and the judge will compel it. As for according to them (Sahibayn), it is apparent because two houses with them are like one house. And it has been said: he does not compel according to him, by analogy to partition. And from Abu Hanifa: that muhayat in them is not permissible at all by compulsion, for what we said, nor by mutual consent, because it is a sale of dwelling for dwelling, unlike division of their corpus because selling part of one for part of the other is permissible. The face of the apparent [view] is that the difference is slight in usufruct, so it is permissible by mutual consent and the judge's compulsion runs in it, considering it as ifraz. As for their corpus, the difference is great, so it is considered exchange. (Translation of Arabic matn and Urdu).
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding muhayat in two jointly owned houses. The core issue is whether co-owners can agree to each occupy one house exclusively, and whether a judge can compel such an arrangement. Three positions are presented: (1) The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it permissible and enforceably by the judge because they treat two houses as equivalent to one house regarding the permissibility of partition of usufruct. (2) A narration from Abu Hanifa prohibits it entirely—neither by consent nor compulsion—because it constitutes a sale of dwelling for dwelling, which is a barter of uncertain value, unlike a sale of parts of the corpus. (3) Another narration from Abu Hanifa (reported by al-Karkhi) permits it by mutual consent but not by judicial compulsion. The relied-upon view (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is permissible by mutual consent and the judge can compel, as stated in the text. The reasoning is that since the difference in usufruct (manafi') between the two houses is slight, the arrangement is considered ifraz (separation of shares of usufruct), not a mubadala (exchange). In partition of corpus (qismat al-raqaba), the difference is significant, so it is treated as exchange and cannot be compelled. The commentary resolves a question: why would all three imams agree on compulsion when Abu Hanifa rejects partitioning separate houses? The answer: muhayat is about usufruct, where difference is slight, so it is ifraz and compulsion is allowed; this does not contradict Abu Hanifa's view on partition of houses (where difference is significant and thus prohibited).

Key Terms
التهايؤ (al-muhayat): An agreement among co-owners to divide the usufruct (manfa'ah) of a jointly owned asset without dividing the corpus (raqaba).
الإفراز (al-ifraz): Separation of shares in a joint property that does not involve exchange; the shares are considered distinct even though the corpus remains undivided.
المبادلة (al-mubadala): Exchange of shares, which requires strict equivalence and is subject to rules of sale, including prohibition of gharar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (zahir al-riwaya), what is the ruling on muhayat in two houses?
A) It is impermissible both by consent and compulsion
B) It is permissible by consent but the judge cannot compel
C) It is permissible by consent and the judge can compel
D) It is permissible only if the houses are exactly equal in usufruct value

Key Takeaway
Muhayat in two houses is treated as ifraz (separation of usufruct) when differences are slight, making it permissible and compellable by a judge; significant differences turn it into a non-compellable exchange.

Muhayat for Riding Animals: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on muhayat for riding animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on muhayat for riding animals and explain the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's prohibition and the Sahibayn's permissibility.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prohibits muhayat for riding animals because rider skill differences cause unequal exertion; Sahibayn permit by analogy to property partition.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding muhayat (mutual assignment) for riding animals. The central question is whether two or more animals can be shared by alternating riding, given that the exertion on the animal depends on the rider's skill. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold opposing positions, and their reasoning highlights a key distinction between animals and slaves in Hanafi fiduciary law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is muhayat for riding animals – two or more persons mutually assign turns to ride a jointly owned animal. The dispute is whether such an arrangement is permissible (ja'iz) or not.
Muhayat is a form of usufruct division, not a transfer of ownership.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that muhayat for riding animals is not permissible (la yajuz). His proof is that the actual usage of the animal varies significantly with the rider's skill (haziq vs akhraq), creating an unequal and uncertain exchange (tafawut fahish).
The difference in usage is considered 'fahish' (gross), making the arrangement akin to an invalid sale of uncertain value.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that muhayat is permissible (yajuz). They analogize (qiyas) to the division of corporeal property (qismat al-a'yan), where differences in value are tolerated and compensation can be made.
In property division, even if lots are unequal, the division is valid and the difference may be rectified by khul' (money compensation).
4
Note the extension to a single animal
The same disagreement applies to muhayat for riding a single animal (e.g., two persons sharing one horse). The reasoning remains: for Abu Hanifa, rider skill still causes unequal usage; for Sahibayn, the analogy to property division holds.
The text explicitly extends the ruling: 'and muhayat for riding on one animal is subject to the same disagreement'.
5
Contrast with a slave
The text distinguishes a slave from an animal: a slave serves by choice and will not exceed his capacity, so muhayat regarding a slave's services is not subject to this dispute. An animal, however, passively bears the rider's actions, making the skill difference critical.
This distinction underscores that the illa (effective cause) is the animal's lack of volition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو چوپاؤں پر سواری میں تہا یو کا حکم اقوال فقہاء
وَفِي الدَّابَّتَيْنِ لَا يَجُوزُ التَّهَايُؤُ عَلَى الرُّكُوبِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَجُوزُ اعْتِبَارًا بِقِسْمَةِ الْأَعْيَانِ وَلَهُ أَنَّ الِاسْتِعْمَالَ يَتَفَاوَتُ بِتَفَاوُتِ الرَّاكِبِينَ فَإِنَّهُمْ بَيْنَ حَاذِقٍ وَأَخْرَقَ وَالتَّهَايُؤُ فِي الرُّكُوبِ فِي دَابَّةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ عَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ لِمَا قُلْنَا بِخِلَافِ الْعَبْدِ لِأَنَّهُ يَخْدُمُ بِاخْتِيَارِهِ فَلَا يَتَحَمَّلُ زِيَادَةً عَلَى طَاقَتِهِ وَالدَّابَّةُ تَحْمِلُهَا
ترجمہ اور دو چوپاؤں پریوار ہونے پر مہایات ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک قسمت اعیان پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے جائز ہے اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ استعمال متفاوت ہوتا ہے سواروں کے تفاوت سے اس لئے کہ سوار ماہر اور اناڑی کے درمیان ہے اور ایک چوپایہ میں سورای پر مہایات اسی اختلاف پر ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں بخلاف غلام کے اس لئے کہ وہ
And regarding two riding animals, muhayat for riding is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but according to them (Sahibayn) it is permissible, by analogy to division of corporeal property. Abu Hanifa's proof: that the usage varies with the variation of riders, for they are between skilled and unskilled. And muhayat for riding on one animal is subject to the same disagreement for the reason we said, unlike a slave because he serves by his choice and does not bear more than his capacity, but the animal bears it. (Translation of Arabic matn and Urdu).
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on muhayat for riding animals (two or one). Abu Hanifa prohibits it because the actual usage (istikmal) of the animal differs greatly based on the rider's skill; a skilled rider causes more strain, so the difference in usufruct is significant (tafawut fahish), making the arrangement an uncertain exchange (mubadala) which is invalid. The Sahibayn analogize (qiyas) to partition of corporeal property (qismat al-a'yan), where even if values differ, partition is permissible. They consider the animals as fungible units. The text notes that the same disagreement applies to muhayat for riding on a single animal. However, a slave is different because a slave serves voluntarily and will not exceed his capacity; hence muhayat regarding a slave's service may be permissible on a different basis.

Key Terms
الدابة (al-dabbah): A riding animal, such as a horse, mule, or donkey.
الحاذق (al-haziq): A skilled rider who can manage the animal well, causing less strain.
الأخرق (al-akhraq): An unskilled rider who mishandles the animal, causing greater strain and wear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hanifa prohibit muhayat for riding animals, according to the text?
A) Because animals are not owned
B) Because riders' varying skills cause significant difference in the animal's usage
C) Because muhayat is always prohibited
D) Because the animals are alive

Key Takeaway
The dispute on muhayat for riding animals turns on whether the usufruct is considered equal when riders have different skills – Abu Hanifa says no due to tafawut fahish, while the Sahibayn analogize to property division.

Muhayaat in Two Houses: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on muhayaat in two houses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on muhayaat in two houses, explain the illa behind each position, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Muhayaat in two houses is permissible and compellable if the usufruct disparity is minimal; otherwise it is a barter where compulsion is invalid.

This passage from Kitab al-Qismah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on whether time-sharing (muhayaat) of two co-owned houses is permissible and whether a qadi can compel it. Imam Abu Hanifa's view differs from his two disciples, the Sahibayn, and the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) sides with the Sahibayn. Understanding the distinction between division of usufruct (ifraz) and exchange (mubadala) is key to grasping the legal logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the parties
The issue is muhayaat (time-sharing of usufruct) in two jointly owned houses. The parties are Imam Abu Hanifa, his disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), and later authorities like al-Karkhi. The text also mentions other transmitted opinions (nawadir).
Remember that muhayaat is a division of usufruct, not physical partition (qismah al-a'yan).
2
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn hold that muhayaat in two houses is permissible with mutual consent, and the qadi can compel it. Their proof: the disparity in usufruct is minimal, so it is treated as ifraz (separation) where compulsion is allowed. They analogize two houses to a single house, which is allowed by consensus.
This is the zahir al-riwaya position, which is mufta bihi.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to have said muhayaat in two houses is absolutely impermissible, neither by consent nor compulsion. His proof: it is like exchanging one dwelling for another (sukna bi-sukna), which is invalid because it resembles a ribawi transaction or an invalid sale. In physical division, disparity is great, so it is treated as mubadala (barter) where compulsion is not allowed.
The text also mentions other nawadir opinions, e.g., al-Karkhi's view that only mutual consent suffices.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to the Sahibayn, co-owners can be compelled to accept a time-sharing arrangement; according to Abu Hanifa, they cannot, and such an arrangement would be invalid even if mutually agreed. This affects real estate disputes and court rulings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view, as it is the zahir al-riwaya. Later Hanafi works like al-Hidayah adopt this as the operative ruling. The text resolves the apparent conflict by noting that muhayaat involves usufruct (minimal disparity) while physical division involves assets (great disparity).
The tarjih is based on the principle that qadi's compulsion applies to ifraz but not mubadala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اس پر جبر کرے گا بہر حال صاحبین کے نزدیک پس ظاہر ہے اس لئے کہ دو گھر ان کے نزدیک ایک گھر کے مثل ہیں اور کہا گیا ہے کلام ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ دو گھروں میں مہایات بالکل جائز نہیں نہ جبر کے ساتھ۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور نہ تراضی کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ یہ سکنی کی سکنی کے بدلہ بیج ہے بخلاف ان دونوں کے رقبہ کی قسمت کے اس لئے کہ ان دو گھروں میں سے ایک کے کچھ حصہ کی بیع دوسرے کے بعض کے بدلہ جائز ہے ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع میں کم ہوتا ہے تو یہ تر اضی کے ساتھ جائز ہے اور اس میں قاضی کا جبر جاری ہوگا اور اس کو افر از اعتبار کیا جائے گا بہر حال ان دونوں کے اعیان میں تفاوت زیادہ ہوتا ہے تو اس کو مبادلہ اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح زید اور عمر کے درمیان دو گھر مشترک ہیں انہوں نے یہ طے کر لیا کہ ایک میں زیدر ہے اور دوسرے میں عمر تو یہ جائز ہے اور دونوں میں سے ایک کی طلب پر قاضی اس مہایات پر جبر کرے گا اس میں ائمہ ثلاثہ کا اتفاق ہے
سوال . یہ بات تو صرف صاحبین کے یہاں درست ہوسکتی ہے جو دارین کو دارین واحد کا درجہ دیتے ہیں اور اس میں تقسیم کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں جیسا کہ ہدایہ ص ۳۹۹ ج ۳ پر اس کی تفصیل گزر چکی ہے مگر ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تو یہ مہایات جائز نہ ہونی چاہیئے کیوں کہ جدا جدا ان کی تقسیم ان کے یہاں جائز نہیں ہے ( تمامر ) تو پھر اتفاق کیسے؟ جواب ... مہایات میں منافع کی تحصیل ہے جس میں تفاوت قلیل ہے تو یہ بتر اضی بھی جائز اور جب ابھی کیوں کہ یہ افراز کا درجہ ہے اور ان کی قسمت میں تفاوت فاحش ہے تو وہاں یہ مبادلہ ہے اور مبادلہ میں جبر جائز نہیں ہوتا۔
سوال ... امام صاحب سے تو اور بھی اقوال مذکور ہیں؟ جواب ظاہر الروایہ تو وہ ہے جو مذکور ہوا یعنی جواز اور دیگر اقوال نوادرات میں منقول ہیں ان میں سے تو ایک قول یہ ہے کہ بتراضی جائز ہے جبر جائز نہیں اور یہی کرخی کا قول ہے اور دوسرا قول یہ منقول ہے کہ یہ مہایات ہی جائز نہیں نہ جبرا اور نہ بتراضی۔ اول کی دلیل تو ذکر کی جاچکی ہے اور تراضی کی دلیل ہے کہ یہ سنی کی بیچ سکنی کے بدلہ میں ہے اور یہ باطل ہے اور قسمت میں گھر کے بعض حصہ کی بیع دوسرے کے بعض کے بدلہ میں ہے اور وہ جائز ہے ۔۔
Book of Division. He will compel it; in the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is apparent, because two houses in their view are like one house. And it has been said that a saying is narrated from Abu Hanifa that muhayaat in two houses is absolutely not permissible, neither with compulsion—due to the proof we have already stated—nor with mutual consent, because it is selling one dwelling for another dwelling, unlike the physical division of both, because the sale of some part of one house in exchange for some part of another is valid. The proof of the zahir al-riwaya is that since there is little disparity in usufruct, it is permissible with mutual consent, and the qadi's compulsion will apply, and it is considered an ifraz (separation). In any case, in physical assets the disparity is great, so it is considered a mubadala (barter). Clarification: Zaid and 'Amr jointly own two houses. They agree that Zaid will reside in one and 'Amr in the other. This is permissible, and upon the request of either, the qadi will compel this muhayaat; the three imams are agreed on this. Question: This is only valid with the Sahibayn, who treat two houses like one house and permit division therein, as detailed in Hidayah vol. 3 p. 399, but according to Abu Hanifa, such muhayaat should not be permissible because separate division is not permissible with him. So how is there agreement? Answer: In muhayaat, the acquisition of usufruct is involved, in which disparity is little, so it is permissible with both mutual consent and compulsion because it is of the rank of ifraz. In their physical division, disparity is great, so there it is mubadala, and compulsion is not permissible in mubadala. Question: Are there other sayings transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa? Answer: The zahir al-riwaya is what has been mentioned, i.e., permissibility. Other sayings are transmitted in nawadir. Among them, one saying is that it is permissible with mutual consent but compulsion is not permissible; this is the view of al-Karkhi. Another saying transmitted is that this muhayaat is not permissible at all, neither by compulsion nor by mutual consent. The proof of the first has already been mentioned. The proof of (the view that it is permissible only with mutual consent) is that it is selling one dwelling for another, and that is invalid; while in physical division, the sale of some part of a house in exchange for some part of another is valid.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Division (Kitab al-Qismah) addresses the ruling of muhayaat (time-sharing of usufruct) in two co-owned houses. The author presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), as well as other transmitted opinions. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) is that muhayaat in two houses is permissible with mutual consent, and the qadi can compel it upon the request of a co-owner. This is because the parties are simply dividing the usufruct, which involves minimal disparity, so it is treated as an ifraz (separation) rather than a mubadala (barter). The Sahibayn analogize two houses to a single house, where muhayaat is clearly allowed. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, is reported to have said that muhayaat in two houses is absolutely impermissible, neither by consent nor compulsion, because it is akin to exchanging one dwelling for another (sukna bi-sukna) which is a form of ribawi exchange or invalid sale. The text then poses a question: how can there be agreement among the three imams on the permissibility of muhayaat with compulsion if Abu Hanifa differs? The answer is that the agreed-upon case (possibly in a single house) is based on the concept of ifraz, where the disparity is small. In two houses, the disparity in physical assets is large, making it mubadala, and compulsion is not allowed. The passage also mentions other views from nawadir: one by al-Karkhi that only mutual consent suffices, and another that muhayaat is entirely invalid. The student should note the distinction between muhayaat (time-sharing of usage) and qismah al-a'yan (physical division of property).

Key Terms
مہایات (muhāyāh): A form of partition where co-owners agree to use the co-owned property in turns, dividing the usufruct by time.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion by a qadi to enforce a partition or muhayaat against a reluctant co-owner.
صاحبین (Ṣāḥibān): Imam Abu Hanifa's two main disciples: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known and authoritative narrations from Imam Muhammad's six core books (al-Usul al-Sittah).
افراز (ifrāz): Separation or partition of shares, especially of usufruct, where the property remains jointly owned but usage is divided.
مبادلہ (mubādalah): Exchange or barter, where each party gives something in return for another. In property division, it implies a transfer of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) in this passage, what is the ruling of muhayaat in two houses?
A) It is invalid under all circumstances.
B) It is permissible with mutual consent, and the qadi can compel it.
C) It is permissible only with mutual consent, not by compulsion.
D) It is permissible if the houses are considered as one unit.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi for muhayaat in two houses is permissibility with compulsion, based on treating it as ifraz of usufruct with minimal disparity, not mubadala of assets.

Muhayaat for Riding Two Animals: Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling and disagreement on time-sharing two animals for riding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of muhayaat for riding two animals according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn and explain the reasoning based on variability of usufruct.

Core Idea
Muhayaat for riding animals is permitted by the Sahibayn but not by Abu Hanifa because riders' skill disparity creates inequality.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the permissibility of muhayaat (time-sharing) for riding two jointly owned animals. The passage contrasts the Sahibayn's analogy to physical division of property with Imam Abu Hanifa's argument based on the variability of riders' skills. A key distinction is made with muhayaat of a slave's services, which is allowed by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa says muhayaat for riding two animals is not permissible; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is permissible.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's analogy
They analogize to qismat al-a'yan (physical division of assets): just as physical division is allowed, division of usufruct by time should also be allowed.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's objection
He argues that usage varies greatly between a skilled rider (ḥādhiq) and a clumsy rider (akhraq), leading to inequality. This makes muhayaat akin to an unequal exchange, which is not permissible.
The same reasoning applies to muhayaat on a single animal.
4
Compare to the slave exception
Muhayaat for a slave's services is permissible even for Abu Hanifa because a slave serves by choice and will not exceed his capacity, ensuring equality. An animal can be coerced, so the inequality remains.
Shows the principle: self-control (ikhtiyar) ensures equitable use.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to the Sahibayn, the agreement is valid and enforceable; according to Abu Hanifa, it is invalid and cannot be enforced.
The text does not specify which view is mufta bihi.

ترجمہ اور دو چوپاؤں پریوار ہونے پر مہایات ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک قسمت اعیان پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے جائز ہے اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ استعمال متفاوت ہوتا ہے سواروں کے تفاوت سے اس لئے کہ سوار ماہر اور اناڑی کے درمیان ہے اور ایک چوپایہ میں سورای پر مہایات اسی اختلاف پر ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں بخلاف غلام کے اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے اختیار سے خدمت کرتا ہے تو وہ اپنی طاقت سے زیادہ کام نہیں کرے گا اور چو پا یہ زیادہ کام کر لیتا ہے۔ تشریح زید اور عمر کے درمیان دو گھوڑے مشترک ہیں انہوں نے اس طرح مہایا کی ایک پر زید سوار ہوا کرے اور دوسرے پر عمر یا ایک گھوڑا، دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے اور انہوں نے یہ طے کیا کہ اس پر آٹھ دن زید سوار ہوا کرے اور آٹھ دن عمر تو صاحبین کے نزدیک تو یہ صورت جائز ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔
صاحبین نے قسمت کے نزدیک تو یہ صورت جائز ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک جائز نہیں۔ صاحبین نے قسمت اعیان پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اس کو جائز کہا۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک قسمت اعیان کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ (کما مر )
نیز امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سوار سوار میں فرق ہے ایک سوار تو شہسواری میں ماہر ہے جس سے گھوڑے کو کوئی نقصان نہیں پہنچے گا اور دوسرا بالکل اناڑی اور ڈیوٹ ہے جس سے گھوڑے کو نقصان پہنچ سکتا ہے۔
ہاں اگر یہی صورت ایک غلام اور دو غلاموں کو اندر ہو تو وہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ غلام تو صاحب اختیار ہے اپنی قدرت سے زیادہ بوجھ اٹھائے گا ہی نہیں اور چوپایہ مار پیٹ کی صورت میں اپنی طاقت سے زیادہ کام کر لیتا ہے اس وجہ سے دونوں کے درمیان فرق ہو گیا۔
And in the case of two animals, muhayaat for riding is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but according to them (Sahibayn) it is permissible, analogizing to the division of physical assets (qismat al-a'yan). For him (Abu Hanifa), the usage differs with the difference of the riders, for they are between skilled and clumsy. And muhayaat for riding on one animal is subject to the same difference of opinion for the reason we mentioned, unlike the slave because he serves by his own choice and does not bear more than his capacity, while the animal bears it. Translation: And about muhayaat on two animals for riding, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two companions, analogizing to the division of physical assets, it is permissible. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that usage varies with the difference of the riders because riders are between skilled and clumsy. And muhayaat for riding on one animal is subject to the same difference for the reason we mentioned, unlike the slave because he serves by his own choice, so he will not perform more than his capacity, while the animal performs more. Clarification: Zaid and 'Amr jointly own two horses. They make a muhayaat that Zaid rides one and 'Amr the other, or one horse jointly owned between them, and they agree that Zaid rides it for eight days and 'Amr for eight days. According to the two companions, this is permissible; according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), it is not permissible. The two companions, analogizing to the division of physical assets, said it is permissible. And according to Imam, the ruling on division of physical assets is the same (as mentioned). Also, Imam's proof is that there is a difference between riders: one rider is an expert horseman who will cause no harm to the horse, and the other is completely clumsy and unskilled who may harm the horse. Yes, if this same situation occurs with one slave or two slaves, then it is permissible even according to Imam, because a slave has choice and will not bear more than his ability, while an animal, under threat of beating, performs more than its capacity; due to this, a distinction is made between the two.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of muhayaat (time-sharing) for riding two jointly owned animals, according to the Hanafi school. The text presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa does not permit muhayaat for riding two animals, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it by analogizing to the physical division of property (qismat al-a'yan). The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's position is that the use of the animals varies significantly depending on the skill of the riders—an expert rider will treat the animal well, while a clumsy rider may cause harm, leading to inequality in the division of usufruct. This inequality makes muhayaat akin to an exchange (mubadala), not a separation (ifraz), and hence it is not permissible. The same disagreement applies to muhayaat for riding a single animal. The text then distinguishes this case from a slave: muhayaat in the services of a slave is permissible even according to Abu Hanifa because a slave serves by choice and will not exceed his capacity, whereas an animal can be forced to bear more. The student should note that the distinction rests on the nature of the subject: animate beings with self-control (slaves) vs. animals that can be coerced. The Sahibayn's analogy to physical division is based on the idea that the animals themselves are similar, but Abu Hanifa focuses on the variability of use.

Key Terms
تهايؤ (tahāyu’): Another term for muhayaat, meaning time-sharing arrangement for usufruct.
قسمت اعیان (qismat al-a‘yān): Physical division of co-owned property where each party gets a specific portion of the asset itself.
حاذق (ḥādhiq): Skilled, expert (rider).
اخرق (akhraq): Clumsy, unskilled (rider).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa not permit muhayaat for riding two jointly owned animals?
A) Because animals cannot be divided physically.
B) Because riders differ in skill, causing unequal usage and potential harm.
C) Because it involves a slave, which is not allowed.
D) Because the Sahibayn disagree with him.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of muhayaat for riding animals hinges on whether the usufruct is considered divisible equally; the different views reflect different assessments of the nature of use.

Muhayaat in Renting a Single House vs. Slave/Animal
Ruling on muhayaat in renting a single house vs. slave/animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muhayaat in renting a single house vs. a single slave/animal and explain the rational distinction based on asset stability.

Core Idea
Muhayaat for renting is permissible only for stable assets like houses, not for slaves or animals.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Book of Division (Kitab al-Muhayaat) regarding the permissibility of time-sharing (muhayaat) in the exploitation of a single co-owned asset through renting. The Hanafi school distinguishes between immovable property (real estate) and movable living beings based on the stability of equity over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for each asset type
State the permissibility for a house (jā'iz) and for a slave/animal (not jā'iz) according to zahir al-riwaya.
The ruling is clear-cut based on the nature of the asset.
2
Understand the concept of equity (i‘tidāl)
Equity means that each co-owner should receive equal benefit over time. The arrangement must guarantee this equality.
Equity is the core criterion.
3
Analyze the rational distinction (ta‘līl)
The text explains that in real estate, the asset's condition remains stable, so equity at the start is likely to continue. In slaves and animals, constant changes (illness, injury, death) make it impossible to ensure continued equity.
The ta‘līl is based on the presence or absence of stability.
4
Apply the distinction to other cases
Consider other movable vs. immovable assets (e.g., a car vs. a plot of land) and reason whether muhayaat in renting would be permissible.
This tests your understanding of the underlying principle.
5
Note the authority of the ruling
The ruling is from zahir al-riwaya, the relied-upon narrations in the Hanafi school.
Zahir al-riwaya carries the highest authority for fatwa.

Source Text

واما التهايؤ فى الاستغلال يجوز فى الدار الواحدة فى ظاهر الرواية وفى العبد الواحد والدابة الواحدة لا يجوز ووجه الفرق ان النصيبين يتعاقبان فى الاستيفاء والاعتدال ثابت فى الحال والظاهر بقاؤه في العقار غييره فى الحيوانات لتوالى اسباب التغير عليها فتفوت المعادلة
