ترجمہ اور بہر حال کرایہ پر دینے سے مہایات دار واحد میں جائز ہے ظاہر الروایہ میں اور عہد واحد اور دا بہ واحدہ میں جائز نہیں ہے اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ دونوں حصے وصولیابی کے اعتبار سے یکے بعد دیگرے آتے ہیں اور اعتدال فی الحال ثابت ہے اور ظاہر زمین میں اس اعتدال کا بقاء ہے اور حیوانات میں اس کا تغیر ہے حیوانات کے اوپر اسباب تغیر لگا تار آنے کی وجہ سے تو برابری فوت ہو جائے گی۔ تشریح ایک گھر زید و عمر کے درمیان مشترک ہے انہوں نے یہ طے کیا کہ اس کو ایک مہینہ کرایہ پر زید چلائے اور ایک مہینہ عمر و چلائے اور اس کا کرایہ وصول کرے تو ظاہر الروایہ میں یہ صورت جائز ہے۔ اور ایک غلام اور ایک گھوڑے میں یہی صورت ہو تو بالاتفاق جائز نہیں کیونکہ شریکین جب دونوں برابر کے شریک ہیں تو بہر صورت ان کی برابری کا خیال ہونا چاہیے اور یہ خیال اول صورت میں باقی ہے اور آخری صورتوں میں باقی نہیں رہتا۔ کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ گھر کی جو پوزیشن اب ہے اگلے مہینے میں بھی وہی برقرار رہے گی تو برابری ثابت ہے۔ اور غلام اور گھوڑے کی صورت میں اس کی کوئی گارنٹی نہیں ہے ہو سکتا ہے کہ غلام اور گھوڑا بیا ہو جائے یا کچھ اور بات پیدا ہو جائے کیونکہ حیوانات اسباب تغیر کے درمیان گھرے ہوئے ہیں تو
And as for muhayaat in exploitation (renting), it is permissible in a single house according to zahir al-riwaya, but in a single slave and a single animal it is not permissible. The face of the distinction is that the two shares alternate in the receipt (of rent), and equity (i'tidal) is established at the present moment, and its continuance is apparent in real estate (al-'iqar), but not in animals because the causes of change follow upon them, so equality is lost. And [word cut off]. Translation: And regarding muhayaat in renting out, it is permissible in a single house in zahir al-riwaya, but in a single slave and a single animal it is not permissible. The reason for the distinction is that the two shares come one after the other in terms of receipt, and equity is established at the present moment, and in land this equity apparently remains, but in animals it changes because causes of change continuously affect animals, so equality is lost. Clarification: A house is jointly owned between Zaid and 'Amr. They agree that Zaid will rent it out for one month and 'Amr for the next month, and each will collect the rent. In zahir al-riwaya, this is permissible. If the same is done with a single slave or a single horse, then by consensus it is not permissible, because when co-owners are equal, their equality must be considered in all circumstances. This consideration remains in the first case (house) but not in the latter cases (slave/animal). For it is apparent that the condition of the house that exists now will remain the same next month, so equality is established. In the case of a slave or horse, there is no guarantee; the slave or horse may become ill or something else may happen, because animals are surrounded by causes of change.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Division discusses the ruling of muhayaat (time-sharing) in the exploitation (istighlal) of a single co-owned asset through renting. According to the relied-upon narrations (zahir al-riwaya), muhayaat is permissible for a single house: the co-owners can take turns renting it out and receiving the income. However, for a single slave or a single animal, such an arrangement is not permissible. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that in a house, the asset is stable; its condition remains essentially unchanged over time, so the co-owners can be assured that each period will yield equal benefits. In contrast, slaves and animals are subject to constant changes—they may become ill, lose value, or change in capacity—so equality between the periods cannot be guaranteed. The text emphasizes that equity ('i'tidal) must be preserved between co-owners. In real estate, equity at the start is likely to persist, but in living beings, it is not. Therefore, muhayaat in renting a house is acceptable, but not in renting a slave or animal. The student should note that this ruling applies to a single unit; for multiple units (e.g., two houses or two animals), the ruling may differ as seen in previous sections.

Key Terms
مہایات (muhāyāt): Time-sharing arrangement between co-owners, where each takes turns using or benefiting from the jointly owned asset.
استغلال (istighlāl): Exploitation of property by renting it out to generate income.
اعتدال (i‘tidāl): Equity, balance, equality of shares between co-owners.
عقار (‘iqār): Real estate, immovable property like land and buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is muhayaat for renting a single house permissible in zahir al-riwaya but not for a single slave or animal?
A) Because slaves and animals cannot be rented.
B) Because there is no agreement among the imams on the matter.
C) Because real estate is stable and equality between time periods can be maintained, while animals are subject to change.
D) Because the rent for animals is less predictable.

Key Takeaway
Muhayaat for renting is permissible only for stable assets like real estate to preserve equity between co-owners.

Tahayu on Two Houses: Non-Sharing of Excess Rent
Expansion of tahayu ruling from a single house to two houses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahayu for two separate houses and explain why excess rent is not shared, distinguishing it from the single-house case.

Core Idea
In tahayu on two houses, each partner keeps his own income; excess is not shared because exploitation is simultaneous, not successive.

Previously, the text ruled that in tahayu on a single house, any excess income from one partner's turn must be shared with the other, treating each turn as a loan. Now the ruling is extended to two separate houses, where the outcome differs: the partner whose house yields more does not share the excess. Understanding this distinction requires analyzing the nature of the division and the time of exploitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tahayu on two houses for renting (istighlal). The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) in Zahir al-Riwaya. Also, if one house yields more rent, the partners do not share that excess.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the prior reasoning about the single house case, extended by analogy (qiyas). The key is that in two houses, the meaning of tamyiz and ifraz is dominant because the times of extracting profit are simultaneous (ittihad zaman al-istifa').
The text references a previously stated reason: 'لما بينا' (for the reason we have stated).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
In two houses, each partner has exclusive right to his own house for the entire duration; they can both rent out simultaneously. Thus, there is no loan-like relationship. Each partner's income is solely his own. In a single house, only one can rent at a time, so each turn is like an agent for the other, requiring return of excess.
The distinction hinges on ta'aqub (succession) vs. ittihad (simultaneity).
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If partners own two separate houses and agree that each rents out one, any difference in rent is not equalized. This is contrary to the single-house case where excess must be shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتهايؤ على الاستغلال في الدارين جائز ايضا فى ظاهر الرواية لما بينا ولو فضل غلة احدهما لا يشتركان فيه بخلاف الدار الواحدة والفرق ان فى الدارين معنى التمييز والافراز راجح لاتحاد زمان الاستيفاء وفي الدار الواحدة يتعاقب الوصول فاعتبر قرضا وجعل كل واحد فى نوبته كالو كيل عن صاحبه فلهذا يرد على حصته من الفضل. ترجمہ اور دوگھروں میں استغلال پر مہایات ظاہر الروایہ میں جائز ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی آمدنی زیادہ ہو جائے تو اس میں دونوں شریک نہ ہوں گے بخلاف دار واحد کے اور فرق یہ ہے کہ دارین میں تمیز اور افراز کے معنی راج ہیں زمانہ استیفاء کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور دار واحد میں وصول یکے بعد دیگرے ہے تو اس کو قرض اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور ہر ایک کو اس کی باری میں اپنے ساتھی کے وکیل کے مثل قرار دیا جائے گا پس اس وجہ سے وہ اپنے ساتھی پر اس کا زیادتی کا حصہ واپس کرے گا۔ تشریح: پہلے مسئلہ میں مہایات دار واحد میں تھی جس کا حکم بیان کر چکا ہے اور اگر مہایات دو گھروں میں ہوں اس طریقہ پر کہ ایک گھر زید کوں کیا کہ وہ اس کو کرایہ پر چلائے اور دوسرا عمر و کہ اس کو وہ کرایہ پر چلائے تو ظاہر الروایہ میں اس سابق دلیل سے یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں اور اس میں یہ فرق ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں اگر کسی کی باری میں آمدنی زیادہ ہو تو اس میں دونوں شریک ہوں گے اور دوسری صورت میں اگر ایک طرف زیادہ آمدنی ہو تو زیادتی میں شرکت نہیں ہوگی اور ان دونوں میں فرق کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ دوسری صورت میں زیادہ ہو تو میں یہ افراز اور تمیز کے معنی رائج ہے کیونکہ تحصیل منافع کا زمانہ ایک ہے اور پہلی صورت میں وصول منفعت یکے بعد دیگرے ہے تو اس کو قرض شمار کیا جائے گا کہ یہ اپنے ساتھی کا وکیل ہے اور جب وکیل پھر اتو ساتھی کا حصہ واپس کرنا ضروری ہو گیا۔
And tahayu on exploitation (renting) in two houses is also permissible in Zahir al-Riwayah, for the reason we have stated. And if the rent of one of them is surplus, they do not share in it, contrary to the single house. The difference is that in two houses, the meaning of separation and segregation is dominant due to unity of time of extraction, whereas in a single house, the receipt is successive, so it is treated as a loan, and each is considered an agent of the other in his turn, therefore he returns to his partner his share of the excess. Translation: And tahayu on renting in two houses is permissible in Zahir al-Riwaya due to the evidence we have given. If one of the houses yields more income, they do not share in that excess, unlike the single house. The difference is that in two houses, the concept of segregation and separation is strong because the time of exploitation is the same, whereas in a single house, the receipt is successive, so it is considered a loan, and each person in his turn acts as an agent for his partner, so he must return his partner's share of the excess. Explanation: The first issue dealt with tahayu in a single house. Now if tahayu is made on two houses, e.g., one house assigned to Zaid to rent out and the other to Amr, it is also permissible. The difference is that in the first case (single house), excess income is shared, but in the second case (two houses), excess is not shared. The reason is that in the second case, the meaning of separation and segregation is strong because the time of obtaining profit is simultaneous, whereas in the first case, receipt is successive, so it is treated as a loan, and each is considered an agent of the other, requiring return of excess.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling for tahayu on renting out two separate houses. According to Zahir al-Riwaya, it is permissible. However, unlike the single house case, if one house yields more rent than the other, the partner does not share in that excess. The reason is that in two houses, the division is effectively a separation (ifraz) where each has exclusive right to his house for the entire period, and the exploitation is simultaneous (both can rent out at the same time). In contrast, in a single house, the exploitation is successive (only one can rent at a time), making it akin to a loan each turn, where the tenant-partner is like an agent for the other and must return any surplus. The commentary explains that this distinction is based on the unity of time (ittihad zaman) vs. succession (ta'aqub). The ruling is based on the principle of equity and the nature of the division.

Key Terms
تمييز (tamyiz): Separation or distinction between properties, here referring to the physical and temporal separation of two houses.
افراز (ifraz): Segregation or allocation of specific shares, such as assigning particular houses to individual owners.
قرض (qard): Loan; in this context, the treatment of the turn as a loan (i.e., each turn is like a loan from the other party).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In tahayu on two separate houses, if one house yields more rent, what is the Hanafi ruling on the excess?
A) The excess must be shared equally between the partners.
B) The excess is not shared because the properties are separate and exploitation is simultaneous.
C) The excess is given to charity.
D) The arrangement is invalid because the houses are not identical.

Key Takeaway
In tahayu on two separate houses, excess rent is not shared because the properties are effectively segregated and exploitation is simultaneous, unlike a single house where turns are successive and treated as loans.
